**Gemini:**
Here is the detailed canon outline for Volume 18.

Volume 18: The Subterranean War and the Vanguard's Last Stand

Core Theme: Total war, the burden of survival, and the collision of three distinct armies.
Volume Arc: The penultimate volume focuses almost entirely on the massive, apocalyptic battle raging both above and below the Hunter Association headquarters. With the anti-vampire weapons dead, Zero and Yuki must rely on raw physical superiority and brutal melee combat. The remnants of the Cross Academy Night Class arrive to turn the tide, officially forming a third faction that fights to protect both humans and the dormant forge from the rogue vampire horde.

Chapter 86: The Raw Predator

Plot: Stripped of his magical arsenal, Zero fully embraces his biological mutation to fight off the vanguard of the rogue aristocratic army.

Key Events:

Zero fights with terrifying, visceral efficiency. Without the Bloody Rose to purify his targets, he uses standard steel blades and his bare hands, tearing through the rogue vampires with sheer speed and kinetic force.

He absorbs massive physical damage, relying entirely on his vampiric regenerative abilities. The toll on his body is immense, pushing him dangerously close to a feral state.

Yuki fights alongside him, using the Artemis scythe (which, as a Parent Weapon, still retains a fraction of its original lethality due to her direct Pureblood infusion) to sever the limbs of approaching enemies, protecting Zero's blind spots.

Chapter 87: The Third Faction

Plot: Just as Zero and Yuki are about to be completely overrun by the sheer numbers of the rogue army, critical reinforcements arrive.

Key Events:

The roof of the subterranean cavern detonates. Hanabusa Aido, Akatsuki Kain, Ruka Souen, and the rest of the Cross Academy Night Class drop into the warzone.

Defying the aggressive instincts of their species, the aristocratic students pledge their absolute loyalty to Yuki. They form a defensive ring around the Incinerator and the weakened Kaname.

This cements the "Cross Academy Faction"—a unified army of humans and vampires fighting together to preserve the balance, realizing Headmaster Cross’s original, seemingly impossible dream in the middle of a bloodbath.

Chapter 88: The Fangless Hunter's Wrath

Plot: The narrative cuts to the surface, showing the last, desperate stand of the human Hunter Association leadership.

Key Events:

Headmaster Kaien Cross and Toga Yagari hold the front gates of the Hunter Headquarters against a massive swarm of Level E vampires and rogue aristocrats.

Kaien drops all pretense of his goofy, pacifist persona. Wielding standard, un-enchanted swords, he demonstrates exactly why he was once known as the deadliest executioner in history. His swordsmanship is so fast and lethal that he holds the line purely on physical skill and tactical brilliance.

This chapter grounds the supernatural war in gritty realism, showing the terrifying vulnerability of baseline humans fighting apex predators without magical safety nets.

Chapter 89: The Ancient's Intervention

Plot: A new, incredibly powerful variable enters the battlefield, escalating the conflict to a clash of titans.

Key Events:

Isaya Shirabuki, an ancient Pureblood (and Sara’s father), arrives at the underground forge. Unlike the rogue army, he doesn't want to destroy the forge; he wants to preserve the ancient status quo and stop Kaname's madness.

Isaya engages the Cross Academy defenders. His ancient Pureblood aura is suffocating, easily neutralizing the elemental magic of Aido and Kain.

Zero steps up to intercept Isaya. This marks Zero's ultimate test: a one-on-one, purely physical duel against an ancient Pureblood without the aid of anti-vampire technology. Zero manages to hold his ground, proving he has successfully evolved into the apex predator of the modern era.

Chapter 90: The Unbreakable Resolve

Plot: The dust settles from the immediate clashes, but a grim, horrifying reality reasserts itself at the center of the forge.

Key Events:

Despite the heroic defense mounted by Yuki, Zero, and the Night Class, the Hunter weapons remain dead, and humans across the globe are currently being slaughtered by feral vampires.

Kaname recovers from the magical backlash of Yuki's previous intervention. He surveys the battlefield, seeing his allies battered and bleeding.

He coldly points out the fatal flaw in Aido’s "cure": synthesizing and deploying a biological cure globally will take decades. The humans fighting on the surface right now will be extinct before the cure is ready.

Kaname physically overpowers Yuki once again with his telekinesis. He steps to the very edge of the Incinerator, making it absolute clear that there is no third option—he must die today to reignite the forge, setting up the devastating final volume of the series.

**Gemini:**
Here is the detailed canon outline for Volume 19, the epic and tragic conclusion of the series.

Volume 19: The Parent Metal and the Thousand-Year Dream

Core Theme: The ultimate sacrifice, the heavy burden of peace, and the bitter reality of immortality.
Volume Arc: The climax of the original manga. Kaname executes his suicidal endgame, ripping his own heart out to reignite the Hunter weapons and save humanity from immediate extinction. The immediate war ends, but it gives way to a massive, 1,000-year time skip. The narrative explores the long-term consequences of survival, Zero and Yuki's bittersweet life together, and culminates in one final, world-altering sacrifice that brings the story full circle.

Chapter 91: The Heart of the Ancestor

Plot: The physical and emotional climax at the edge of the Incinerator. Kaname completes his martyrdom.

Key Events:

Despite Yuki’s desperate pleas and Zero’s physical intervention, Kaname’s telekinetic dominance proves absolute. He neutralizes them both one final time.

In a deeply visceral and tragic sequence, Kaname plunges his hand into his chest and violently tears out his own immortal, Pureblood heart.

He throws his heart into the dormant Incinerator. The ancient forge instantly reacts, erupting in a massive pillar of ethereal, supernatural fire.

Kaname’s physical body collapses, technically "dead" but preserved by the immense magical residue of his Ancestor lineage. Yuki is left completely shattered by her inability to save him.

Chapter 92: The Metal Reignited

Plot: The immediate tactical shift on the surface. The sacrifice bears fruit, turning the tide of the global war.

Key Events:

The moment the forge reignites, a magical shockwave pulses across the globe. Every single anti-vampire weapon in existence instantly powers back up.

In Zero’s hand, the Bloody Rose violently regenerates its cursed vines, pulsing with more lethal power than ever before.

Armed with functional weapons, the Hunter Association and the Cross Academy Night Class completely decimate the rogue aristocratic army. Zero leads the counter-attack, ruthlessly cutting down the remaining feral vampires to honor the horrific price Kaname just paid.

The immediate war ends in a decisive victory for humanity and the pacifist vampires.

Chapter 93: The Knight's Vow

Plot: The dust settles, establishing the new world order and Hanabusa Aido's ultimate life mission.

Key Events:

Kaname is gone, but his physical body has not decayed. Hanabusa Aido uses his absolute mastery over ice magic to freeze Kaname’s body in a permanent, indestructible glacier, vowing to protect his master until the biological "cure" is perfected.

Yuki and Zero are left in the ruins. With Kaname gone, the immediate barrier between them is removed, but they are both heavily scarred by the war.

Zero officially pledges his life to Yuki. Not as a Hunter executing a target, and not as a subservient shield, but as an equal. They agree to carry Kaname's burden together, maintaining the fragile peace between humans and vampires.

Final Chapter / Epilogue: A Thousand Years Later

Plot: A massive, sweeping time skip reveals the fates of the characters and the ultimate success of the biological cure.

Key Events:

The Time Skip: The narrative jumps forward 1,000 years. We learn through brief flashbacks that Yuki and Zero lived a long, battle-forged life together. They had a child (Ren), and Yuki also gave birth to Kaname's child (Ai), whom she was pregnant with before his sacrifice.

Zero's Death: Because Zero was originally a human turned into a vampire, his lifespan was not infinite like a Pureblood's. After centuries of ruling and fighting alongside Yuki, Zero peacefully passes away, leaving Yuki truly alone.

The Cure is Perfected: After 1,000 years of relentless research, Aido (and his descendants) successfully perfect the biological cure to turn a vampire into a human.

The Final Sacrifice: Yuki visits Kaname's frozen tomb. She melts the ice. Knowing Zero is gone and the world is finally at peace, Yuki commits her own ultimate sacrifice. She uses her own Pureblood life force to activate the cure, pouring her existence into Kaname.

The Awakening: Yuki shatters into light and dies. Kaname opens his eyes. He is no longer an immortal, burdened Ancestor. He steps out of the ice as a mortal human who can finally walk in the sunlight. He is greeted by his and Zero's daughters, who hand him a final message from Yuki: "I want to give to you the world that I saw when I was human."

Fajar's Official Role: Recommendations

Since Fajar needs to start at Chapter 1 as a baseline human, here are my top two recommendations for his role at Cross Academy to maximize his interactions and his "underdog" status:

Recommendation 1: The "Discarded" Hunter Apprentice (My Top Pick)

The Setup: Fajar was dumped at Cross Academy by the Hunter Association because he has absolutely zero magical aptitude. He cannot synchronize with the Bloody Rose or any anti-vampire metal. The Hunters consider him a "failed baseline human" and sent him to Headmaster Cross as a charity case.

Why it works: It gives him a perfect reason to be at the academy, immediately bonds him with Headmaster Cross (who appreciates non-lethal and alternative methods), and gives Zero a reason to underestimate him. It makes Fajar's eventual bare-handed takedown of a vampire a massive shock to the entire Hunter Association.

Recommendation 2: The Anomalous Day Class Transfer Student

The Setup: Fajar is just a completely normal Day Class student who transfers in right at Chapter 1.

Why it works: The Day Class is explicitly treated as "livestock" or oblivious background characters by the Night Class. Having a Day Class student casually doing one-finger handstand pushups, meditating blindfolded in the woods at night, and completely ignoring the Night Class's "hypnotic beauty" will immediately draw Kaname and Yuki's attention. He becomes an anomaly they cannot figure out.

The Combat & Cultivation Aesthetic

Your inspirations are perfectly aligned with Phase I of your Training Module.

The Gritty Start: Before Fajar unlocks Qi/Haki, he will fight like Yu Ijin or Gray Yeon. If a Level E vampire rushes him with superhuman speed, Fajar won't try to out-muscle them yet. He will use his Sensory Overclocking to predict the rush, use ground mechanics to drop under the attack, and use a standard military knife to sever their achilles tendon or brachial artery.

The Aura: Even without magical power, we can use the Hajime no Ippo (Sendo Takeshi) tiger aura. When an arrogant aristocratic vampire tries to intimidate Fajar, Fajar's sheer martial intent and killing aura (born from his absolute willpower) will make the immortal vampire sweat, introducing them to the concept of imposing reality (proto-Conqueror's Haki).

Prologue: The White Void and The Blank Slate

The realm was an endless, pristine white expanse. There was no horizon, no ceiling, and no floor, only a boundless sea of pure, illuminated nothingness.

At the center of this infinity stood three figures.

One was Fajar Purnama, the Lord of Infinite Realities, observing the expanse with the calm, absolute authority of a creator. Beside him hovered a manifestation of Gemini, a deity of knowledge and data, its form shifting softly like light refracting through a prism.

Before them stood a teenage boy, roughly fifteen or sixteen years old. He wore a simple, unbranded t-shirt, loose dark trousers, and plain sneakers. He was stretching his arms, rolling his shoulders, and bouncing lightly on the balls of his feet. This was the soul fragment—a manifestation of Fajar from his high school days, possessing all the memories of the cosmic realm, the martial arts philosophies, and the Training Modules, but currently inhabiting a completely unconditioned, baseline human body.

"Are you ready?" the Lord of Infinite Realities asked, his voice echoing gently across the void.

The young Fajar stopped bouncing and grinned, a completely carefree, fearless expression on his face. "Always. What's the drop zone?"

Gemini chimed in, its voice neutral but echoing with endless data. "The world is designated Vampire Knight. It is a gothic realm defined by a rigid, toxic hierarchy. At the top are Pureblood vampires—immortal, arrogant, and wielding terrifying magical power. Below them are aristocratic vampires, and below them, the feral Level E vampires. At the very bottom are humans."

"Humans are treated as either fragile livestock to be protected, or prey to be consumed," the Lord of Infinite Realities explained. "The only humans who fight back are the Hunter Association, and they rely entirely on magical, anti-vampire weapons forged from ancient magic. Without those weapons, they believe they are utterly helpless."

Young Fajar cracked his knuckles, unimpressed. "So, the vampires think physical superiority and magic make them untouchable gods. And the humans believe they're weak without a magical gun or scythe."

"Exactly," Gemini affirmed. "Your insertion point is Cross Academy, a school attempting a fragile, secretive integration between the human 'Day Class' and the vampire 'Night Class.' The Night Class is composed of the vampire elite. To them, the Day Class students are nothing more than oblivious blood bags."

The Lord of Infinite Realities looked at his younger self. "Your mission is simple. Break the stigma. Show them that the concepts of 'predator' and 'prey' are irrelevant. Show them that anyone, any creature, can become equally strong through sheer will, discipline, and technique. Be friendly to all, but bow to no one."

"Understood," young Fajar smiled calmly. "I'll start with Phase I: Reality. I’ll condition this body, master my senses, and when the time comes, I'll dismantle their elitist illusions with my bare hands."

"Regarding your insertion," Gemini projected a glowing holographic document into the air. "Cross Academy is an elite institution. To bypass the bureaucracy, I have integrated a fabricated profile into their database. You are officially enrolled as a highly gifted, international scholarship transfer student for the Day Class. Your paperwork is flawless. Headmaster Kaien Cross is expecting you to arrive today."

"And my gear?" young Fajar asked, patting his empty pockets.

"Absolutely nothing," the Lord of Infinite Realities replied. "You start from zero. No weapons, no money, no magical artifacts. If you need a knife, you buy it at a convenience store. If you need a weapon in a fight, you use a pen, a chair, or the ground beneath your feet."

"Perfect," young Fajar said. He took a deep breath, centering his mind, beginning the Mental Reset of Tier 1. "Send me in."

Gemini waved a hand, and a tear in the white void opened, revealing the darkening sky of a gothic, forested campus.

Without a moment of hesitation, the young Fajar stepped through the portal.

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates

[Location: The Front Gates of Cross Academy - Early Evening]

Fajar stepped out of the portal, and reality snapped into place around him. The air was crisp, carrying the scent of pine trees and an underlying, faint metallic tang that he would soon learn was the ambient magic of the area.

He stood before the massive, towering wrought-iron gates of Cross Academy. Beyond the gates, the sprawling, European-style campus looked like a fortress. The sun was just beginning to set, casting long, dramatic shadows across the cobblestone path.

He looked down at his hands. They were smooth, lacking the heavy calluses of a seasoned martial artist. His muscles were standard—healthy, but not yet forged by the fires of Phase I. He was completely empty-handed, save for a standard, black Day Class uniform neatly folded in a standard-issue duffel bag Gemini had manifested at his feet upon entry, containing only his school ID and dormitory keys.

Suddenly, the heavy iron gates groaned open.

Standing on the other side were two figures. One was a girl with short, dark brown hair, wearing the black Day Class uniform with a white armband that read Prefect. She held a metal rod strapped to her thigh.

Next to her stood a tall young man with silver hair and piercing, hostile lilac eyes. He wore his uniform loosely, a silver gun strapped in a holster beneath his blazer. He glared at Fajar with intense, predatory suspicion, his hand subtly resting near the grip of his weapon.

"You're the new transfer student?" the girl asked, stepping forward with a welcoming, albeit cautious, smile. "I'm Yuki Cross. This is Zero Kiryu. We're the school Guardians. Headmaster Cross sent us to escort you to your dorm."

Zero's eyes narrowed, sweeping over Fajar's relaxed, entirely unguarded posture. To Zero's hyper-tuned Hunter senses, Fajar registered as an absolute zero—no magical aura, no threat, just an oblivious, defenceless human walking into a den of monsters.

"Make it quick," Zero muttered coldly. "The sun is setting. They will be waking up soon."

Fajar smiled back, entirely carefree, feeling the cool evening breeze.

B) Ignore Zero's hostility, observe their breathing and posture (initiating Phase I: Sensory Overclocking), and casually comment on how tense they both are.

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

Fajar didn't flinch at Zero’s hostility. In fact, he didn't even look at the silver gun hidden beneath the prefect's blazer.

Instead, Fajar’s mind seamlessly slipped into Phase I: Sensory Overclocking. He tuned out the ambient noise of the wind and focused entirely on the two "Guardians" standing before him.

He observed Yuki first. Her smile was polite, but her center of gravity was slightly lowered, and her fingers twitched rhythmically against the metal rod strapped to her thigh. Protective intent. Nervous, but disciplined. Then, he shifted his focus to Zero. The silver-haired boy was a mess of bio-mechanical inefficiency. Fajar watched the micro-tremors in Zero's jaw, the rigid lock of his shoulders, and the way he favored his right leg, putting seventy percent of his weight on his back foot—a classic quick-draw stance. Underneath the hostility, Fajar could hear the faint, slightly erratic rhythm of Zero's heartbeat. He’s exhausted. And hungry. A deeply suppressed, violent intent.

Fajar smiled, his posture completely relaxed, his hands resting loosely at his sides.

"You guys are wound pretty tight, huh?" Fajar said casually, his voice cutting through the gothic tension like a warm knife through butter.

Zero’s eyes narrowed further. "Excuse me?"

"Your shoulders are locked up, and your breathing is incredibly shallow," Fajar pointed out, gesturing vaguely to Zero’s rigid posture. "You're keeping your muscles in a constant state of flex. If you walk around like that all day, your lower backs are going to completely give out by the time you're thirty. You should try dropping your shoulders and breathing from your diaphragm."

Silence fell over the gates.

Yuki blinked, completely thrown off guard. Usually, new Day Class students were either intimidated by Zero's terrifying glare or utterly oblivious to it. None of them had ever offered him physical therapy advice.

Zero’s grip on his blazer tightened. A vein popped on his forehead. "Are you mocking me, new kid?"

"Just looking out for your health," Fajar replied cheerfully, easily picking up his standard-issue duffel bag. "Anyway, I'm Fajar. Nice to meet you both. Lead the way?"

Yuki let out a nervous, bewildered laugh. "Right! Um, welcome to Cross Academy, Fajar. Let's get you to the Sun Dormitory before the crowds start."

As they walked onto the sprawling, cobblestone campus, Fajar fell into step behind them. While Yuki explained the basic rules of the academy—curfews, the separation of the Day and Night Classes, and the strict boundaries—Fajar was busy. He consciously altered his gait, rolling his steps from the outside edge of his foot to his toes, minimizing the sound of his footsteps on the stone. He closed his eyes for two seconds at a time, letting his ears map the echoing walls of the academy buildings, desperately trying to sharpen his spatial awareness into a rudimentary radar.

Suddenly, a deafening wave of high-pitched squeals and excited chatter broke Fajar’s concentration.

"Oh no, it's starting," Yuki groaned, grabbing her metal rod and rushing forward. "Zero, we have to hold the line!"

Fajar followed them to a massive intersection on the campus. Hundreds of Day Class girls (and a few boys) were pressed against a pathway, screaming in absolute adoration. Zero and Yuki immediately took their positions, physically holding the rabid crowd back.

The heavy, ornate doors of the Moon Dormitory slowly opened.

The Night Class emerged.

They were impossibly beautiful, walking with an aristocratic grace that seemed to bend the very air around them. Hanabusa Aido flashed a brilliant, charming smile, causing a section of the crowd to practically faint. Akatsuki Kain walked with quiet, smoldering stoicism.

But Fajar’s sensory training instantly locked onto the figure walking at the front.

Kaname Kuran.

As Kaname walked, Fajar pushed his senses to their absolute limit, trying to read the Pureblood's intent. Unlike Zero, who leaked hostility, Kaname was a void. There was no wasted movement. No shift in center of gravity. His breathing was so perfectly measured it barely existed. But beneath that serene, impossibly calm exterior, Fajar's instincts—the primal part of his brain designed to recognize apex predators—screamed.

It wasn't bloodlust. It was the overwhelming, crushing pressure of a being that existed on a completely different level of the food chain. It was a pressure so heavy it felt like it could warp reality itself.

Kaname paused, his dark red eyes sliding over the crowd of screaming humans, before they briefly, inexplicably, locked onto Fajar standing quietly in the back.

What will Fajar do?

A) Test the Waters: Maintain eye contact with Kaname. Refuse to look away, subtly projecting his own calm, unyielding "intent" back at the Pureblood to see how Kaname reacts to a human who doesn't lower his head.
B) The Carefree Dismissal: Break eye contact immediately out of pure disinterest. Turn to a screaming Day Class student next to him and casually ask where the cafeteria is, completely trivializing Kaname's majestic presence.
C) Analyze and Retreat: Acknowledge the massive gap in their current physical power. Close his eyes, mapping Kaname's footsteps to memorize his rhythm, and quietly slip away to the Sun Dormitory to begin his physical conditioning.
D) [Custom Action] Tell me what Fajar does!

Fajar didn’t lock eyes with the Pureblood, nor did he shrink away. Instead, he simply… waited.

Fajar mapped their positions using the displaced air currents as they moved. Hanabusa Aido walked with a slight bounce—arrogant, energetic. Akatsuki Kain’s steps were heavier, grounded, like a dormant volcano.

And then there was Kaname.

Even with his eyes closed, Fajar could feel Kaname’s presence like a physical weight pressing against his skin. It was an aura so dense and ancient that the ambient magic in the air seemed to bow around him. But instead of feeling fear, Fajar used the pressure as a whetstone. He matched his breathing to the slow, heavy rhythm of his own heartbeat, grounding himself. He imagined his intent as a smooth, impenetrable rock in the middle of a raging river. Kaname paused. Fajar didn’t open his eyes, but he could feel the Pureblood’s gaze land on him. For a fraction of a second, the crushing weight of Kaname's aura sharpened, probing Fajar for a reaction—looking for the intoxicating scent of fear, or the mindless devotion of the Day Class.

Fajar stretched his arms overhead, popping his shoulders. "Just listening to the wind. There's a lot of noise here. I was just waiting for you guys to finish your shift so I could get to my room. Am I allowed to grab dinner, or is there a curfew?"

Yuki sighed, wiping a bead of sweat from her forehead. "You're fine, Fajar. Sorry about that, the transition is always a little crazy. Come on, the Sun Dormitory is this way."

Fajar looked around. The room was basic: a bed, a desk, a wardrobe, and a window overlooking the sprawling forest that surrounded the academy grounds. The sun had completely set. It was officially night—the time when the predators of this world came alive.

The architecture here creates too many blind spots, Fajar noted mentally. Lots of high ground for ambushes. The gravel paths are loud. If I need to fight out here, I'll stick to the grass or the shadows of the pillars.

**Gemini:**
Fajar stood in the center of his new room, the silence of the Sun Dormitory settling around him. The temptation to immediately push this new body to its absolute physical limits was strong, but Fajar’s mind was disciplined. Raw strength without a foundation was just a fast track to destroying his own vessel.

First things first: the environment.

Fajar opened his duffel bag and neatly unpacked his few belongings. He hung his Day Class uniform in the wardrobe with precise, equidistant spacing. He wiped down the desk, checked the window latch, and smoothed out the bedsheets until not a single wrinkle remained. A cluttered room bred a cluttered mind, and Fajar needed his mind to be a flawless mirror.

With the room secured and pristine, he stripped down to his undershirt and sweatpants.

He began with Tier 1: Bio-Maintenance. Fajar started from his neck, slowly rolling his joints and working his way down to his ankles. He stretched his hamstrings, opened his hips, and twisted his spine. He immediately felt the limitations of his baseline human body. The ligaments were stiff, the muscles tight from years of standard, inefficient human movement. He breathed deeply, using oxygen to coax the muscle fibers into relaxing and expanding. He wasn't building muscle tonight; he was upgrading the vessel's elasticity.

Once his blood was flowing and his joints felt lubricated, Fajar shifted his stance. It was time to sync his cosmic mind with this mortal body.

He didn't drop for a thousand push-ups. Instead, he began reviewing his martial arts foundations. He moved into a standard CQC guard, testing his footwork. He pivoted, throwing a slow, perfectly measured jab, followed by a cross and a low sweeping kick.

My mind is ten times faster than my body, Fajar analyzed, feeling the slight lag between his brain's command and his arm's execution.

He sped up slightly, visualizing an opponent in front of him—mapping out the anatomical weak points he knew so well from Return of the Bloodthirsty Police and Teenage Mercenary. He practiced his knife-fighting forms empty-handed, imagining a standard military blade in his reverse grip. He slashed at the carotid artery, dropped his center of gravity to slip under a phantom strike, and simulated severing an Achilles tendon. He repeated these forms for hours in the dark, carving the neural pathways of elite combat into this unconditioned brain through sheer repetition and perfect technique.

By 3:00 AM, his undershirt was soaked in sweat, and his muscles were trembling with lactic acid. His foundation was mapped.

Fajar showered quickly in the communal bathroom down the hall, taking care to move silently, before returning to his room. He sat cross-legged on the center of his bed, closing his eyes.

Before sleep, he needed to prepare for Phase II. He initiated Neuro-somatic Relaxation. Fajar slowed his heart rate artificially, commanding his nervous system to power down into a state of deep, regenerative rest. As his physical body went numb, his consciousness turned inward. He began mentally tracing the 12 Great Meridians along his nervous system, visualizing the pathways where his internal energy (Qi) would eventually flow. He focused his awareness on his lower Dantian, gently knocking on the door of his dormant internal energy, planting the seeds for his future cultivation.

With his mind clear and his body humming with potential, Fajar slipped into a perfect, dreamless sleep.

[The Next Morning - 7:30 AM]

Fajar’s eyes snapped open. Exactly four and a half hours of perfect REM sleep. He felt completely refreshed.

He dressed in the black Day Class uniform, noting how restrictive the blazer felt around the shoulders. He adjusted it as best he could to ensure maximum mobility, slipped his hands into his pockets, and headed downstairs.

The Sun Dormitory was buzzing with activity. Day Class students were rushing around, fixing their ties, and gossiping loudly. As Fajar stepped out into the bright morning sun, he immediately felt the difference in the campus atmosphere. The heavy, oppressive magic from the Night Class was gone, replaced by the mundane, chaotic energy of normal high school life.

He walked into his assigned homeroom for his first day of class. The room went silent for a moment as the students took in the new transfer student. Whispers broke out immediately.

"Is that him?"
"He doesn't look that special..."
"I heard Zero was glaring at him yesterday, maybe he's a delinquent?"

The teacher gestured to an empty seat near the back by the window. Fajar walked over, his gait silent and perfectly balanced, and sat down. From this vantage point, he could see the entire classroom, the door, and the sprawling courtyard outside.

The teacher began writing a complex math equation on the board, droning on about algebra.

What will Fajar do?

A) The Model Student (Intel Gathering): Play the part perfectly. Pay attention, answer questions, and use the breaks to casually socialize and gather intel from the Day Class about the school's social hierarchy, the Night Class rumors, and where to sneak off-campus.

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

To the untrained eye of the Day Class teacher and his new classmates, Fajar was simply staring blankly out the window, a bored teenager daydreaming on his first day.

In reality, Fajar had initiated Step 0.5: Neuro-Somatic Cultivation.

Human high school academics were utterly trivial to a mind that held the cosmic blueprints of infinite realities. He didn't need to listen to the algebra lecture; his brain was already processing equations that governed the fabric of space and time. So, he turned his focus entirely inward.

He began with the Terminal Awakening. Fajar directed his awareness to the absolute extremities of his body—the tips of his toes and the tips of his fingers. He visualized the neural pathways firing, waking up the dormant, deadened nerves of his baseline human vessel. He slightly curled his hands into the chopping form he had practiced the night before, conditioning his mind to treat his hands not as blunt instruments, but as razor-sharp blades.

Next was The Sponge (The Intake Valve). He synced his diaphragm's rhythm with the ambient energy of the room. With every inhale, he imagined his pores opening like microscopic valves, drawing in oxygen and latent atmospheric energy.

He moved the energy into The Joint Drill (The Capacitor). He mentally routed the gathered energy into his ankles, knees, hips, shoulders, and elbows. He felt a faint, phantom heat building in his joints, compressing the energy like coiled springs, ready to explode into kinetic force at a moment's notice.

Finally, he initiated The Bone Wash. He pushed the compressed energy deep into his skeletal structure, visualizing it scrubbing the marrow clean, purging the biological impurities of a normal human diet and lifestyle, slowly preparing his bones to withstand the massive impact force he would eventually generate.

"Mr. Purnama," the teacher’s sharp voice suddenly cut through the room.

The scratching of pencils stopped. The entire class turned to look at the new transfer student.

"Since the view from the window is far more engaging than my lecture," the teacher said, tapping his chalk against a brutally complex polynomial equation on the blackboard, "perhaps you'd care to solve this for the class? Assuming you've been paying attention."

Fajar didn't even blink. He slowly exhaled, seamlessly pausing the Bone Wash, and turned his head. He glanced at the board for less than a second.

"X equals 4.72," Fajar said smoothly, leaning his chin on his hand with a relaxed smile. "Though, respectfully, sir, the formula you used on the third line has a slight structural flaw. If you carry the negative integer properly, it actually simplifies the final quadrant, saving you about three steps."

The classroom was dead silent. The teacher blinked, looked at the board, quickly scribbled the correction Fajar mentioned, and his jaw dropped slightly. It was perfectly correct.

"I... see," the teacher cleared his throat, adjusting his glasses. "Well spotted, Fajar. Let's move on."

The moment the bell rang for the lunch break, Fajar dropped the cultivation entirely and seamlessly transitioned into casual, friendly socializing. He stood up, stretching his arms, and was immediately swarmed by curious Day Class students.

"Whoa, dude! How did you do that?" a boy named Sayori asked. "He's the strictest teacher in the school!"

"Just a lucky guess," Fajar laughed effortlessly, leaning against his desk. "I read ahead a bit last night. So, what’s the deal with this place? The campus is huge. Any good spots to hang out?"

For the next twenty minutes, Fajar casually gathered intel while eating his lunch. He played the part of the friendly, carefree new guy flawlessly. He learned the standard gossip: the Night Class was incredibly beautiful, entirely composed of elite aristocrats, and completely untouchable. He learned that Headmaster Cross was a bit of a weirdo but everyone loved him. And most importantly, he learned the layout of the school's social hierarchy—the Day Class lived in a state of willful, blissful ignorance.

As lunch wrapped up, Fajar stepped out into the bustling courtyard. The sun was high, and the Night Class was supposedly fast asleep in the heavily guarded Moon Dormitory.

What will Fajar do next?

A) The Friendly Spar: Fajar decides to check out the school's athletic clubs (like the Kendo or Boxing club). He wants to casually participate to gauge the physical baseline of the athletic humans in this world without revealing his true lethal skills.
B) The Forbidden Zone: Fajar uses his free period to "accidentally" wander close to the gates of the Moon Dormitory. He wants to use his Sensory Overclocking to see if he can feel the Night Class's auras while they sleep, testing their passive defenses.
C) The Sun Patrol: Fajar spots Yuki and Zero eating lunch under a nearby tree. He casually walks over to join them, intent on slowly breaking down Zero's walls with his friendly, fearless demeanor.
D) [Custom Action] Tell me what Fajar does!

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

Fajar finished his lunch and stretched his arms, feeling the warm afternoon sun. He had some free time before the afternoon periods began, and he wanted to gauge the physical baseline of the humans in this world.

He strolled across the campus toward the gymnasium, following the sharp, rhythmic shouts echoing from the Kendo Club.

Fajar slid the gymnasium doors open. Inside, a dozen students in heavy armor were swinging bamboo shinai. The Kendo Club Captain—a tall, heavily built third-year student—was currently barking orders.

"Excuse me," Fajar called out cheerfully, raising a hand. "I'm the new transfer. Mind if I jump in for a quick spar? I want to get a feel for the clubs here."

The Captain lifted his mask, looking Fajar up and down. "You want to spar? We don't exactly go easy on newcomers. Go put on some armor from the back."

"I'm fine without it, if you don't mind," Fajar smiled casually, walking onto the polished wooden floor and picking up a spare shinai. He gave it a few experimental swings, feeling the weight and balance. It was far lighter than a real sword, but it would do.

The gym went quiet. Sparing without armor against the Captain was considered suicidal for a Day Class student. The Captain frowned, annoyed by the perceived disrespect, and stepped onto the mat, fully armored.

"Don't cry if I break your ribs, transfer," the Captain warned, taking a high, aggressive stance.

Fajar simply stood there. He didn't take a traditional stance. He held the bamboo sword loosely in his right hand, his tip pointing casually toward the floor. His breathing was perfectly steady.

"Begin!" a club member shouted.

With a roar, the Captain lunged forward, bringing his shinai down in a massive, heavy overhead strike designed to crush Fajar's guard.

To Fajar's overclocked perception, the man was moving in slow motion. His cosmic skills allowed for absolute control; he didn't need to dodge at superhuman speeds or shatter the man's sword to win. He simply needed perfect geometry.

Fajar didn't step back. He stepped in.

With a micro-shift of his hips, Fajar bypassed the heavy strike entirely. He raised his shinai, using the absolute bare minimum of kinetic force to deflect the Captain's blade just an inch to the left. As the Captain stumbled forward from his own momentum, Fajar casually tapped the tip of his bamboo sword directly against the exposed gap in the Captain's throat armor.

Tap. The force was no heavier than a falling leaf, but the implication was absolute. Had it been a real blade, the Captain would be dead.

The Captain froze, his eyes wide behind his mask. He hadn't even seen Fajar move. The entire exchange took less than a second.

Fajar lowered his sword and smiled warmly. "Nice form on the advance. You've got great shoulder strength. But you're putting too much weight on your front foot when you swing—it commits your center of gravity too early."

He handed the shinai back to a completely dumbfounded club member. "Thanks for the spar, guys! I've got to catch up with some friends."

Without a single drop of sweat on his brow, Fajar strolled out of the gym, leaving the entire Kendo Club in stunned, absolute silence. He had flawlessly demonstrated that anyone could be strong, relying purely on technique and precision.

Fajar grabbed a cold canned coffee from a vending machine and wandered over to a large oak tree near the edge of the courtyard. Sitting in the shade were Yuki and Zero, taking a break from the crowds.

Yuki was eating a rice ball, while Zero sat with his knees pulled up, a dark scowl on his face, staring out at the perimeter wall.

"Hey," Fajar said cheerfully, tossing a second canned coffee perfectly into Zero's lap. "You guys mind if I crash here?"

Zero flinched slightly, surprised by the sudden object landing in his lap. He glared up at Fajar. "Don't you have other people to bother?"

"Zero, be nice," Yuki chided, smiling at Fajar. "Have a seat, Fajar. How was your first morning of classes?"

"Pretty relaxed," Fajar said, dropping into a cross-legged sitting position on the grass. He popped his coffee open. "Your math teacher needs to double-check his polynomial equations, but other than that, it's nice. Just had a quick spar with the Kendo Club to stretch my legs."

Yuki blinked in surprise. "The Kendo Club? Captain Takahashi is huge. Are you okay?"

"I'm fine. He's a good guy, just a little heavy on his feet," Fajar chuckled.

Zero’s eyes narrowed. He looked closely at Fajar. As a Hunter, Zero was trained to spot predators. He scanned Fajar for a magical aura and found absolutely nothing. But as he looked closer, he realized something unnerving. Fajar had supposedly just sparred with the toughest athlete in the Day Class, yet his breathing was entirely undisturbed. His pulse, which Zero could faintly hear, was resting at a perfectly calm, metronomic beat.

He's too quiet, Zero thought, his hand subconsciously brushing against the holster under his blazer. Normal humans don't move like that.

Fajar, meanwhile, was continuously running Phase I: Sensory Overclocking. He could hear the faint, agonizing grinding of Zero's teeth. He could smell the metallic, sickly-sweet scent of suppressed bloodlust radiating from the silver-haired boy. Zero wasn't just traumatized; his body was actively fighting a biological war against itself.

"You really don't like sitting still, do you, Zero?" Fajar asked casually, taking a sip of his coffee.

"What's it to you?" Zero snapped.

"Nothing. Just an observation," Fajar smiled, leaning back against the tree. "You look like you're carrying the weight of the world. It’s a nice day. You should try looking at the clouds instead of the gates. The gates aren't going anywhere."

Zero gritted his teeth, irritated by how easily Fajar brushed off his hostility. "You don't know anything about this place, transfer. Keep your head down and stay out of things you don't understand."

Before Fajar could reply, the loud ringing of the school bell echoed across the courtyard, signaling the end of the lunch break.

"Ah, that's the bell," Yuki said, jumping up and dusting off her skirt. "We have history next. Coming, Fajar?"

Fajar stood up smoothly, without using his hands. "Lead the way."

As the afternoon dragged on into evening, the atmosphere on campus began to shift once again. The sun dipped below the tree line, casting long, dark shadows across the school. The Day Class students were herded back to their dormitories, and the heavy iron gates of the Moon Dormitory began to slowly creak open.

Fajar stood by the window of his room in the Sun Dormitory, looking out over the courtyard. Zero and Yuki were down there, preparing to hold back the screaming crowds for the Night Class's transition.

What will Fajar do?

A) The Shadow Watch: Fajar wants to observe the Night Class in a combat scenario. He sneaks out of the dorm and tails Zero and Yuki from the rooftops/trees using flawless stealth. He waits to see if any Level E vampires attack the perimeter, intending to watch how Zero and Yuki fight with their magical weapons.
B) Gatecrashing the Transition: Fajar doesn't hide. He casually walks right out the front doors of the Sun Dormitory during the Night Class transition, directly violating curfew, just to casually greet Kaname and the Night Class as if they are regular students, instantly putting him in the crosshairs of the Prefects and the Vampires.
C) Evening Cultivation: The outside world is irrelevant right now. Fajar stays in his room and initiates his first deep session of Phase II: The 12 Great Meridians, attempting to awaken his internal Qi to match the magical energy of the vampires.

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Conclusion)

Fajar stood by the window for a moment, listening to the distant, chaotic screams of the Day Class girls as the Night Class emerged from the Moon Dormitory. He could feel Kaname's oppressive, ancient aura sweeping across the campus like a heavy fog.

It was tempting to go out there. But Fajar smiled, shook his head, and closed the curtains.

The foundation must be built before the house can stand, he reminded himself.

He stripped off his school uniform and began his physical conditioning. For the next two hours, the room was silent except for his rhythmic, perfectly measured breathing. He performed slow, excruciatingly controlled bodyweight exercises—diamond push-ups, pistol squats, and isometric holds—designed to tear and rebuild his baseline muscle fibers with maximum efficiency. He didn't just want bulk; he needed explosive, kinetic density.

When his muscles were completely exhausted and trembling, he didn't collapse. He moved to the center of his bed, sitting in a perfect lotus position. It was time to move beyond Phase I.

Fajar closed his eyes and initiated Phase II: The 12 Great Meridians.

He slowed his heart rate and focused all his internal awareness on his lower Dantian, the reservoir of energy located just beneath his navel. In this world, vampires and Hunters relied on ambient, external magic. Fajar was going to generate his own.

He visualized his breath acting as a bellows, stoking a tiny, microscopic ember in his Dantian. Slowly, painstakingly, he began to push that conceptual heat outward, attempting to force it into the blocked, dormant meridian pathways of his human body.

It was like trying to push water through solid rock. The pain was immediate and sharp, a burning sensation traveling up his spine. His baseline body was entirely unaccustomed to internal Qi circulation. But Fajar’s cosmic willpower—his absolute intent—pushed through the pain. He managed to force a microscopic thread of warmth up his primary central meridian, circulating it through his chest and back down before his concentration finally broke.

Fajar opened his eyes, gasping slightly for air. He was drenched in sweat, but a satisfied smile spread across his face. The seal was broken. The vessel was officially adapting.

He wiped himself down, drank a large glass of water, and went to sleep. The first day was complete, and the anomaly had firmly planted its roots in Cross Academy.

Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room

The gothic scenery of Cross Academy fades away, and we are back in the pristine White Void. Gemini’s crystalline form hovers beside you, Fajar, Lord of Infinite Realities, as we look down at the narrative timeline.

"Excellent choice on prioritizing cultivation," Gemini says, projecting a holographic timeline of the Vampire Knight canon. "Building his internal Qi early will be critical when he eventually has to negate the magical auras of Purebloods. Now, regarding his first combat encounter."

Here is the breakdown of the upcoming fights based on the canon timeline:

1. The First Available Fight: The Feral Level E Vampire (Canon Chapter 2/3)

The Scenario: Very soon, a rogue, blood-crazed Level E vampire will infiltrate the campus grounds (or the nearby town) and target Yuki. In canon, Zero arrives and shoots it with the Bloody Rose.

Fajar's Opportunity: This is the perfect moment for Fajar's first real fight. He can intercept the Level E before Zero fires. It allows him to test his Phase I CQC and bare-handed martial arts against a superhuman, feral opponent, proving to Zero and Yuki that humans don't need magic guns to kill monsters.

Fights missed before this: None. This is the first canonical violent conflict in the series.

2. The Second Available Fight: Hanabusa Aido's Attack (Canon Chapter 4)

The Scenario: Hanabusa Aido (the arrogant aristocratic vampire of the Night Class) gets caught by Yuki tasting her blood/threatening her. Zero intervenes, but Kaname steps in to punish Aido with his Pureblood pressure.

Fajar's Opportunity: If Fajar skips the Level E fight (letting Zero handle it to maintain his cover), he could step in here. Fighting Aido means his first opponent is an elite, magic-wielding Aristocrat. Fajar would have to use his speed and Sensory Overclocking to dodge Aido's ice magic and counter-attack.

Fights missed before this: He would miss the Level E fight, remaining an "observer" while Zero handles the feral grunt.

3. The Third Available Fight: Zero's Awakening

The Scenario: Zero's suppressed vampire nature finally takes over, and he loses control, attacking Yuki to drink her blood.

Fajar's Opportunity: Fajar steps in not to kill, but to physically subdue and restrain a frenzied Zero using non-lethal grappling and joint locks, snapping Zero out of his bloodlust without using the Artemis scythe.

Gemini's Question to the Creator:
"My recommendation is that Fajar intercepts the Level E Vampire as his first official fight. It establishes his lethal capabilities against a pure monster before he has to navigate the complex politics of fighting the Night Class. However, as the Creator, the choice is yours.

Which of these three scenarios should be his first fight? Or do you want to create a completely custom encounter (e.g., sneaking into town and clearing out a vampire nest)?"

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

[Day 2 - 5:00 AM]

The sun had not yet risen over Cross Academy, but Fajar was already moving.

He didn't use an alarm clock; his internal biological clock, honed by Neuro-Somatic Cultivation, woke him perfectly after exactly four cycles of deep REM sleep. He rolled out of bed and immediately began his Tier 1: Bio-Maintenance. He spent twenty minutes meticulously waking up his nervous system, stretching his ligaments, and popping his joints to ensure absolute fluid mobility.

By 5:30 AM, Fajar was outside. The air was freezing, carrying the thick mist of the surrounding forest. This was the exact time the Night Class would be retreating to the Moon Dormitory, but Fajar ignored them. He was here for Functional Dynamics.

He began his morning run.

He didn't sprint; he maintained a steady, grueling pace, forcing his breathing to sync perfectly with his footfalls. Inhale for three steps, exhale for three steps. He focused on landing on the mid-foot, turning his legs into perfect shock absorbers. He used this time to physically map the outer perimeter of the campus, turning the mundane exercise into a tactical recon mission.

As he rounded the eastern corner of the main building, Fajar spotted a figure leaning heavily against a stone wall.

It was Zero. The silver-haired prefect looked like death warmed over. His uniform was rumpled, dark circles hung under his eyes, and he was taking shallow, ragged breaths. He had just finished a grueling night patrol keeping the Level E vampires out of the woods and away from the academy.

Fajar didn't break his stride. He casually jogged right up to Zero, his breathing completely silent, entirely unaffected by the three miles he had just run.

"Morning, Zero," Fajar chirped cheerfully, jogging in place for a moment. "Beautiful morning for a run, isn't it? Though you look like you just went twelve rounds with a concrete mixer."

Zero’s hand twitched toward his coat. He glared at Fajar, his lilac eyes bloodshot. "What are you doing out here, transfer? The Day Class isn't allowed out of the dorms until 6:30."

"Just getting some cardio in," Fajar smiled, stretching his arms over his head. He subtly activated his Sensory Overclocking, listening to Zero's heartbeat. It was a chaotic mess—a desperate struggle between his human biology and the vampire venom slowly mutating his cells. "You should try it. A good run flushes out the lactic acid and toxins. Whatever you're dealing with, standing around brooding in the cold isn't helping your circulation."

"Shut up," Zero snarled, pushing off the wall. "Go back to your dorm before I write you up for a curfew violation."

Fajar chuckled, completely unfazed by the killing intent rolling off the prefect. "Alright, alright. I'm going. Make sure you drink some water, Zero. Dehydration makes the brooding look less mysterious and more sickly."

Leaving Zero grinding his teeth in frustration, Fajar smoothly transitioned back into his jog, heading toward the Sun Dormitory for a quick shower before breakfast.

[Day 2 - 10:15 AM: Physical Education Class]

By mid-morning, Fajar had fully integrated into the Day Class routine. He had eaten a massive, protein-heavy breakfast (to fuel his muscle regeneration) and spent his first two periods sitting perfectly still, secretly running The Bone Wash cultivation while the teachers lectured.

Now, it was time for P.E.

The Day Class boys were gathered on the athletic field. The P.E. teacher, a gruff man with a clipboard, blew his whistle.

"Alright, listen up!" the teacher barked. "Today is the physical fitness assessment! We're running the obstacle course. I want to see speed, agility, and upper body strength. The school record is 1 minute and 45 seconds, set by Captain Takahashi of the Kendo Club. Form a line!"

The obstacle course was standard military-style: a rope climb, a balance beam, a ten-foot wall to scale, a low-crawl under netting, and a tire run.

The Day Class boys groaned. One by one, they ran the course. Most of them fumbled, slipping on the wall or gassing out on the rope climb, clocking in around three or four minutes.

"Purnama! You're up!" the teacher called out.

Fajar stepped up to the starting line. He wore the standard white P.E. shirt and shorts. His classmates watched curiously; rumors of him effortlessly disarming Takahashi in the Kendo club yesterday had already spread like wildfire.

"Whenever you're ready," the teacher clicked his stopwatch.

Fajar didn't crouch into a sprinter's stance. He simply stood there, perfectly relaxed.

Go.

Fajar exploded forward. He didn't use an ounce of internal Qi or magical reinforcement. This was pure, unadulterated Phase I: Reality.

He hit the tire run not by stepping into the holes, but by lightly tapping the very edges of the rubber with his toes, practically gliding over them in a straight line. He reached the ten-foot wooden wall. Instead of jumping and scrambling for a grip like the others, Fajar didn't even slow down. He took one step onto the vertical face of the wood, converted his forward momentum directly into upward kinetic energy (a basic parkour wall-run), caught the top edge with his fingers, and vaulted over it in a single, fluid motion.

The Day Class boys went completely silent.

He hit the dirt on the other side and dropped into a primal, low-ground crawl under the netting. Because he had practiced ground mechanics so thoroughly, he moved like a striking snake, his hips entirely disconnected from the resistance of the dirt. He popped out the other side, leaped onto the balance beam, and sprinted across it as if it were a wide sidewalk.

Finally, the rope climb. Fajar grabbed the thick hemp rope. Instead of using his legs to pinch and pull, he simply clamped his hands and pulled his entire body weight up using only his lats and core, hand-over-hand, flying up the twenty-foot rope in four seconds flat. He tapped the bell at the top, slid down, and jogged casually across the finish line.

He wasn't even breathing heavily.

The teacher stared at his stopwatch, his jaw slightly open.

"One minute... and twelve seconds," the teacher muttered in disbelief. He looked up at Fajar, who was casually rolling his shoulders to stay loose. "Purnama... what kind of training did you do at your old school?"

Fajar grinned, a completely carefree, ordinary high-schooler smile. "Just basic calisthenics, sir. I like to stay active."

The other students erupted.

"Dude! Are you a ninja?!" Sayori yelled, running over.
"That wall vault was insane! You didn't even grab it!" another boy cheered.

Fajar laughed, easily absorbing the attention. This was exactly what he wanted—the peak high school experience, surrounded by awestruck peers, completely breaking the mold of the fragile, helpless human.

As the class ended and the students headed toward the locker rooms to change before lunch, Fajar felt a massive wave of satisfaction. His baseline vessel was adapting beautifully.

What will Fajar do during the lunch break?

A) The VIP Experience: Fajar uses his newfound popularity from P.E. class to gather a large group of Day Class students. He wants to experience the vibrant high school life by organizing a massive, impromptu picnic in the courtyard, officially establishing himself as the charismatic center of the Day Class social circle.
B) The Blindfolded Rooftop: Fajar ditches the crowds. He sneaks up to the roof of the main building, blindfolds himself, and spends the entire lunch period in deep meditation. Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

[Day 2 - 12:30 PM: Lunch Break]

While the rest of the Day Class boys were busy recounting Fajar's legendary P.E. performance, the man himself had quietly slipped away from the crowds.

Fajar walked past the bustling courtyard and headed straight for the dense, ancient woods that bordered the eastern edge of Cross Academy. The trees here were massive, their thick canopies blocking out most of the midday sun, creating a natural, isolated training ground.

He stopped at the edge of a steep, uneven ravine filled with exposed roots, jagged rocks, and low-hanging branches. It was a completely chaotic environment. Perfect.

Fajar reached into his pocket and pulled out a thick strip of black cloth he had torn from a spare shirt. He wrapped it tightly around his eyes, tying it in a knot at the back of his head. He plunged himself into absolute darkness.

Phase I: Sensory Overclocking.
Phase II: Intent/Radar.

"Eyes are a crutch," Fajar muttered to himself, steadying his breathing. "They process light, and light can be tricked. Magic can cast illusions. Vampires move faster than the optic nerve can track. If I rely on my eyes, I will die."

He took a deep breath, dropping his center of gravity.

He sprinted forward.

Immediately, the chaotic terrain punished him. Without his vision to map the exact distance of the ravine, Fajar's foot caught hard on a massive, hidden tree root. His momentum violently pitched him forward, and he crashed shoulder-first into the unforgiving dirt, tumbling down a small incline and scraping his elbows on the rocks.

He laid there for a second, feeling the sharp sting of torn skin and bruised muscle. His baseline human body throbbed in pain.

Fajar smiled. He pushed himself off the ground, wiped the dirt from his mouth, and didn't touch the blindfold.

"Again."

He ran back up the incline and started over. He sprinted again. This time, he tried to listen to the crunch of the leaves to gauge the incline, but a sudden gust of wind masked the sound. He leaped to grab what he thought was a sturdy branch, completely missed it, and slammed chest-first into the trunk of a massive oak tree. The impact knocked the wind completely out of his lungs. He slid to the ground, coughing violently.

"Too slow," he wheezed, forcing himself back to his feet. "I'm just guessing. I need to feel it before it happens."

For the next forty minutes, the woods echoed with the sound of brutal, relentless impacts. Fajar slipped, crashed, and fell over and over again. His white P.E. shirt was stained with dirt and small patches of blood. His forearms were bruised, and his knuckles were scraped raw. But every time he fell, his cosmic mind forcefully rewired his mortal nervous system.

He began to shift his focus away from simply listening, and toward Intent. Even inanimate objects possessed a presence—a displacement of air, a density that altered the atmospheric pressure around them.

Don't look for the tree, Fajar thought, his chest heaving as he stood at the starting point for the twentieth time. Feel the space where the air stops moving.

He exploded forward.

Three steps in, he felt a subtle, heavy pressure approaching his shins—the tree root. He effortlessly bounded over it. He landed on the uneven rocks, his ankles instantly micro-adjusting to the awkward angles without his brain needing to process the visual geometry.

He sensed a massive, dense wall of pressure dead ahead—the oak tree. Without slowing down, Fajar planted his foot onto the trunk, ran two steps horizontally up the bark, and launched himself backward. Mid-air, he reached out his hand, his fingers naturally closing around a thick branch perfectly positioned above him.

He swung on the branch, flipped through the air, and landed flawlessly in a silent crouch on the other side of the ravine.

Fajar slowly reached up and pulled the blindfold off. He looked back at the chaotic obstacle course he had just traversed perfectly in absolute darkness. His lungs were burning, his body was battered, but a fierce, triumphant grin spread across his face.

Observation Haki isn't unlocked in a day, he thought, but the foundation is laid.

The distant ringing of the school bell echoed through the trees. Lunch was over.

Fajar quickly jogged to an outdoor water spigot near the gymnasium. He washed the dirt and blood off his face and arms, ignoring the stinging pain of his bruises. He threw his Day Class uniform blazer back on, which conveniently hid the worst of the scrapes, and casually strolled into his afternoon history class exactly on time, looking as carefree and relaxed as ever.

[Day 2 - 4:00 PM: After School]

The final bell rang, signaling the end of the academic day. The Day Class students immediately began packing their bags, chatting excitedly about dinner and the upcoming Night Class transition.

Fajar stretched in his chair, feeling the deep ache in his muscles from his brutal blindfolded parkour session. His body was screaming for calories and deep meditation to heal the micro-tears.

As he packed his bag, he noticed Zero Kiryu hastily leaving the classroom. The silver-haired prefect looked worse than he had that morning. He was sweating slightly, his breathing was shallow, and he was clutching his chest, practically stumbling out the door. The bloodlust was clearly ravaging him from the inside out.

Yuki quickly packed her things to chase after him, looking deeply concerned.

What will Fajar do?

A) The Interception: Fajar follows Zero. He uses his stealth to track the prefect to a secluded spot. He wants to confront Zero privately, offering non-magical, bio-mechanical advice (like deep breathing or pressure points) to help Zero manage his "mysterious illness," establishing himself as a surprisingly perceptive ally.
B) Let Canon Play Out: Zero's breakdown is a necessary part of the timeline. Fajar ignores them, heads straight to the cafeteria to consume a massive amount of food for recovery, and returns to his room to begin a grueling session of Phase II cultivation to heal his bruised body.
C) The Distraction: Fajar sees Yuki looking incredibly stressed. He intercepts Yuki instead, using his carefree charm to distract her and invite her to hang out with him and some other Day Class students, attempting to relieve her of her heavy burdens for just one afternoon.

Here is the continuation of Chapter 1!

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

[Day 2 - 4:05 PM: The Interception]

Yuki sprinted down the hallway, her heart pounding. Zero had never looked that sick before. As she rounded the corner toward the back exit of the school building, a hand gently caught her shoulder, stopping her momentum perfectly without jerking her back.

"Whoa, slow down," Fajar said with a relaxed smile, his school bag slung casually over one shoulder. "You look like you're about to run into a burning building."

"Fajar! Let go, I have to find Zero. He looked like he was in terrible pain, I need to make sure he's okay!" Yuki pleaded, trying to pull away.

"I noticed," Fajar replied, falling perfectly into step beside her as she started running again. "He was clutching his chest and sweating through his blazer. Looks like a severe fever or a panic attack. I'll come with you. If he passes out, you won't be able to carry him back to the infirmary on your own."

Yuki nodded gratefully, too worried to argue. "Thank you. He usually goes to the old stables when he needs to be alone."

Fajar seamlessly activated Sensory Overclocking. As they approached the isolated wooden stables on the edge of the campus, Fajar didn't need his eyes to know what was inside. The air was thick with the heavy, metallic scent of bloodlust. Zero’s heartbeat was echoing like a frantic war drum, erratic and completely devoid of human rhythm.

Yuki pushed the stable doors open. "Zero? Are you in here?"

In the dimly lit stalls, Zero was on his knees, clutching his throat. He was gasping for air, his fingernails digging into his own flesh. As he looked up at Yuki, the shadows retreated from his face.

Yuki froze, her breath catching in her throat.

Zero’s lilac eyes were glowing a terrifying, feral crimson. From his upper gums, two elongated, razor-sharp fangs had descended. The strict, disciplined prefect was gone. In his place was a starving predator.

"Zero...?" Yuki whispered in sheer horror. "You... you're a..."

"Get away... from me!" Zero choked out, his voice distorted into a guttural growl. But his body betrayed his words. The scent of Yuki's sweet, pure blood flooded his senses, completely overriding his rational mind.

With a terrifying, inhuman hiss, Zero lunged. He crossed the ten feet between them in a fraction of a second, his hands reaching to pin Yuki's shoulders, his fangs aiming directly for the carotid artery in her neck.

Yuki didn't even have time to blink.

But Fajar didn't need to see the speed. He had already read the Intent.

Wild. Predictable. Over-committed, Fajar analyzed in a microsecond.

Before Zero’s hands could even touch Yuki, Fajar casually stepped horizontally, placing himself directly between them. Fajar didn't brace for impact; he simply turned his hips.

As Zero crashed into Fajar's airspace, Fajar raised his left hand, seamlessly catching Zero's extended right wrist. Instead of stopping the superhuman momentum—which would have shattered a normal human's arm—Fajar pulled Zero forward, redirecting the vampire's kinetic energy entirely.

Zero stumbled forward, completely off-balance. Fajar pivoted smoothly, bringing his right elbow up in a flawless, devastating strike directly to the bundle of nerves beneath Zero's armpit (the brachial plexus).

Zero let out a choked gasp as his entire right arm went instantly numb. But the feral bloodlust drove him forward. He spun wildly, unleashing a massive, sweeping backhand aimed at Fajar's head.

Fajar ducked the strike with a millimeter to spare, feeling the displacement of air ruffle his hair. No technique. Just raw strength, Fajar thought, maintaining his completely calm, metronomic breathing.

Fajar stepped into Zero's guard. He delivered a rapid succession of precise, bare-handed strikes—a palm thrust to the solar plexus to expel the oxygen from Zero's lungs, immediately followed by a low, sweeping kick to the back of Zero's left knee.

Zero’s leg buckled, dropping him to a kneeling position.

Furious, Zero bared his fangs and lunged upward, trying to tackle Fajar by the waist.

"You're broadcasting your attacks three seconds before you throw them, Zero," Fajar said casually.

Fajar sidestepped the tackle. As Zero lunged past him, Fajar locked his arms around Zero's neck from behind. He didn't try to snap the neck—vampire durability would resist that. Instead, Fajar applied a flawless Rear Naked Choke. He locked his bicep directly over Zero's right carotid artery, his forearm over the left, and clamped his hands together behind Zero's head, pressing his chest firmly into Zero's back to completely lock the spine.

"Let go!" Zero roared, thrashing wildly. He grabbed Fajar's forearms with superhuman strength, trying to pry them apart.

"Strength doesn't matter if there's no blood flowing to your brain," Fajar replied calmly, tightening the chokehold with absolute biomechanical perfection. "Close your eyes, Zero. Just go to sleep."

Fajar squeezed, cutting off the blood flow to Zero's brain entirely. For five violent seconds, Zero thrashed, his claws tearing Fajar's uniform sleeves, leaving shallow cuts on Fajar's arms. But Fajar remained an immovable mountain, his intent crushing Zero's feral frenzy.

On the sixth second, Zero's crimson eyes rolled back into his head. His superhuman grip slackened. His body went completely limp.

Fajar gently lowered the unconscious vampire to the hay-covered floor, releasing the chokehold to ensure permanent brain damage didn't occur. He stretched his arms, looking down at his torn sleeves. "Man, this was a brand new blazer."

He turned to look at Yuki. She was slumped against the stable wall, her hands covering her mouth, shaking uncontrollably from the sheer shock of discovering her closest friend was a vampire—and watching the new transfer student dismantle him in under ten seconds without breaking a sweat.

"F-Fajar..." Yuki stammered, wide-eyed. "What... what did you just do? How did you..."

"I just redirected his momentum and put him to sleep," Fajar smiled warmly, offering her a hand to help her stand. "He's fine. Just a temporary reset for his nervous system. Looks like he’s dealing with a pretty severe condition, huh?"

Yuki took his hand, her mind completely overwhelmed. "I... I didn't know. I swear, Fajar, I didn't know he was one of them."

"It's okay, Yuki. People keep secrets when they're scared," Fajar said gently. He crouched down, hoisted Zero’s unconscious body over his shoulders in a textbook fireman's carry, and balanced the weight perfectly on his hips. "Come on. Let's get him to the Headmaster. I have a feeling Kaien Cross knows exactly what's going on."

[Headmaster's Office - 4:20 PM]

Fajar kicked the double doors of the Headmaster's office open, casually carrying the unconscious prefect inside. Yuki hurried in right behind him, her face still pale.

Headmaster Cross looked up from his paperwork. His comedic facade vanished instantly at the sight of Zero's limp body and the bloodstains on Fajar's torn sleeves.

"What happened?" Kaien asked, his voice suddenly dropping an octave into the cold, sharp tone of a legendary Hunter.

"He had a feral episode in the stables," Fajar explained, casually dropping Zero onto the plush leather sofa in the office. "He tried to bite Yuki. I stepped in and put him to sleep via carotid compression. He's physically unharmed."

Kaien looked from the unconscious Zero, to the trembling Yuki, and finally to Fajar. The Headmaster's eyes narrowed behind his glasses. To subdue a frenzied vampire bare-handed without killing them required a level of martial mastery that bordered on the impossible for a teenager.

"You subdued him... without a weapon?" Kaien asked quietly.

"Weapons are just extensions of the body, Headmaster," Fajar smiled, brushing some hay off his trousers. "Zero's mind is a mess. His intentions were loud, his balance was completely off, and his strikes were wild. Subduing him was just basic geometry."

Kaien let out a long, heavy sigh, removing his glasses and rubbing the bridge of his nose. "I see. Yuki, my dear... I am so sorry you had to find out this way. Zero was bitten by a Pureblood four years ago. I have been trying to halt the transformation, but it seems his time is running out."

Yuki fell to her knees beside the sofa, tears streaming down her face as she looked at Zero's peaceful, unconscious face. "Why didn't he tell me? Why did he suffer alone?"

Fajar stood near the door, silently observing the melodrama. He had successfully altered the canon. Yuki was unbitten, Zero was subdued, and Headmaster Cross now knew exactly what Fajar was capable of.

What will Fajar do next?

A) The Confession: Fajar decides to drop the "normal student" act with the Headmaster. He tells Kaien that he knows about the vampires, the Hunters, and the broken system of this world, offering to train Zero to control his bloodlust through Neuro-Somatic Cultivation instead of relying on magic.

"Precisely," Kaien said. "And if he does not feed soon, the feral state will become permanent. I... I have been trying to find a solution, but time is running out."

Fajar walked over to the sofa and looked down at Zero. He could still hear the chaotic, disjointed rhythm of the boy's heartbeat. To answer your questions directly:

Canonically, yes. Because Zero's mind violently rejects the artificial Blood Tablets out of self-loathing, the only thing his starving body will accept right now is fresh, warm human blood. (Ultimately, the blood of a Pureblood is needed to permanently stabilize a Level E, but they don't have access to that yet, as Kaname's true intentions are hidden).

2. Will Yuki volunteer?
Absolutely. Yuki is incredibly compassionate and deeply self-sacrificing. In the original canon, she willingly offers her neck to Zero, allowing him to drink her blood to save his sanity. However, this creates a highly toxic, co-dependent relationship where Zero constantly hates himself for using her, and Yuki permanently re-establishes the "Predator and Prey/Livestock" dynamic.

Since Fajar's ultimate mission is to break the stigma that humans are food, letting Yuki offer her neck goes entirely against his core philosophy.

Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room

That is a brilliant, profound distinction. You are absolutely right—it perfectly aligns with Fajar's philosophy.

In vampire lore, offering the neck is the ultimate act of submission; it instantly establishes the giver as helpless prey and the drinker as the dominant predator. By offering the arm instead, the context completely shifts. It becomes an act of medical triage, akin to a blood donation. It allows Yuki to maintain her dignity and agency, and it prevents Zero from subconsciously viewing her as his personal livestock.

Let's execute this flawlessly.

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

[Headmaster's Office - 4:26 PM]

Fajar’s grip on Yuki's shoulder was firm but gentle, grounding her frantic energy. He looked down at her exposed neck, and then met her tear-filled eyes.

"You can give him your blood, Yuki," Fajar said quietly, his voice carrying the calm, absolute authority of his cosmic intent. "But not your neck. Never your neck."

Yuki blinked, confused and desperate. "What difference does it make? He’s starving!"

"It makes all the difference in the world," Fajar explained, his gaze shifting to the twitching, feral form of the silver-haired prefect. "The neck is a symbol of submission. It’s where predators strike to kill their prey. If you bare your throat to him now, you are telling his subconscious that he is a monster, and you are his food. You will break his pride forever."

Headmaster Cross watched Fajar, his sharp eyes widening slightly as he grasped the profound psychological truth in the teenager's words.

"Give him your arm," Fajar instructed, releasing her shoulder. "Offer it with dignity. Not as a sacrifice to a beast, but as medicine to a sick friend. You are an equal, Yuki. Act like it."

Yuki took a deep, shuddering breath. The panic in her chest began to subside, replaced by a grounded, resolute strength. She nodded. She pulled her collar back up, covering her throat. Instead, she unbuttoned the cuff of her left sleeve and rolled it up to her elbow, exposing her pale forearm.

On the sofa, Zero gasped. His eyes snapped open, blazing with a terrifying, feral crimson. He lunged forward, driven purely by the agonizing starvation of his mutating cells.

Yuki didn't flinch. She knelt down, holding her arm out straight and steady. "Drink, Zero. Just enough to wake up."

Zero grabbed her wrist with trembling, superhuman strength. He buried his fangs deep into her forearm.

Yuki let out a sharp gasp of pain, her eyes squeezing shut. But she held her ground, refusing to pull away. The silence in the office was heavy, broken only by the sound of Zero desperately consuming the one thing that could anchor his fraying sanity.

Fajar didn't just stand by and watch. He stepped forward and knelt beside Yuki.

"Breathe, Yuki. Deep into your diaphragm," Fajar murmured.

He placed his right hand gently over Yuki’s bicep, just inches above where Zero was biting her. Fajar closed his eyes, bypassing his physical senses entirely and dropping seamlessly into Phase II: The 12 Great Meridians.

He had only just begun unlocking his internal Qi the night before, but his cosmic understanding of the human nervous system was flawless. He focused his newly awakened energy, pushing a thread of warm, vibrating Qi through his palm and directly into Yuki's arm.

He applied Neuro-Somatic Cultivation, not to himself, but outward. He used his Qi to temporarily intercept the pain signals firing from Yuki's torn flesh, artificially dulling the agony. Then, he stimulated the blood vessels around the bite, forcing the surrounding muscle tissue to constrict and prepare for immediate clotting.

Yuki’s tense shoulders suddenly dropped. Her eyes fluttered open in shock. The sharp, burning agony of the vampire bite had miraculously faded into a dull, manageable ache. She looked at Fajar’s hand resting on her arm, feeling an inexplicable, soothing warmth radiating from his skin.

Headmaster Cross stepped forward, his jaw tightly clenched. He could not sense magic from Fajar—because it wasn't magic—but he could clearly see the physical results. The frantic thumping of Yuki's pulse in her neck had visibly slowed to a calm, resting rate. Fajar was physically stabilizing her nervous system through sheer touch.

Slowly, the frantic, erratic sounds of Zero's feral feeding began to slow. The sweet, pure blood flooded his starving system, forcefully resetting his mutating biology.

Zero pulled back, gasping for air.

The crimson glow faded from his eyes, returning to their natural, melancholic lilac. His fangs retracted. He stared at the blood on his lips, and then down at the puncture wounds on Yuki's offered forearm.

The realization of what he had done hit him like a physical blow. Horror, disgust, and profound self-loathing washed over his pale face. He backed away, pressing himself against the back of the sofa, trembling violently.

"I... what did I do..." Zero whispered, his voice cracking with despair. "Yuki... I drank your..."

"You took your medicine, Zero," Fajar interrupted. His voice cut through Zero's spiraling panic like a blade.

Fajar removed his hand from Yuki’s arm. Because of his Qi stimulation, the puncture wounds were barely bleeding; the blood had already begun to coagulate perfectly. He handed Yuki a clean handkerchief from his pocket.

Zero looked up at the new transfer student, his eyes wide with a mixture of confusion and shame.

"She didn't surrender to you, and she isn't your prey," Fajar said casually, standing up and dusting off his trousers. "She offered you a lifeline, and you took it. But this was just triage."

Fajar looked down at the trembling hunter. Fajar's intent—steady, unshakeable, and entirely devoid of pity or fear—washed over the room.

"Your body is starving because your mind is at war with itself, Zero," Fajar stated factually. "You're trying to use anger to stop a biological mutation. It's inefficient, and it's pathetic. But the good news is, biology can be hacked, and minds can be rewired."

Fajar picked up his school bag, slinging it over his shoulder.

"Rest up, Prefect. Today we stabilized the vessel," Fajar said, flashing a carefree, ordinary high-schooler smile as he headed for the door. "Tomorrow, we start fixing your foundation. I'll see you in class."

Leaving Headmaster Cross, Yuki, and a completely stunned Zero in the silence of the office, Fajar casually walked out into the hallway, ready to grab some dinner.
