[Day 3 - 12:20 PM: The Old Campus Greenhouse]

Fajar looked at the brave, completely un-hypnotized human girl standing before him. For a long moment, the greenhouse was utterly silent.

Then, Fajar smiled. It wasn't the polite, distant smile of a transfer student, nor was it the arrogant smirk of the Night Class. It was a genuine, deeply appreciative grin.

"You are absolutely spot on, Wakaba-san," Fajar said, his voice dropping its casual tone, replacing it with the grounded cadence of a martial arts master addressing a promising talent. "You're right. I'm not a normal student, the injury wasn't a scrape, and Cross Academy is absolutely not what it pretends to be."

Yori didn't relax her posture, but her eyes widened slightly at his blunt honesty. "So you admit it."

"I have no reason to lie to someone who has the eyes to see the truth," Fajar replied, standing up from the concrete bench. He stretched his arms, his joints popping with a crisp, fluid sound. "I am here to protect the human students, and by extension, Yuki. But before we cooperate, I need to test exactly how sharp those eyes of yours really are."

Yori narrowed her eyes. "A test?"

"An assignment," Fajar corrected. "You've noticed the symptoms, but you don't know the disease. Over the next few days, I want you to investigate the academy yourself. Look at the logistics. Look at the Night Class's habits, the medical supply shipments to the Headmaster's office, the way the Disciplinary Committee is structured. Take as much time as you like. Come back to me tomorrow, or the day after, or a week from now. When you have a working theory about what the Night Class actually is, find me."

Fajar picked up his empty bento box and walked past her toward the exit. He paused at the door, glancing back over his shoulder.

"Stay in the shadows, Yori. Don't let them catch you looking."

[Days 4 to 6 - Fajar's Internal Progression]

While Yori spent the next few days quietly turning the Day Class upside down with her observations, Fajar focused entirely on his vessel's internal architecture.

During the boring daytime lectures, Fajar wasn't just sitting still; he was aggressively cycling his internal energy. He had already mastered Phase I: Bio-Maintenance, aligning his bones and muscles perfectly. Now, he was pushing deeper into the esoteric foundation of his cultivation.

By the evening of the fourth day, Fajar achieved a critical breakthrough. Sitting cross-legged on his dormitory bed, he forcefully guided his intent through the 12 Great Meridians (Step 1.5). The latent, stagnant energy blockages within the human teenager's body shattered. His neuro-somatic network completely smoothed out. His nervous system and blood vessels synchronized perfectly, allowing his brain to send electrical signals to his muscles at near-instantaneous speeds without tearing the fibers.

By the sixth day, Fajar didn't stop. He pushed the newly purified energy deeper, breaking into the 8 Extraordinary Meridians (Step 2).

A wave of profound, boiling heat washed over his internal organs, followed immediately by an absolute, terrifying lightness. The Extraordinary Meridians acted as massive reservoirs for his Qi. He no longer just had perfect posture; he had a bottomless well of stamina. He could now run for days without sleeping, process complex information instantly, and hit with the kinetic force of a speeding truck without using a single drop of magic.

The human baseline was established. He was ready for a fight.

[Day 6 - 5:00 PM: The School Library Archives]

The library was mostly empty as the afternoon sun cast long, orange rays through the stained-glass windows. Fajar was sitting at a corner table, casually flipping through an advanced anatomy textbook.

Footsteps approached. Fajar didn't need to look up. His Radar Intent easily recognized the steady, grounded heartbeat and practical stride of Sayori Wakaba.

Yori sat down across from him and placed a small, leather-bound notebook on the table. She looked exhausted, but her eyes were burning with intellectual triumph.

"Three days," Fajar noted, closing his textbook. "I'm impressed. What did you find?"

"A logistical nightmare," Yori said, keeping her voice to a low whisper. She opened the notebook, revealing pages of meticulously organized data. "I checked the cafeteria manifests. The Night Class orders massive amounts of luxury food, but based on the waste disposal weights, they barely eat a fraction of it. They're faking their caloric intake."

Fajar nodded approvingly. "Good. What else?"

"Their physical traits," Yori continued, pointing to her notes. "Zero Kiryu's hostility isn't just emotional prejudice. I watched his hands when Hanabusa Aido walked past the other night. Zero's pulse skyrocketed, and his pupils dilated—it was a biological fight-or-flight response. The Night Class themselves are unnaturally fast, they avoid direct sunlight like it's a physical irritant, and their skin temperature is demonstrably lower than human average based on the condensation of their breath in the cold evening air."

She flipped to the final page, a list of shipments delivered to Headmaster Cross.

"And then there's this," Yori said, her voice grim. "The Headmaster receives a massive shipment of 'effervescent iron supplements' every month. But they don't go to the student infirmary. They go directly to the Moon Dormitory. Iron supplements. Pale skin. Fake eating. Fast healing."

Yori closed the notebook and looked Fajar in the eye.

"They aren't a normal aristocratic elite," Yori concluded. "They're a biological anomaly. Some kind of apex predator species that mimics humans but sustains itself on something else entirely. And the school is a massive containment facility designed to keep us from realizing we are locked in a cage with them."

Fajar stared at her for a moment. Then, slowly, he raised his hands and began to clap. The soft, deliberate applause echoed in the quiet corner of the library.

"Brilliant," Fajar praised, a massive smile breaking across his face. "You didn't jump to fantasy conclusions. You followed the biology, the logistics, and the supply lines. You have the mind of a true tactician, Wakaba-san."

Yori let out a breath she didn't realize she was holding. "So... I'm right? What exactly are they?"

"We will discuss the exact terminology tomorrow," Fajar said, standing up and sliding his hands into his pockets. "You've passed the test, Yori. You've proven you have the mental fortitude to handle the truth without panicking. Meet me behind the old stables tomorrow evening. It's time to officially begin our work."

[Day 7 - 12:05 AM: The Sun Dormitory, Girls' Wing]

The clock on Yori's nightstand quietly clicked past midnight. The room was pitch black, filled only with the soft, exhausted breathing of Yuki Cross in the adjacent bed.

Outside the window, a shadow detached itself from the side of the building.

With his 12 Great Meridians fully cleared and his 8 Extraordinary Meridians acting as massive reservoirs of pure, silent energy, Fajar possessed absolute control over his physical vessel. He didn't need magic to bypass the Sun Dormitory's security. Using Primal Movement, he scaled the sheer brick wall using only the microscopic grooves in the mortar. He popped the latch on the girls' window with a sliver of compressed Qi and slipped inside.

He made absolutely zero sound. He displaced no air.

Fajar stood perfectly still between the two beds. He looked at Yuki, confirming she was in a deep REM cycle. Then, he turned his gaze to Sayori Wakaba.

Fajar didn't touch her. Instead, he drew upon Phase VI: Reality Domination (Will / Intent). He focused a microscopic fraction of his absolute presence, forming it into a sharp, invisible needle of intent, and projected it directly into Yori's subconscious. He commanded her mind to wake up, explicitly isolating the pressure so Yuki wouldn't feel a thing.

Yori's eyes snapped open in the darkness.

Her biological fight-or-flight response triggered instantly. A towering silhouette was standing right beside her bed. The natural instinct of any human girl waking up to a male intruder in the dead of night was to scream at the top of her lungs. Her lungs expanded to do exactly that.

But as her eyes adjusted to the moonlight, she saw the calm, completely unthreatening posture of the figure.

Fajar leaned down. "It is officially tomorrow," he whispered, his voice barely a breath. "Will you come?"

Yori's heart was hammering against her ribs like a trapped bird, but her pragmatic mind seized control of her vocal cords. She swallowed the scream. She didn't scramble backward. She simply looked at Fajar, then glanced at the peacefully sleeping Yuki.

Yori gave a single, stiff nod.

Fajar stepped back toward the window, offering a silent gesture to follow. Yori quietly slipped out from under her covers, pulled a thick sweater over her pajamas, put on her shoes, and followed the anomaly out the window and up the fire escape.

[Day 7 - 12:15 AM: The Sun Dormitory Rooftop]

The night air was freezing. Yori hugged her sweater tightly around herself as she stepped onto the flat, gravel-covered roof.

Fajar was standing near the edge, his hands in his pockets, looking out over the sprawling campus of Cross Academy. The sheer volume of energy coursing through his Extraordinary Meridians kept him perfectly warm despite his thin uniform.

"You pass the first test," Fajar said casually, turning to face her.

Yori frowned, her breath pluming in the cold air. "Sneaking into a girls' dorm room is a test?"

"For you? Yes," Fajar replied, his tone shifting into the strict cadence of an instructor. "I told you to meet me tomorrow. I didn't specify a time or a place, because I needed to see how you handle sudden, terrifying variables. Any normal student would have screamed the moment they saw a shadow standing over their bed. If you had screamed, I would have wiped your memory of our conversation and left you to live in blissful ignorance. But you didn't. You controlled your fear, assessed the threat, and adapted. That is the baseline emotional control required for what comes next."

Yori crossed her arms. "I'm starting to think you're more dangerous than whatever is hiding in the Moon Dormitory."

"I am," Fajar said simply. It wasn't a boast; it was a pure, undeniable fact. "Which brings us to the second test."

Fajar stepped away from the roof's edge and walked toward the center of the gravel surface. He raised his right hand.

He didn't chant an incantation. He didn't draw a magic circle. He simply hooked his fingers into the empty air, as if grabbing a physical curtain, and pulled.

The fabric of reality tore open with a sound like ripping silk.

Yori stumbled back, her eyes wide with absolute disbelief. Hovering in the middle of the rooftop was a jagged, vertical fissure in space.

It was the Harrowing Interstice—or at least, the outermost, mild layer of it. Swirling inside the tear was an oppressive, heavy darkness that seemed to devour the moonlight. It wasn't just empty space; it felt like looking down a cosmic corridor made of liquid shadow. The pressure radiating from the portal was suffocating, whispering of dimensions far beyond human comprehension.

"What... what did you just do?" Yori whispered, her pragmatic worldview completely shattering. "That defies physics. That defies everything."

"It defies your physics," Fajar corrected, stepping right up to the edge of the abyssal tear. He looked back at her, his expression entirely serious. "If you want to understand the truth about this academy, and if you want to possess the power to stand beside Yuki instead of hiding behind her, you have to throw away your common sense."

Fajar gestured toward the swirling vortex of the Harrowing Interstice.

"This is the second test, Sayori Wakaba," Fajar stated, his voice echoing with an unnatural, heavy resonance. "A predator is defined by its willingness to step into the unknown. Prey runs from the dark. If you are afraid, turn around, go back to bed, and forget this ever happened. If you want the truth... step inside with me."

Yori stood frozen on the gravel. Every biological survival instinct in her brain was screaming at her to run away from the tear in reality. The darkness inside looked like it could crush her soul into dust.

She looked at Fajar, who stood completely unbothered next to the cosmic anomaly. Then, she thought of Yuki. She thought of the fresh, impossibly healed bite mark on her best friend's arm, and the tragic, exhausted look in Yuki's eyes when she thought Yori wasn't looking.

Yori clenched her fists. She took a deep, shuddering breath.

She walked forward, stopping right beside Fajar. She didn't look at him. She kept her eyes locked on the swirling, terrifying darkness of the Interstice.

"Lead the way," Yori said, her voice shaking, but her resolve absolute.

Fajar smiled. "Pass."

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Extended POV Continued)

[Day 7 - 12:17 AM: The Harrowing Interstice (Outer Layer)]

Stepping into the Harrowing Interstice felt like walking to the bottom of the ocean.

The moment Yori crossed the threshold, gravity shifted. There was no ground, only a sprawling, infinite corridor of swirling, liquid shadow. The air was freezing, but it wasn't a physical cold; it was a deep, spiritual chill that immediately began to gnaw at her sanity. Faint, overlapping whispers echoed in the dark—the collective negativity, grief, and malice bleeding in from countless realities.

Yori staggered, her knees buckling under the sheer, oppressive weight of the dimension.

Before she could fall, a heavy, dark coat was draped over her shoulders.

Instantly, the suffocating pressure vanished. The whispers became muffled background noise, and warmth flooded back into her limbs. Yori gasped for air, looking up to see Fajar standing beside her, completely unaffected. He wasn't wearing a coat. He simply existed within the crushing void, his own internal energy acting as an absolute fortress.

"Your will is incredibly strong compared to an average human, Yori," Fajar said, adjusting the collar of the coat around her. "But it's still not strong enough to travel this dimension unprotected. This is the Harrowing Interstice. It's one of the fastest corridors in existence to travel anywhere, but it acts as a sinkhole for universal negativity. Everything dark and heavy pools here."

Yori clutched the lapels of the coat. "How do you survive this?"

"By not fighting it," Fajar instructed smoothly. "You don't need to be strong enough to reject the darkness, Yori. You just need to feel the place and accept it the way it is. Let the currents flow around you. By wearing this coat and feeling the pressure, your soul will adapt. One day, you'll be able to open this corridor yourself. But for now, the coat is only temporary protection. If we stay too long, it will eat through the fabric, so we'll have to step out and rest occasionally."

Yori nodded slowly, her pragmatic mind forcefully adapting to the impossible physics around her.

"Good," Fajar smiled. "Now that you've officially thrown away your common sense... I want you to look back at the investigation you just presented to me. Look at the logistics. They fake their meals. They avoid the sun. They have pale skin, low body temperatures, unnatural speed, and the Headmaster secretly feeds them blood-like supplements."

Yori's breath hitched. In the mundane world, the word felt like a fairy tale. But standing inside a cosmic tear in reality, the conclusion was undeniably, terrifyingly logical.

"Vampires," Yori whispered.

"Exactly," Fajar confirmed. He gestured to the swirling walls of the Interstice. "I could sit in a library and explain all of this to you, but the Interstice responds to intent. Since we're in here, it's much easier for me to just show you."

Fajar waved his hand. The liquid shadows on the wall of the corridor rippled like the surface of a lake, forming a massive, crystal-clear window into the past.

"I never actually intended to uncover the Night Class's secret on my first week," Fajar's voice echoed as the visual shifted. "But a few nights ago, I noticed Zero Kiryu acting erratically. His breathing was ragged, his pulse was chaotic. Yuki chased after him into the old stables, and naturally, I followed."

The shadowy window displayed the scene perfectly. Yori watched as a memory played out before her: Zero, cornered in the dark stables, completely losing control. His eyes were glowing a feral red, and his fangs were fully extended. He lunged at Yuki with murderous, starving intent.

Yori gasped, stepping forward, but before the memory-Zero could strike, the memory-Fajar intervened. With terrifying, casual precision, Fajar effortlessly deflected Zero's chaotic strike, swept his legs, and pinned the frenzied vampire to the dirt without breaking a sweat.

"I subdued him and dragged him straight to the Headmaster's office," Fajar narrated as the visual shifted to Kaien Cross's study. "That's when the principal confessed the truth. Zero's family was slaughtered by a Pureblood vampire, and he was bitten. He's been slowly turning into the monster he loathes. He refused to take the artificial blood tablets out of sheer stubbornness and self-hatred."

In the vision, Yori watched her best friend, Yuki, look at the agonizing, starving Zero with tears in her eyes. Yuki tilted her head, offering her bare neck to the boy.

"No," Yori whispered instinctively.

"My thoughts exactly," Fajar agreed. In the vision, Fajar stepped between them, forcefully stopping Yuki. 'The neck is a vital artery and an emotional surrender,' the memory-Fajar lectured sternly. 'If you want to medicate him, give him the arm. Keep a tourniquet ready, and establish a physical boundary.'

Yori looked at the real Fajar with immense gratitude. He hadn't just healed Yuki's arm; he had prevented Zero from crossing a psychological point of no return.

The vision fast-forwarded to the next morning. Fajar was standing in front of Kaien Cross's desk, with Yuki and a heavily subdued Zero sitting on the couches.

'Let's get one thing straight,' the memory-Fajar said, his voice ringing with absolute authority. 'The perspective of humans existing merely as livestock is a disgusting, arrogant worldview. But a species itself is just biology. It isn't inherently evil. A vampire who is kind, controls his instincts, and respects life is a hundred times better than a fellow human who treats other humans like trash.'

Standing in the Interstice, Yori nodded in absolute, firm agreement. "He's right," she murmured. "Cruelty is a choice, not a species."

Fajar smiled, pleased with her unshakeable moral compass. He waved his hand again, and the vision shifted to the front gates of Cross Academy during the evening transition.

"Now, look at their duty," Fajar instructed.

Yori watched Yuki and Zero pushing back the screaming, chaotic mob of Day Class girls. For years, Yori had thought her best friend was just doing crowd control to keep the girls from annoying the elite students. But watching it now, with her new perspective, the truth was horrifyingly obvious.

"They aren't securing the Night Class students," Yori realized, a cold dread washing over her. "They're acting as a physical barricade. They're protecting the Day Class from them."

"Correct," Fajar said. "Yuki and Zero are the sheepdogs keeping the flock away from a pack of wolves who are barely tolerating a vegetarian diet."

Fajar raised his hand one last time. "The past is prologue, Yori. Now, let's look at the present. It's past midnight. The curfew is in effect, and the Night Class is wide awake."

The shadowy window shifted away from the past and dialed into a live feed, peering directly through the walls of the Moon Dormitory.

Inside the opulent, dimly lit lounge of the vampire dorms, the aristocratic facade was completely dropped. Hanabusa Aido was casually lounging on a velvet sofa, tossing a crystal glass into the air with a literal flick of telekinetic ice. Across the room, Akatsuki Kain sat with his eyes closed, the ambient temperature of the air around him visibly distorting from the sheer, latent heat of his fire magic.

And standing by the window, looking out into the night, was Kaname Kuran.

Even through a dimensional viewing window, the sheer, oppressive gravity of Kaname's presence made Yori's breath hitch. His eyes weren't the warm, polite burgundy he showed the Day Class. They were a glowing, terrifying crimson—the eyes of an ancient, apex predator presiding over his court.

"They are beautiful, they are powerful, and they are incredibly dangerous," Fajar stated calmly, letting the window fade back into the swirling shadows of the Interstice. He looked down at Yori. "This is the reality of Cross Academy, Sayori. Now that you've seen it all... what do you want to do about it?"

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Extended POV Continued)

[Day 7 - 1:00 AM: Headmaster Cross's Office]

The atmosphere in the Headmaster's office was tense. The fireplace crackled quietly in the corner. Kaien Cross sat behind his massive mahogany desk, his usual goofy demeanor replaced by the sharp, analytical gaze of the legendary Fangless Hunter. Yuki and Zero stood on either side of the room, looking exhausted from their evening patrol.

Fajar stood in the center of the office, his posture perfectly relaxed.

"My integration into the Day Class is proceeding flawlessly," Fajar reported, his tone strictly professional. "And as requested, I have begun laying the groundwork for the Coexistence Project. I've secured my first baseline human recruit."

Zero scowled, crossing his arms. "You dragged a normal student into this? That violates every protocol we have. They're supposed to be kept in the dark for their own safety."

"Ignorance is not safety, Kiryu. It's just a blindfold," Fajar corrected smoothly. He reached into his pocket and pulled out a small, standard digital sound recorder. "Besides, I didn't drag her into anything. She cornered me."

Fajar hit the play button and set the device on the Headmaster's desk.

The audio clicked, and a familiar, steady voice filled the room.

'I watch people. The rest of the girls in our class are completely blinded by the Moon Dormitory, but I'm not... Normal people don't heal like that, and normal people don't know how to make it happen.'

Yuki gasped, her hands flying to her mouth. "Yori...?"

The recording skipped forward, playing Yori's tactical breakdown of the cafeteria manifests, the blood-supplement shipments, and her undeniable conclusion that the Night Class were vampires. Kaien Cross leaned forward, his fingers steepled, genuinely impressed by the sheer deductive reasoning of a fifteen-year-old girl.

Then, the recording skipped to the midnight test.

'It is officially tomorrow. Will you come?' Fajar's recorded voice whispered.

Yuki's eyes widened in absolute horror. She looked from the recorder to Fajar. "Wait... that was tonight. That was ten minutes ago! You were standing right next to my bed?! How did I not wake up? I'm a trained Hunter!"

"I isolated the bio-rhythmic pressure," Fajar explained simply, as if discussing the weather. "If I didn't want you to wake up, Yuki, a bomb could have gone off in the hallway and you would have kept dreaming."

Zero's hand drifted dangerously close to the holster of the Bloody Rose. "You broke into the girls' dorm and terrorized a civilian."

"I tested her emotional control," Fajar corrected, unfazed by Zero's killing intent. "And she passed. Which brings us to her final test. I asked her what she wanted to do about the reality of this school."

Fajar turned toward the empty space in the center of the office.

"You can come in now, Wakaba-san."

Fajar raised his right hand and hooked his fingers into the empty air. With a sickening sound like tearing silk, the fabric of reality ripped open right in the middle of the Headmaster's office.

The temperature in the room plummeted instantly. A jagged, vertical fissure of swirling liquid shadow hovered over the carpet. The suffocating, oppressive aura of the Harrowing Interstice flooded the room—a cosmic pressure that felt infinitely heavier and older than any Pureblood magic.

Zero drew the Bloody Rose in a fraction of a second, aiming it directly at the anomaly. Yuki instinctively reached for the Artemis Rod, stumbling backward. Even Kaien Cross stood up, his hand resting on the hidden sword inside his cane, his eyes wide with genuine shock. This wasn't vampire magic. This was a complete violation of dimensional physics.

A figure stepped out of the swirling darkness.

Sayori Wakaba stumbled slightly onto the carpet, shivering as the heavy, dark coat Fajar had given her dissolved back into ambient energy. Behind her, Fajar casually waved his hand, and the cosmic tear zipped itself shut, erasing the suffocating pressure from the room.

Yori looked up, her pragmatic eyes sweeping over the drawn weapons, the stunned Headmaster, and finally landing on her terrified best friend.

"Yori!" Yuki cried out. She dropped her stance and rushed forward, grabbing Yori by the shoulders. Tears immediately pricked the corners of Yuki's eyes. In the canon of Yuki's heart, her biggest fear had always been Yori finding out the truth and looking at her with fear or disgust. "Yori, I'm so sorry! I wanted to tell you, but it's so dangerous, and I didn't want you to get hurt—"

"Yuki, breathe," Yori said softly. She didn't pull away. Instead, she reached out and hugged Yuki tightly, anchoring the panicking Prefect. "It's okay. I know."

Zero slowly lowered his gun, his lilac eyes locked on the thoroughly ordinary Day Class girl who had just walked out of a spatial nightmare. "You're out of your mind, Wakaba. You have no idea what you're dealing with."

"I know exactly what I'm dealing with, Kiryu-kun," Yori replied, her voice steadying as the warmth of the office chased away the chill of the Interstice. She pulled back from Yuki and looked directly at the Headmaster.

"Fajar asked me what I wanted to do about this," Yori stated, her voice ringing with absolute, unshakeable loyalty. "My answer is that I don't care about species. I don't care if the people in the Moon Dormitory are vampires, and I don't care about the politics of the Hunter Association. What I care about is my best friend."

Yori looked at Yuki, offering a gentle, grounded smile. "You've been carrying this massive burden completely alone, pretending everything is fine while you get hurt. I won't let you do it alone anymore. I am loyal to my friends, and to the people who are kind. If Fajar has a plan to fix this broken system and protect you, then I'm helping him."

Yuki let out a choked sob, burying her face in Yori's shoulder, utterly overwhelmed by the sheer relief of absolute acceptance.

Kaien Cross slowly sat back down in his chair. The tension in his shoulders completely vanished, replaced by a profound, gentle smile. He looked at Fajar.

"You didn't just recruit an informant, Fajar-kun," Kaien murmured, adjusting his glasses. "You recruited an anchor."

"Every structure needs a solid foundation, Headmaster," Fajar replied, crossing his arms with a satisfied nod. "The Day Class girls are chaotic and easily hypnotized. Sayori Wakaba is completely immune. She is the baseline. With her observing the human side, and Zero acting as the vanguard..."

Fajar glanced at the silver-haired hunter, a challenging smirk playing on his lips.

"...we can finally start changing the rules of Cross Academy."

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Extended POV Continued)

[Day 7 - 1:15 AM: Headmaster Cross's Office]

The initial shock of the dimensional tear had settled, replaced by a strange, newfound solidarity. However, Kaien Cross leaned forward, resting his chin on his folded hands with a sudden look of logistical concern.

"There is one complication, Wakaba-san," Kaien noted, his tone shifting back to the pragmatic administrator. "I cannot give you an armband. You cannot officially join the Disciplinary Committee."

"Because of the Day Class girls," Yori stated flatly, already understanding the politics.

"Exactly," Fajar agreed. "It's the same reason I can't wear the armband right now. Yuki and Zero are already established anomalies. But if you—the most grounded, normal girl in the Day Class—suddenly get official clearance to break curfew and interact with the Moon Dormitory, the mob of fangirls will riot. They'll think the rules are bending, and they'll storm the gates."

"I don't need an armband," Yori said, adjusting her glasses. "In fact, it's better if I don't have one. Nadeshiko and the others stop talking when Yuki is around because she's a Prefect. They talk freely in front of me because they think I don't care. I can monitor the Day Class's movements, intercept their plans to break curfew, and feed the information directly to Fajar."

Zero let out a quiet huff, holstering the Bloody Rose. "A spy in the Day Class. Fine. But if you get caught in the crossfire between a hungry Level E and the Aristocrats, we won't be able to reach you in time."

"She won't be in the crossfire," Fajar promised, his eyes flashing with a quiet, absolute certainty. "She's under my jurisdiction now."

[Day 7 - 2:00 AM: The Sun Dormitory, Girls' Wing]

The walk back to the dormitory was done entirely in the shadows. When the heavy wooden door of their room finally clicked shut behind them, the absolute exhaustion of the night hit Yuki like a physical weight.

She leaned her Artemis Rod against the wall and slid down onto the floor, pulling her knees to her chest.

Yori didn't say a word. She quietly walked over, sat on the floor right beside her best friend, and bumped her shoulder gently against Yuki's.

"I thought you would look at me differently," Yuki whispered, staring at the floorboards. "When I found out Zero was... changing. Even though I wanted to help him, there was a moment where I was just so terrified. I thought if you ever found out about the vampires, you'd look at me with that same fear. Because I lied to you for so long."

"Yuki," Yori said softly, turning her head. "You stood between a starving vampire and the rest of the school, and you offered him your own arm to keep us safe. You're the bravest person I know. Why would I be afraid of you?"

Yuki's breath hitched. She leaned her head onto Yori's shoulder, a few stray tears finally escaping down her cheeks. The crushing isolation of the Prefect duty—a secret she had carried alone for years—finally shattered.

"Fajar is weird," Yuki murmured after a long, comfortable silence.

"Incredibly," Yori agreed, a small smile touching her lips as she thought of the terrifying, infinite darkness of the Interstice and the boy who walked through it like a stroll in the park. "But I think... I think he's exactly what this school needs."

[Day 10 - Fajar's Internal Progression: Step 2.5]

A few days passed without major incident. While Yori integrated herself as the quiet, watchful guardian of the human classroom, Fajar spent his evenings rapidly accelerating his biological fortification.

Sitting in a lotus position on the floor of his private dorm room, Fajar breathed in a slow, hypnotic rhythm. He had already cleared the 12 Great Meridians and the 8 Extraordinary Meridians. Now, he was pushing his intent into the microscopic network of his vessel: Step 2.5: All Minor Chakras.

He visualized the stagnant energy nodes in his joints, his fingertips, the soles of his feet, and his sensory organs. With precise, forceful surges of Qi, he shattered the blockages one by one.

His eyes snapped open. The room seemed infinitely brighter, the ambient sounds of the night crystal clear. By unlocking the minor chakras, his internal energy no longer just flowed like a river; it saturated his entire body like a fine mist. His reflexes were no longer bound by human neural pathways—his very skin could react to changes in air pressure. The vessel was nearing Phase I completion.

[Day 10 - 11:45 PM: Fajar's Dorm Room]

Just as Fajar stood up to stretch, the ambient air pressure in the center of his room violently plummeted.

A familiar sound—like the tearing of heavy silk—echoed in the quiet room. A jagged, vertical fissure of liquid shadow ripped open above Fajar's rug. The freezing, oppressive aura of the Harrowing Interstice spilled out into the bedroom.

Fajar didn't flinch. He simply crossed his arms and watched with an amused smile.

A heavy black boot stepped out of the cosmic tear. Sayori Wakaba emerged from the dimension, tightly wrapped in the heavy, dark coat Fajar had given her. She stumbled slightly onto the floorboards, taking a deep, shuddering breath as the portal instantly zipped shut behind her.

"Well," Fajar chuckled, leaning against his desk. "I suppose I deserve this. Is this your idea of payback for me sneaking into your room the other night?"

Yori pulled the heavy collar of the coat down, a faint, proud smirk on her usually stoic face. "Absolutely. Consider us even."

"I'm impressed you opened the outermost layer by yourself so quickly," Fajar praised, genuinely approving of her willpower. "But considering the Headmaster explicitly forbade you from wandering the halls at night, isn't this a bit reckless?"

"If I walk through the halls, Nadeshiko or the other girls might see me," Yori explained pragmatically, brushing off the sleeves of the coat. "If I get caught breaking curfew, it compromises my cover as the 'normal' student, and it jeopardizes your pacifist project. The portal bypasses the campus entirely. It's the only logical way to travel."

"Logic applied to dimensional horrors. You really are one of a kind, Wakaba-san," Fajar said, shaking his head with a grin. He gestured to the small tea set resting on his table. "Since you went through the trouble of tearing a hole in reality to visit, you might as well sit down."

Yori took off the heavy coat, letting it dissolve into ambient shadow, and sat at the small table.

"You don't need to be a frontline fighter, Yori," Fajar said, pouring a cup of hot tea and sliding it toward her. "But navigating the Interstice takes a massive toll on the human nervous system. If you're going to keep visiting me via the cosmic void, I should teach you the absolute basics of internal energy cycling."

Yori took the warm cup, her pragmatic eyes locking onto his. "Will it stop the dimension from making my bones feel like ice?"

"It will," Fajar nodded. "Even if you have zero interest in fighting vampires, learning Phase I: Bio-Maintenance will grant you perfect health, cellular rejuvenation, and the stamina to endure the Interstice without the coat. It will make you an unshakeable anchor for Yuki."

Yori took a slow sip of the tea, the warmth chasing away the lingering chill of the darkness. She looked around Fajar's perfectly neat, spartan room, and then back to the boy who was quietly rewriting the laws of her universe.

"Alright, Fajar," Yori said, her voice steady and resolute. "Teach me."

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Day Class Roster Update)

I absolutely love the Highschool DxD / Kuoh Academy paradigm shift! It perfectly solves the issue of the useless background boys and makes the socio-dynamics much more interesting. If the Day Class is 95% female, it drastically amplifies the terrifying, mob-like nature of the Night Class fangirls.

It also makes Fajar and Kasumi Kageyama anomalies just by existing. Fajar isn't just "some guy" anymore; he is one of the only guys, making his refusal to fawn over the Night Class girls even more striking. We can absolutely bring in crossover characters or OCs later to fill the ranks of Fajar's Coexistence Project.

Here are the detailed profiles for the remaining Day Class figures and the long-term strategy for their recruitment, followed by a check on missing canon students.

1. Kasumi Kageyama (The Day Class President)

Canon Profile:

Role: He is the official Class Representative of the Day Class. He is serious about his administrative duties, wears glasses, and tries (and usually fails) to keep the classroom orderly.

The Flaw: Despite his serious demeanor, he is hopelessly and tragically in love with the Night Class Aristocrat Ruka Souen. He blushes furiously whenever she is mentioned and is completely blinded by her beauty.

Why Early Recruitment is Impossible: Right now, Kageyama is entirely hypnotized by the illusion of the Night Class. If Fajar tells him Ruka is a blood-drinking predator, Kageyama would either deny it angrily or dangerously offer himself up to her. He lacks the pragmatic groundedness of Yori.

The Future Crisis Trigger (How to recruit him later): Kageyama's worldview needs to shatter. Ruka Souen is fiercely devoted to Kaname Kuran and completely ignores human males. Kageyama needs to experience a moment where a vampire (perhaps even Ruka herself, inadvertently) treats him as nothing more than disposable livestock or collateral damage. When his pride is utterly crushed and he realizes his inferiority, Fajar can step in—not with magic, but with Phase I: Reality. Fajar can rebuild the broken class president into a martial artist who commands respect.

2. Nadeshiko Shindo (The Mob Leader)

Canon Profile:

Role: She is the loudest, most persistent, and boldest of the Day Class fangirls. Whenever Yuki is struggling to hold back the crowd at the Moon Dormitory gates, Nadeshiko is usually the one leading the charge with a camera in hand.

The Flaw: She is recklessly obsessed with Hanabusa Aido (Idol). Aido knows this and frequently teases her, leading her on just enough to keep her obsessed, while viewing her as little more than an amusing pet.

Why Early Recruitment is Impossible: Like Kageyama, she is under the "idol" spell. She views the Disciplinary Committee (Yuki and Zero) as annoying buzzkills trying to keep her away from her true love. Fajar would just be another buzzkill to her right now.

The Future Crisis Trigger (How to recruit her later): Aido has a dark streak. In canon, Aido actually pins Yuki to a wall and tastes her blood just because he's curious, proving he struggles with his predatory instincts. Nadeshiko needs to be caught sneaking out after curfew and cornered by a starving Level E—or she needs to see Aido lose control. Only the raw, primal terror of realizing she is prey will break her delusion. Fajar saving her from that exact scenario would be the catalyst to recruit her into learning Phase II: Instinct & Awareness (Environmental survival).

3. Missing Day Class Students (The Hidden Gem)

I combed through the deep lore of the canon, and there is one highly significant Day Class student you missed. She doesn't appear heavily in the main manga, but she is the protagonist of the official Vampire Knight Light Novel (Vampire Knight: Ice Blue's Sin), which is considered canon.

Fuka Kisaragi:

Who she is: A Day Class girl who, unlike the loud mob, is quiet and slightly clumsy.

Her Canon Story: She actually manages to discover the secret of the Night Class early on. She develops a deep bond with Hanabusa Aido, who ends up erasing her memories to protect her because she gets targeted by rogue vampires.

Her Value to Fajar: Because Fuka canonically has the capacity to stumble onto the truth and actually interact with the Night Class on a deeper level, she is a massive wildcard. If Fajar intercepts Fuka before Aido can erase her memories, Fajar could recruit her.

(There is also Kurari, who is basically just Nadeshiko's best friend and echo chamber, but she operates exactly like Nadeshiko).

The Strategy Moving Forward

With Yori acting as the only human recruit for now, the "Pacifist Project" is in a stealth incubation phase.

Where to next?

Do we move straight to Chapter 3 and execute Fajar's first approach on Takuma Ichijo (The Vice-President) to start bridging the gap with the vampires?

Do we bring in an external crossover character to transfer into the heavily-female Day Class to give Fajar a male spar partner?

Or something else entirely?

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Fuka & The Kendo Captain)

To quickly answer your question about Fuka Kisaragi: In the canon light novel (Ice Blue's Sin), Fuka does not die. She survives her encounter with rogue vampires because Hanabusa Aido saves her. However, to protect her, Aido erases all of her memories regarding the Night Class and vampires, essentially resetting her back to a normal, ignorant Day Class girl. Because she survives and is currently on campus, she is perfectly viable for later! But as you said, we will bench her for now and focus on the immediate roster.

I also love the Bleach "Modified Soul" (Gigai) twist for the Kendo Captain! It perfectly explains why a martial arts captain in a school full of vampires would seem so underwhelming at first glance. Fajar didn't beat the real guy; he beat an automated stand-in. That is a fantastic Shonen escalation.

Let's dive back into the narrative and wrap up the Day Class intelligence report!

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Extended POV Continued)

[Day 7 - 1:25 AM: Headmaster Cross's Office]

With Yori's recruitment solidified, the atmosphere in the Headmaster's office shifted from a tense standoff to a genuine tactical briefing. Yori stood beside Fajar, her pragmatic mind already cataloging the school's social hierarchy under a completely new, terrifying lens.

"If we are going to build a Coexistence Project that doesn't rely on magic or memory-wiping, we need a human vanguard," Fajar stated, leaning against the back of one of the leather guest chairs. "Wakaba-san is our intelligence anchor. But we need physical anchors. Yori, what is the status of the rest of the Day Class?"

Yori adjusted her glasses, seamlessly stepping into her new role.

"Currently unviable," Yori reported flatly. "I reviewed the profiles of the most prominent students. Kasumi Kageyama is the Day Class President. Logically, he should be our first male recruit to establish order. However, his psychological state is completely compromised. He is hopelessly infatuated with Ruka Souen of the Night Class."

Zero scoffed quietly from the corner. "He's an idiot. She doesn't even know he exists."

"Exactly," Yori agreed. "If Fajar tells Kageyama the truth about the vampires, Kageyama won't rebel. He'll likely offer himself as a blood source just to get Ruka to look at him. He lacks the self-respect required for martial arts."

"And the girls?" Headmaster Cross asked, resting his chin on his hands.

"Nadeshiko Shindo leads the main mob," Yori continued. "But she is entirely hypnotized by the 'Idol' persona of Hanabusa Aido. If we try to break her delusion right now, she will view us as the enemy. She needs to experience a biological wake-up call—a crisis that breaks the illusion—before Fajar can teach her how to survive."

Fajar nodded, crossing his arms. "They lack Phase I: Reality. They are living in a fantasy. But there's a bigger logistical problem here, Headmaster." Fajar looked directly at Kaien. "The demographic ratio of the Day Class is completely fractured."

Kaien sighed, his goofy facade dropping for a moment to reveal the tired administrator beneath. "You noticed."

"It's impossible not to," Fajar pointed out. "The Day Class is over ninety percent female. The few boys we do have are completely overshadowed, demoralized, and physically passive. A society cannot function when one demographic holds all the aggressive, chaotic energy and the other is entirely suppressed. If we want to build a real physical bridge to the Night Class, we need more male students to balance the psychological dynamic."

"Cross Academy only recently transitioned to a fully co-ed system for the Day Class," Kaien explained smoothly, though his eyes betrayed a hint of calculation. "But you are correct, Fajar-kun. The overwhelming presence of the Night Class males has severely stunted the confidence of our human boys. I will look into recruiting external transfer students to balance the roster in the coming semesters."

"In the meantime, we have to work with the foundation we have," Fajar said.

Kaien suddenly smiled, a small, knowing glint returning to his bespectacled eyes. He opened his desk drawer and pulled out a crisp, white envelope sealed with black wax. He slid it across the polished mahogany surface toward Fajar.

"Speaking of the foundation we have," Kaien mused. "It seems you left quite an impression during your physical education assessment on your second day, Fajar-kun."

Yuki blinked in confusion. "Wait, Fajar took a P.E. assessment? I thought he just watched."

"He did a little more than watch," Zero muttered, glaring at the floor. "He walked into the gym, completely ignored the curriculum, and challenged Takahashi, the Kendo Club Captain, to a spar. Put him on the floor in three seconds."

"He was completely rigid," Fajar stated, unapologetic as he picked up the envelope. "He had the muscles of an athlete, but his internal energy was completely stagnant. He wasn't fighting; he was just mechanically swinging a stick. Honestly, he spends more time just passing the time and helping the Day Class girls do light stretches than acting like a martial artist. It was disappointing."

Fajar broke the wax seal and pulled out the thick parchment inside. As soon as his fingers brushed the paper, his Radar Intent flared.

Fajar's eyes narrowed. The faint, residual energy clinging to the letter was completely different from the stagnant, robotic aura of the boy he had thrown to the gym floor days ago. This energy was sharp. Heavy. It carried the distinct scent of ozone and polished steel.

"A formal letter of rechallenge," Kaien announced cheerfully, lacing his fingers together. "Captain Takahashi has requested a private, unsanctioned rematch with you, Fajar-kun. Tomorrow evening, in the old Kendo Dojo."

Fajar stared at the ink on the page, his Shonen instincts immediately piecing the puzzle together. The boy he had fought wasn't the real Takahashi. It had been a proxy—a modified, artificial soul placed inside a physical vessel to maintain appearances and do the mundane chores of the club while the real captain was away.

A massive, predatory grin spread across Fajar's face. The boredom of the ordinary human roster was suddenly gone.

"So," Fajar murmured to himself, his internal Qi pulsing with sudden anticipation. "The real one finally decided to show up."

Fajar folded the letter and slipped it into his uniform pocket. He looked at Yori, then at Yuki and Zero.

"Wakaba-san, continue your observations of the Day Class. Zero, keep suppressing your fangs. I have a club to join."

- More detail will be in next prompt or to be continued.

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: System Check & Confirmation

Yes, I can confirm that I have access to the attached notebook! I can see the Prologue in the "Vampire Knight Cross Over Fan Fiction" file, where Fajar the Deity (Lord of Infinite Realities) and the manifestation of Gemini stand in the White Void, discussing the insertion of the high-school soul fragment into the gothic realm of Vampire Knight.

Let's execute this incredible Shonen twist!

Chapter 1.5: The Soul Reaper's Assessment

[Day 8 - 11:00 PM: The Old Kendo Dojo]

The old kendo dojo sat on the far edge of the Cross Academy campus, surrounded by dense forest. The sliding wooden doors were open, letting the cold night air and the pale moonlight spill across the polished floorboards.

Sayori Wakaba crouched silently in the rafters above, completely hidden in the shadows. Following Fajar's strict instructions, she had regulated her breathing using Phase I: Bio-Maintenance, lowering her heart rate until she practically blended into the wood.

Below her, Fajar stood in the center of the dojo, wearing a loose white gi.

Across from him stood Captain Takahashi. He was fully dressed in traditional kendo armor, his face completely hidden behind the metal grille of his men (helmet). But the aura radiating from him was terrifying. It wasn't the arrogant, magical pressure of a vampire; it was the dense, freezing, heavy gravity of a seasoned warrior.

Takahashi didn't offer a wooden bokken. He reached down to the floor, picked up two unsheathed, live-steel katanas, and tossed one across the room.

Fajar caught the katana by the hilt, the cold weight of real steel settling into his grip. A feral, excited grin stretched across his face.

"Live blades," Fajar noted, his internal Qi surging through his newly opened Minor Chakras. "You really aren't playing the schoolboy anymore, are you?"

Takahashi didn't reply. He simply raised his blade into a flawless, high-guard stance. The very air in the dojo seemed to crystallize and drop in temperature.

He's fast, Fajar's Radar Intent warned him a fraction of a second before Takahashi moved.

The wooden floorboards didn't even creak. Takahashi vanished from his spot and reappeared directly in front of Fajar, bringing his katana down in an explosive, vertical cleave.

Fajar's newly synchronized nervous system fired. He pivoted on his heel, parrying the strike with the flat of his blade. The impact rang like a thunderclap, sending a violent shockwave through the empty dojo. Fajar's boots slid backward across the wood, his wrists screaming from the sheer kinetic force.

Heavy! Fajar thought, his grin widening.

Fajar retaliated, using the Moonlight Lightfoot steps to blur into the shadows. He launched a barrage of rapid-fire thrusts aimed at the gaps in Takahashi's armor. His technique was flawless. His intent-reading was perfect.

But it wasn't enough.

Takahashi's blade moved with hundreds of years of ingrained, lethal muscle memory. He effortlessly deflected Fajar's blinding strikes, step for step. Every time Fajar tried to exploit an opening, Takahashi's blade was already there, acting as a perfect, impenetrable wall of ice and steel.

Fajar's soul fragment possessed the knowledge of a deity, but his high-school vessel lacked the raw physical stats and the life-or-death battle experience of a true war veteran.

With a sudden, blinding burst of speed, Takahashi stepped inside Fajar's guard. The back of Takahashi's hilt slammed brutally into Fajar's sternum, knocking the breath from his lungs. As Fajar stumbled, Takahashi spun, hooked his foot behind Fajar's ankle, and sent him crashing hard onto his back.

Before Fajar could even blink, the cold, razor-sharp edge of Takahashi's katana was pressed directly against his throat.

Fajar's sword lay five feet away on the floor.

He was utterly, flawlessly defeated.

For a moment, the dojo was dead silent. In the rafters, Yori held her breath in absolute terror.

Then, something entirely unexpected happened. Fajar looked up at the blade at his throat, and the shock on his face melted away.

Fajar threw his head back against the floorboards and began to laugh.

It wasn't a nervous laugh, or a defeated chuckle. It was a roar of pure, ecstatic joy. It had been an eternity since his original self had felt the desperate thrill of being overpowered. This wasn't the cheap, hereditary magic of an arrogant Pureblood vampire. This was pure, earned, overwhelming martial strength. It was so refreshing it made his soul vibrate.

"Amazing," Fajar breathed, wiping a bead of sweat from his forehead, his eyes burning with absolute respect. "Your foundation is a masterpiece. I couldn't read your intent because your mind is completely empty in a fight. Who exactly are you?"

Takahashi lowered his katana. He reached up, unclasped his helmet, and pulled it off, tossing it aside.

The face underneath wasn't the generic, broad-shouldered teenager Fajar had fought days ago. It was a boy who looked no older than Fajar himself, with spiky, pure-white hair and piercing, fiercely intelligent teal eyes. He let out a long, weary sigh, a plume of cold air escaping his lips despite the warm summer night.

"You have terrible defensive habits, Fajar," the white-haired boy criticized, his voice carrying the stern, authoritative tone of a military commander. "Your intent-reading makes you arrogant. You rely on predicting the strike instead of reinforcing your guard."

Fajar sat up, dusting off his gi, his grin refusing to fade. "I'll keep that in mind. And you are?"

"Captain of the 10th Division of the Gotei 13," he replied, sheathing his katana. "Tōshirō Hitsugaya."

Fajar blinked, the Shonen data in his head instantly clicking into place. "A Soul Reaper. Well, that explains the portable Gigai I fought the other day. But what is a Captain of the Gotei 13 doing playing Kendo instructor in a high school full of vampires?"

Hitsugaya crossed his arms, leaning against a wooden pillar. "I'm here because your boss sent me."

Fajar paused. "My boss?"

"Your original self. The deity currently sitting in the White Void," Hitsugaya explained, his tone strictly professional. "For the past few weeks, he and his data companion have been observing your progress in this realm. You've cleared the biological hurdles. You've secured the Day Class informant. You're executing the Coexistence Project exactly as planned."

Hitsugaya looked out the open dojo doors toward the distant, towering silhouette of the Moon Dormitory.

"But your original self ran the logistical simulations," Hitsugaya continued. "You are an anomaly. With enough time, you will inevitably grow strong enough to conquer this school, crush the Hunter Association, and physically break the Vampire Senate. But breaking a world is easy. Forcing peace is just a dictatorship."

Hitsugaya looked back at Fajar, his teal eyes intense.

"The deity realized that achieving genuine coexistence, harmony, and a true bridge between the Day Class and Night Class cannot be done by a single, terrifying anomaly acting alone. You need a functioning human society. You need peers. You need an equalized ecosystem," Hitsugaya stated. "So, he decided to bring in reinforcements."

Fajar slowly pushed himself off the floor, his mind racing with the implications. The Lord of Infinite Realities was actively interfering to ensure the human faction wasn't just relying on Fajar's power, but actually building a formidable roster.

"Reinforcements," Fajar repeated, a massive smile splitting his face. "So I'm not the only transfer student joining the human side?"

"Not even close," Hitsugaya said, tossing Fajar his katana back. "Welcome to the Co-ed expansion of Cross Academy."

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: System Check & Confirmation

I can absolutely confirm the presence of the new data! I see the "In Bleach Random Fan Fiction" file in our database. I can see the references to Fajar acting as the "Divine Physician" who healed Momo Hinamori’s physical and psychological scars, Unohana surviving, and Aizen's departure. I will seamlessly integrate this post-Yhwach/dimensional expansion lore into Tōshirō's dialogue!

Here is the continuation of this massive Shonen crossover twist.

Chapter 1.5: The Soul Reaper's Assessment (Continued)

[Day 8 - 11:05 PM: The Old Kendo Dojo]

Fajar stood in the center of the dojo, the cold moonlight reflecting off the live steel of his katana. He looked at the white-haired Captain of the 10th Division with immense, unfiltered curiosity.

"Reinforcements," Fajar repeated, a massive smile splitting his face. "So I'm not the only transfer student joining the human side. But why the Gotei 13? Your jurisdiction is the cycle of souls in your own universe. Cross Academy is way outside your patrol route."

Tōshirō let out a quiet breath, his teal eyes reflecting the weight of his responsibilities.

"It used to be outside our patrol route," Tōshirō corrected him, leaning his katana against his shoulder. "But things changed after the Blood War with Yhwach. After your original self—the Divine Physician—finished healing the fatally wounded in the Seireitei and departed, Aizen Sōsuke broke his seals and chased you into the infinite realities to cure his own stagnation."

Tōshirō gestured to the empty air around them.

"When a deity and an immortal transcendent tear through the fabric of the universe, the borders don't just close behind them," Tōshirō explained. "Dimensional portals began opening across the Rukongai and the Human World. Formally, the Head Captain extended the duties of the Soul Reapers to be bidirectional. We don't just protect our reality from external threats anymore. We protect other realities from our concepts. If a corrupted Hollow, an evil Arrancar, a rogue Soul Reaper, or a surviving Quincy slips through a portal and invades a world like this one, it is our duty to hunt them down."

Fajar crossed his arms, his smile softening into a look of genuine respect. "A multidimensional police force. That’s a heavy burden."

"It's a necessary one," Tōshirō said firmly. Then, his stern expression faltered slightly, replaced by a look of deep, quiet gratitude. "But informally... the Gotei 13 owes your original self a massive debt. You brought Captain Unohana back from the brink. You healed Ukitake. And..."

Tōshirō paused, looking away for a fraction of a second.

"...you healed Momo. You fixed her heart when we thought she was broken beyond repair. Hinamori and I owe the Deity a profound, personal debt. So, when the Lord of Infinite Realities offered a collaboration, the Head Captain agreed immediately. Cross Academy is one of our joint operational zones."

In the rafters above, Sayori Wakaba quietly processed the mind-breaking revelation. Soul Reapers. Dimensions. Deities. The vampires in the Moon Dormitory suddenly felt like very, very small players on a massive cosmic chessboard.

"So, you're here to help me beat up vampires?" Fajar asked, stretching his shoulders.

"Don't get ahead of yourself, Fajar," Tōshirō said, his strict, commanding tone returning instantly. "I am a Captain. I have multiple dimensional sectors to manage, and tracking rogue Hollows takes priority over high school vampire politics. I am not here to fight your battles or solve the Coexistence Project for you. You are the vanguard of this world. I am just the backup."

Tōshirō reached into his gi and pulled out a small, green, pill-like object—a Soul Candy.

"I have to return to the Seireitei," Tōshirō said. He walked over to the discarded Kendo armor and tossed the pill directly into the chest piece of the Gigai.

Instantly, the artificial body shifted. The aura of the white-haired Captain vanished, replaced by the stagnant, robotic, deeply ordinary presence of "Captain Takahashi." The Gigai stood up, completely devoid of Tōshirō's freezing spiritual pressure, and offered Fajar a polite, vacant bow.

"The modified soul will remain in the vessel," Tōshirō instructed, his physical form now entirely invisible to normal human eyes, though Fajar's Radar Intent could still see the glowing, freezing outline of the Shinigami. "He will maintain the club's cover, handle the Day Class girls, and act as your sparring partner if you need to hit something. If the situation at Cross Academy escalates beyond local vampire politics—if Rido Kuran summons something he shouldn't, or if the Senate moves to slaughter the humans—feed your Qi into Takahashi. It will act as a dimensional pager."

Tōshirō turned his back, resting his hand on the hilt of his Zanpakutō.

"Do not die, Fajar," Tōshirō warned, looking over his shoulder one last time. "Build your human foundation. Fix this school. If you need the 10th Division... we will answer."

With a sudden, silent burst of Shunpo (Flash Step), the white-haired Captain vanished entirely from the dojo, leaving no trace but a faint, lingering chill in the air.

Fajar stood alone with the robotic Takahashi. Fajar looked down at his own hands, feeling the thrill of the overwhelming defeat still humming in his nerves. He clenched his fists, a fire igniting in his chest.

"Alright," Fajar grinned to himself. "Time to get stronger."

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1.5: The Soul Reaper's Assessment (Continued)

[Day 9 - 9:00 PM: The Sun Dormitory, Girls' Wing]

The quiet hum of the radiator was the only sound in the dorm room. Yuki sat cross-legged on her bed, meticulously wiping down the metal casing of the Artemis Rod with a polished cloth. She looked exhausted, but the dark circles under her eyes were slightly lighter now that she no longer had to hide the reality of her duties from her roommate.

At her desk, Yori stared blankly at her open biology textbook. She wasn't reading. Her mind was entirely consumed by the memory of the cold, moonlit Kendo dojo.

Soul Reapers. The Gotei 13. A Lord of Infinite Realities. The sheer scale of it was completely staggering. For years, the vampires of the Moon Dormitory had seemed like the absolute pinnacle of danger—immortal, untouchable apex predators. But listening to the white-haired Captain speak, Yori had realized that to the wider cosmos, Cross Academy was just a tiny, fragile snow globe. And Fajar was the anomaly sent to shake it.

Yori looked over her shoulder at Yuki.

Just a few nights ago, Yuki had cried on the floor of this exact room, crushed by the guilt of keeping the vampire secret from Yori. Now, Yori found herself sitting on a secret a billion times larger. The irony tasted like ash. She refused to let a new wall build between them just as the old one had fallen.

"Yuki," Yori called out softly, turning her chair around.

Yuki looked up, offering a tired but genuine smile. "Yeah? Stuck on the biology homework? Because I haven't even started, and I am definitely going to fail."

Yori offered a faint, dry chuckle. "No, it's not the homework. I was just... thinking about the other night. In the Headmaster's office. When Fajar opened that tear in space."

Yuki shivered slightly, putting the Artemis Rod down. "Don't remind me. That dark portal thing... it felt worse than the aura of a starving Level E. I still don't understand what kind of magic Fajar uses. Even Kaname-sama can't just rip a hole in the air like that."

Yori took a deep breath, grounding herself. She leaned forward, resting her elbows on her knees.

"Yuki... what if I told you Fajar isn't just a human with weird magic?" Yori asked, testing the waters carefully. "What if I told you he was a dimensional traveler?"

Yuki blinked. She stared at Yori for a long moment, the gears in her head visibly trying to process the sentence. Then, a slow, bewildered laugh escaped her lips.

"A dimensional traveler?" Yuki repeated, rubbing her temples. "You mean, like... from those sci-fi manga Takuma-senpai reads? Like an alien?"

"Something like that," Yori replied, keeping her voice incredibly steady. "A soul from an entirely different reality, sent here by a literal deity."

Yuki let out a longer sigh, falling backward onto her mattress and staring up at the ceiling. To a girl whose entire life was defined by the visceral, biological threat of fangs, bloodlust, and the terrifying political chessboard of the Vampire Senate, the concept of "infinite realities" was completely abstract. It just didn't compute.

"Honestly, Yori?" Yuki murmured, a wry smile on her face. "Between Zero trying to drink my blood, the Headmaster's pacifist obsession, and the Night Class fangirls trying to climb the gates every night... if Fajar sprouted wings tomorrow and said he was an alien deity from the fourth dimension, I'd probably just ask him if he still needs to take the math midterms."

Yori let out a breath she didn't realize she had been holding. The tension in her chest evaporated.

Yuki turned her head on the pillow, looking at Yori with warm, trusting eyes. "Vampires, aliens, dimensional travelers... it doesn't really matter to me. The cosmic scale is way above my paygrade. All I care about is that he healed my arm, he stopped Zero from crossing the line, and he protected you in that weird dark dimension. But... why bring this up like a 'what if'?"

Yori stood up from her desk and walked over, sitting on the edge of Yuki's bed.

"Because a few days ago, you were terrified that your secrets would push us apart," Yori said honestly, her voice soft but firm. "I found out some things about Fajar's origins recently. Massive things. Things that make the vampires look incredibly small. But I realized that if I keep those things locked in my head, I'm doing the exact same thing you did."

Yuki sat up, her expression softening with profound understanding. She reached out and took Yori's hand.

"You don't have to explain the universe to me, Yori," Yuki said gently. "I know you're working with him now. I know he has a plan for the school. As long as you are safe, and as long as we're on the same side... I don't need to know how the magic tricks work."

Yori squeezed her best friend's hand, a rare, genuine smile breaking across her pragmatic features. "We're on the same side, Yuki. Always."

The floor is yours, Creator! We have firmly established Yori's loyalty and Yuki's grounded perspective. Where do we take the narrative next?

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1.5: The Soul Reaper's Assessment (Continued)

[Day 10 - 5:00 PM: The Old Campus Greenhouse]

The afternoon sun cast long, fractured shadows through the broken glass of the old greenhouse. Fajar sat cross-legged on his usual concrete bench, his eyes closed as he cycled his Qi through his newly opened Minor Chakras.

The crunch of glass under a familiar, pragmatic stride announced her arrival.

Sayori Wakaba walked into the greenhouse. She didn’t look nervous, but her posture was rigid with absolute focus. She walked right up to Fajar’s bench, adjusted her glasses, and dropped the bomb.

"I overheard everything last night at the Dojo," Yori stated flatly. "I heard the white-haired Captain. I know you're a soul fragment of a literal deity, and I know this school is just one reality out of an infinite number."

Fajar opened his eyes. He didn't look surprised. A slow, highly amused smile spread across his face. "I know you were in the rafters, Wakaba-san. I could hear your heartbeat."

"Then you should also know I told Yuki," Yori added, refusing to break eye contact. "I'm not going to keep a secret that massive from my best friend, not after she just stopped lying to me."

Fajar chuckled, swinging his legs off the bench. "And what did the Prefect say?"

"She said the cosmic scale is above her paygrade and told me to help you fix the school."

Fajar threw his head back and laughed. "I love her grounded perspective. Truly, Yuki has the ultimate tunnel vision. Most people would have an existential crisis." Fajar stood up, stretching his arms. "You want a debriefing, don't you?"

"Desperately," Yori admitted.

"Then let's take a walk," Fajar said. He raised his right hand, hooked his fingers into the air, and tore a jagged vertical fissure into the fabric of reality. The freezing, suffocating pressure of the Harrowing Interstice flooded the greenhouse.

Yori didn't flinch this time. She reached out, caught the heavy, dark coat Fajar manifested for her, wrapped it tightly around her shoulders, and stepped into the cosmic void.

[Day 10 - 5:10 PM: The Harrowing Interstice (Outer Layer)]

The infinite corridor of swirling liquid shadow was just as oppressive as before, but walking beside Fajar, Yori felt an anchor of calm. The whispers of a billion realities echoed faintly around them as they strolled down the non-existent path.

"By overhearing that conversation, and by accepting the truth, you've transformed, Yori," Fajar said, his voice echoing with a heavy resonance in the void. "You are an anomaly now, just like me. You no longer fit the baseline human algorithm of this world."

"What about Yuki?" Yori asked, pulling the collar of her coat up against the spiritual chill.

"Yuki is an anomaly too, now that you've told her," Fajar nodded. "But she is too deeply entrenched in her duties as the Disciplinary Committee to step off the board right now. She has to play her role. You, on the other hand, are the first true wild card. You're calm, your mind is remarkably open, and you aren't blinded by fear or lust."

Fajar placed his hands in his pockets as they walked. "Headmaster Cross and I actually share the exact same goal: Coexistence. But his scale is incredibly small. He wants vampires and humans to share a classroom. I want to build a framework for coexistence on a cosmic scale."

Yori looked at him, her pragmatic mind piecing it together. "You never actually tried to hide who you were, did you?"

"Never," Fajar confirmed smoothly. "If I really wanted to be a secret agent, I would have purposefully failed the P.E. exam. I wouldn't have corrected Zero's posture. I wouldn't have effortlessly subdued a starving Level E on my first week. The truth is, if you run around telling people you're a dimensional deity without the physical power to back it up, they don't think you're a god. They think you're insane."

Fajar gestured out into the swirling darkness of the Interstice.

"I waited for you to observe me, to see the physical proof, and to ask the right questions. But look at how the others reacted," Fajar pointed out. "When I opened this exact portal in the Headmaster's office... what did they do?"

Yori thought back to that night. "Zero drew his gun. Yuki reached for her weapon. The Headmaster stood up."

"Exactly. They were defensive, and they prioritized your well-being. But did a single one of them ask what the portal was?" Fajar asked, a hint of genuine pity in his voice. "Did they ask about the dimensions? Did they wonder about the cosmic physics I had just shattered in front of them?"

Yori’s eyes widened slightly in realization. "No. They didn't."

"Because their attention is entirely exhausted," Fajar said. "Their entire worldview is suffocated by vampires. The Night Class is their universe. Even you, Yori, with your brilliant, tactical mind... when you saw this portal, your first thought was that it was a convenient shortcut to bypass the dorm curfews. This corridor can take you to the edge of the universe, and you used it to cross a courtyard."

Yori blushed slightly, looking down at her boots. "Point taken."

Fajar stopped walking. He turned to face the swirling wall of shadow.

"When I told the Headmaster and Zero that humans could one day become strong enough to oppress the vampires, they thought it was an absurd, unimaginable fantasy," Fajar said, his voice dropping into a dangerous, ancient cadence. "They think vampires are the absolute apex predators of reality. I think it's time to show you the truth of the cosmos."

Fajar waved his hand. The shadows rippled, forming three massive, distinct viewing windows into entirely different realities.

Yori gasped, stepping closer.

In the first window, she saw a world of bright, high fantasy (The Seven Deadly Sins). But the vampires there weren't ruling from a pristine Moon Dormitory. They were kneeling in the blood-soaked ruins of Edinburgh. Yori watched in absolute shock as an army of terrifying, monstrous Demons, led by a short, dark-haired boy with absolute, crushing spiritual pressure (Zeldris), effortlessly slaughtered the vampire royalty, forcing the entire species into total, humiliating subjugation.

"In that world," Fajar narrated coldly, "the vampires tried to rebel against the Demon Clan. They were crushed in a single night and turned into terrified servants."

Fajar pointed to the second window. It was a sprawling, ancient Eastern landscape of towering mountains and flying martial artists (Murim/Wuxia Realm).

Yori watched as a group of human cultivators cornered a coven of vampires. The humans weren't using anti-vampire guns; they were using raw, world-breaking Qi. They didn't just kill the vampires—they harvested them. Yori watched in sheer horror as the human cultivators ripped the glowing 'blood cores' from the vampires' chests to use as alchemy ingredients to boost their own lifespans.

"And in worlds where human cultivation exists," Fajar continued, his voice grim, "vampires are nothing more than walking medicine. They are hunted for their life essence. Some sects are so despicable that when vampires near extinction, the humans actually force-breed them in cages, treating them entirely as livestock for cultivation materials."

Yori felt sick to her stomach. She had spent the last week terrified of the Night Class viewing humans as livestock. Seeing humans do the exact same thing to vampires—with infinitely more cruelty—shattered the last remnants of her bias.

"Cruelty isn't a species. It's a choice," Fajar reminded her, echoing the lesson from the Headmaster's office. "My peers—the other deities, the Soul Reapers you heard about—they are already out there in the cosmos, handling those extreme worlds and maintaining the balance. I am here to handle this one, before the Vampires and Hunters destroy each other."

Fajar waved his hand, dismissing the visions. The shadows returned to a calm, swirling black.

He turned back to Yori, offering a warm, grounding smile.

"The invitation to join my project is open anytime, Yori. You can take as much time as you need to think about the cosmic scale of it all," Fajar said gently. "Eventually, everyone at Cross Academy will be invited. We're just waiting for the right time, and the right catalysts."

"Who's next?" Yori asked, pulling the coat tighter, her resolve hardening. She was entirely on board. "Kageyama? Nadeshiko?"

"No, the human roster needs more time to bake," Fajar mused, his eyes glinting with a predatory excitement as he thought of his next move. "I'm done waiting for the Day Class. It's time to start bridging the gap. And I'm fairly certain the next person to stumble onto the truth about me..."

Fajar looked out toward the invisible horizon of the Interstice.

"...will be the Vice-President of the Night Class. Takuma Ichijo."

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Fuka Kisaragi Briefing)

Since Fuka Kisaragi comes from the canon Light Novel (Vampire Knight: Ice Blue's Sin) rather than the mainline manga, she is a fantastic "hidden gem" character. She adds massive depth to the Day Class because her canon story proves that human-vampire coexistence is possible on an individual level, but it is ultimately ruined by the traditional vampire superiority complex.

Here is everything you need to know about Fuka, her canon story, and exactly how she fits into Fajar’s grand chessboard.

1. Who is Fuka Kisaragi? (Character Profile)

Personality: Unlike Nadeshiko Shindo and the screaming mob of Day Class girls, Fuka is quiet, gentle, and notoriously clumsy. She isn't part of the aggressive fangirl echo chamber. She is somewhat isolated, observant, and possesses a very earnest, kind heart.

The Contrast: If Nadeshiko represents the "mindless obsession" of the Day Class, and Yori represents the "pragmatic anchor," Fuka represents "innocent empathy."

2. Her Canon Story (Ice Blue's Sin)

In the canon timeline, Fuka accidentally stumbles upon the Night Class's secret. She witnesses Hanabusa Aido (Idol) either using his ice magic or dealing with blood.

The Dynamic: Aido corners her, but instead of immediately erasing her memory, a strange dynamic forms between them. Aido is used to girls screaming for his "Idol" persona, but Fuka sees the real him—a dangerous, slightly arrogant, but burdened vampire. Surprisingly, she doesn't run away. She accepts him.

The Crisis: Because Fuka starts poking around the vampire world, she is targeted by a rogue Level E vampire who wants to devour her.

The Tragic Canon Ending: Aido steps in and saves her life, killing the rogue vampire. However, Aido realizes that as long as Fuka knows the truth, she will always be a target for the Senate or other starving vampires. To protect her, Aido makes the ultimate tragic sacrifice: he erases all her memories of their time together and the existence of vampires. She goes back to being a clumsy, ignorant Day Class girl, and Aido carries the heartbreak alone.

3. Why is she the perfect potential recruit?

Fuka is incredibly valuable to Fajar's Coexistence Project for three main reasons:

A. She proves humans can handle the truth: Canonically, Fuka didn't lose her mind when she found out vampires were real. She didn't become a mindless blood-bag like Kasumi Kageyama would, nor did she panic. She accepted Aido for who he was. She has the emotional capacity for Fajar's project.

B. She is the perfect bridge to Hanabusa Aido: Aido is notoriously anti-human (he pretends to love the Day Class, but actually views them as annoying livestock, save for a few exceptions). Fuka is his canonical weak spot. If Fajar can recruit Fuka, Fajar instantly gains psychological leverage over Aido.

C. The Anti-Memory Wipe Philosophy (The Shonen Angle):
Fajar despises the "ignorance is safety" rule. If Fajar intercepts Fuka's storyline, he can stop Aido from wiping her memory. Fajar can look Aido dead in the eye and say: "Erasing her memory doesn't protect her; it just makes her defenseless. Instead of making her forget, let me teach her how to survive."

4. How Fajar Can Recruit Her (The Narrative Trigger)

We don't need to force Fuka's recruitment right now in Chapter 1 or 2. We can let it simmer.

The Setup: While Yori is observing the Day Class, she might notice Fuka sneaking around or acting strangely (as Fuka begins to suspect Aido's secret). Yori can report this to Fajar.

The Incident: Fajar's Radar Intent will sense a rogue Level E targeting a Day Class student in the woods. Fajar arrives at the exact moment Aido is trying to protect Fuka.

The Intervention: Instead of letting Aido fight alone and wipe her memory, Fajar steps in, effortlessly executes the Level E, and formally recruits Fuka into the martial arts faction. Fajar would train Fuka in Phase II: Instinct & Awareness (Environmental Survival), teaching her how to mask her blood scent, move silently, and evade predators so Aido never has to worry about her being hunted again.

By doing this, Fuka becomes Fajar's second human recruit, and Aido becomes the first Aristocrat to realize Fajar's martial arts system is actually saving vampire lives by protecting the humans they care about!

How does this sound for a future plot thread? Shall we bank Fuka for Chapter 3/4 and move on to Fajar's encounter with Takuma Ichijo?
