You hit on a massive piece of canon lore! Yes, Sayori (Yori) Wakaba and Hanabusa Aido actually get married in the canon timeline.

Here are the details of their canon relationship, and how we can perfectly resolve the dynamic with Fuka Kisaragi in our Shonen-style fanfiction.

1. The Canon Details: Yori & Aido (Endgame)

In the sequel manga, Vampire Knight: Memories, the narrative jumps through the centuries.

The Foundation: Their relationship doesn't start from "fangirl obsession." Yori is immune to Aido's "Idol" persona. She treats him like a normal person, and she is incredibly blunt with him. Aido, who is used to girls throwing themselves at him, finds Yori's pragmatism incredibly refreshing and deeply respects her.

The Shared Goal: After the events of the main series, Aido dedicates his immortal life to fulfilling Kaname's dream: creating a biological cure to turn vampires into humans. Yori, being fiercely intelligent, becomes his research partner and stays by his side.

The Marriage: They fall in love, get married, and have a child together (a son).

The Tragic/Beautiful End: Because Aido is a vampire and Yori is human, Yori ages while Aido remains frozen in time. Yori eventually passes away from old age, surrounded by her family. Aido is heartbroken but deeply grateful for the life they shared, and he continues her legacy, eventually perfecting the cure centuries later.

Their relationship is arguably the healthiest, most grounded romance in the entire Vampire Knight series because it represents true, equal coexistence.

2. The Dynamic Issue: What about Fuka?

In canon, Fuka (Ice Blue's Sin) was essentially Aido's tragic "first human connection." He cared for her, but because she was fragile and hunted, he erased her memories. Yori, on the other hand, was his mature, endgame partner.

3. Fuka's New Life (The Shonen Evolution)

In this fanfiction, we don't need Fuka to be Aido's tragic lost love, nor do we need her to fight Yori for his affection. Fajar's intervention will fundamentally change Fuka's psychology.

The Rejection of "Idolization"
Right now, Fuka's feelings for Aido are based on the traditional vampire trope: the weak, clumsy human girl swooning over the beautiful, dangerous predator.

When Fajar recruits Fuka and teaches her Phase II: Instinct & Awareness, she stops being prey. As she learns how to mask her scent, move silently, and defend herself, she gains massive self-respect.

Through martial arts, Fuka will realize that her infatuation with Aido wasn't true love; it was just a teenage crush amplified by his vampire pheromones and her own insecurity.

Once she becomes strong, she will look at Aido's arrogant, dramatic "Idol" personality and simply roll her eyes. She outgrows him.

The Sisterhood (Yori & Fuka)
Instead of rivals, Yori and Fuka become the core of the human faction's sisterhood.

Yori is the tactical brain and the pragmatist. (She naturally gravitates toward Aido later because they share an intellectual bond over solving the vampire biology issue).

Fuka becomes the stealth/scout specialist. Fajar turns the "clumsy" girl into a ghost who can track vampires through the woods without being seen.

Fuka's Alternate Romance/Path
Since she is no longer chained to the Aido plotline, Fuka is a free agent!

She could become utterly devoted to the martial path, acting as Fajar's most loyal human disciple.

She could develop a hilarious, bickering dynamic with Takahashi (the Gigai possessed by Tōshirō Hitsugaya), where the clumsy girl and the perpetually annoyed Soul Reaper form an unlikely bond.

Or, when the other dimensional crossover characters finally arrive to fill the Day Class's missing male roster, Fuka could find a romance with a genuinely strong, equal human partner instead of an aristocratic vampire.

Fajar's Perspective

Fajar would absolutely support Yori and Aido's eventual romance because it proves his thesis: Coexistence requires both sides to drop their facades. Aido has to drop his arrogant Aristocrat persona, and Yori proves that humans don't need magic to stand as equals with vampires.

Meanwhile, Fajar gets to turn Fuka into a total badass who realizes she doesn't need a vampire prince to save her.

Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Resetting Fuka Kisaragi)

Understood completely. We are scrapping the previous lighthearted ideas and grounding this entirely in the dark, tragic reality of the Ice Blue's Sin novel. Let's break down exactly what the novel dictates regarding Fuka, her timeline, and her relationships to perfectly set up her place in Fajar's current world.

Here are the answers based strictly on the novel's canon:

1. Where is Fuka now? Is she in the Day Class?

Yes, she is currently in the Day Class. In the timeline, Fuka transferred to Cross Academy recently. Because the novel takes place in the early, "peaceful" days of the academy (which aligns perfectly with Fajar's first week), Fuka is already here. She is currently attending classes right alongside Fajar, Yori, and Yuki.

2. How did she bypass Zero and Yuki to get to the Moon Dorm?

She didn't use stealth or martial arts; she was invited in by the predators.
Before transferring to Cross Academy, Fuka was attacked by a rogue vampire during her summer vacation. Because of this, she is slowly, painfully mutating into a Level E. The mutation causes her to sleepwalk at night, driven by a subconscious thirst for blood.
During one of these sleepwalking episodes, she wandered into the forest and encountered Hanabusa Aido. Instead of Yuki and Zero catching her, Kaname Kuran intervened. Kaname realized she was turning, and because he is deeply pragmatic and sometimes ruthless, he gave the Night Class secret authorization to bring her into the Moon Dormitory. Zero and Yuki don't know she goes there because the Aristocrats are actively hiding her from the Disciplinary Committee to use her as a secret project.

3. Has the experiment happened or not?

It is currently happening right now.
Fuka does not know she is turning into a vampire. She thinks she has a strange, chronic illness (like severe anemia). Aido and Kaname are giving her experimental, newly developed "Blood Tablets," telling her it is special medicine for her condition.
At this exact moment in our timeline, Fuka is secretly visiting the Moon Dormitory, taking these pills, and feeling a false sense of security, completely unaware that she is just a lab rat for Kaname's pharmaceutical testing.

4. Who is her roommate Kanae, and does she forgive Fuka?

Kanae is Fuka’s best friend and roommate in the Sun Dormitory. Kanae is fiercely loyal, perceptive, and deeply protective of Fuka. She is the one who constantly worries about Fuka’s pale complexion, her exhaustion, and her strange behavior.

The Bite and Forgiveness:
In the climax of the novel, the experimental pills stop working. Fuka's vampire instincts completely take over, and in a state of starving delirium, she attacks and bites Kanae in their dorm room.

Kanae is absolutely terrified and goes into shock from the blood loss and the sheer horror of her best friend turning into a monster.

However, Kanae's core character is built on love for Fuka. While she is deeply traumatized, the novel shows that the tragedy is Fuka's overwhelming guilt, not Kanae's hatred.

Unfortunately, Kanae doesn't get the chance to fully process or verbally forgive her in a meaningful, long-term way because after Fuka is executed by Aido, Kaname wipes Kanae's memories entirely. Kanae wakes up believing Fuka transferred away, her mind scrubbed of the trauma.

How this sets up the perfect Shonen Intervention for Fajar:

Right now, Fuka is walking around the Day Class, slowly dying, being manipulated by the Night Class, and sleeping in the same room as her best friend, Kanae, who she is destined to bite.

Since Yori is now actively observing the Day Class for Fajar, Yori could easily notice Kanae constantly worrying about Fuka's "illness," or notice Fuka slipping away at night. This gives Fajar the perfect, organic reason to investigate, intercept the "experiment," and prevent the tragedy before Kanae ever gets bitten.

**Gemini:**
Chapter 2: The Rotting Foundation

[Day 11 - 8:30 PM: The Sun Dormitory, Girls' Wing]

The small desk lamp cast a warm, yellow glow over the dorm room. Kanae sat on the edge of her bed, watching her best friend with a deep, unconcealed crease of worry on her forehead.

Fuka Kisaragi was sitting at her desk, staring blankly at a textbook. Her skin, normally fair, looked almost translucent in the dim light, and a faint, sickly sheen of sweat clung to her collarbone. She looked exhausted, as if gravity itself was pulling her down.

"Fuka, you're spacing out again," Kanae said gently, walking over and placing a mug of hot milk on the desk. "You barely touched your dinner at the cafeteria. Are you feeling dizzy?"

Fuka blinked, snapping out of her trance. She offered Kanae a weak, apologetic smile. "Sorry, Kanae. Just... my anemia acting up again. I've been feeling so lethargic lately."

"Lethargic is an understatement. You look like a ghost," Kanae scolded, though her tone was entirely maternal. She crossed her arms, leaning against the desk. "Honestly, if it wasn't for that special medicine you've been taking, I would have dragged you to the Headmaster's infirmary myself. Did you take your dose today?"

Fuka’s hand instinctively drifted to her pocket, where a small, unmarked bottle of white tablets rested. Kaname Kuran's special medicine. "Yes," Fuka lied softly. She hadn't taken it yet today. The medicine worked, but lately, the periods between doses were getting harder to endure. A strange, dry ache constantly clawed at the back of her throat. "I'll be fine, Kanae. Really."

Kanae sighed, brushing a stray lock of hair behind Fuka's ear. "You better be. Midterms are coming up, and the Day Class girls are already losing their minds trying to organize another 'accidental' run-in with the Night Class before the exams. I heard Nadeshiko is trying to bribe Kageyama for the patrol routes. Idiots. They care more about Aido-senpai's smile than passing math."

At the mention of Hanabusa Aido, Fuka's heart gave a strange, painful flutter. She looked down at her hands, the memory of his cold, beautiful eyes flashing in her mind. He was the only one who seemed to understand her illness. He was the one giving her the medicine.

"Yeah," Fuka murmured, her voice distant. "Idiots."

Kanae patted her shoulder. "Drink the milk and get some sleep. I'm going to take a shower."

As Kanae left the room, Fuka reached into her pocket. She pulled out the small bottle and stared at the white pills. Her throat burned. The urge to leave the room, to walk out into the cold night air and head toward the forest surrounding the Moon Dormitory, was becoming an overwhelming, magnetic pull.

[Day 11 - 11:00 PM: Fajar's Dorm Room]

Across the campus, in the boys' wing, the air pressure inside Fajar's room was behaving bizarrely.

The loose papers on his desk were vibrating. The temperature in the room fluctuated wildly between freezing and boiling. Fajar sat bare-chested in the center of the floor in a deep lotus position, his eyes closed, his breathing practically non-existent.

He was pushing past the Minor Chakras. He was consolidating the foundation.

Step 3: Dan Storage.

Until now, the Qi he had cultivated flowed through his meridians like mist, saturating his muscles and nerves. But mist was inefficient for sustained, heavy combat. He needed a reservoir.

With absolute, tyrannical focus, Fajar commanded the energy coursing through his body to sink. He forced it down into his lower abdomen—the Lower Dantian. The resistance was immense; his human vessel groaned under the pressure of compressing spiritual energy into a physical space.

But Fajar's will was a deity's will.

Compress. The mist thickened into a heavy, swirling liquid. It anchored itself just below his navel, forming a dense, burning core of pure, refined Qi. The moment the Dan Storage stabilized, the chaotic air pressure in the room snapped back to normal.

Fajar opened his eyes. They flashed with a brief, terrifying golden light before settling back into a calm, dark brown. His body felt impossibly light, yet grounded with the weight of a mountain. His stamina was now virtually limitless.

He took a slow breath, letting his Radar Intent sweep outward to test his newly expanded sensory range.

He felt Zero patrolling the front gates. He felt Yuki in the eastern courtyard. He felt the heavy, dark magic of the Aristocrats lounging in the Moon Dormitory.

And then, he felt an anomaly.

Fajar’s brow furrowed. It was a faint signature, moving slowly through the woods near the edge of the campus. It was a human soul, but it felt... wrong. It felt like an apple rotting from the inside out. It carried the distinct, chaotic static of a mutating biology. It was a human turning into a Level E vampire.

Fajar stood up and walked to his window. He traced the trajectory of the rotting signature. It had originated from the Sun Dormitory—specifically, the second floor of the girls' wing—and it was walking a direct, practiced path toward the back entrance of the Moon Dormitory.

A Day Class girl is sneaking into the vampire den, Fajar noted. And she’s already infected.

Normally, Fajar would have jumped out the window and intercepted the anomaly immediately. But considering the signature originated from deep inside the girls' dormitory, Fajar paused. Breaking into the girls' dorm once for a tactical test was one thing. Making a habit of lurking around the female students' quarters or tracking them through the woods at night crossed a line of personal dignity he refused to breach unless lives were in immediate danger.

"If the Night Class is hiding an infected human..." Fajar murmured to himself, his Shonen instincts sensing a massive, hidden conspiracy. "I need inside intel."

[Day 12 - 12:15 PM: The Library]

The next day, during the lunch break, Fajar found Sayori Wakaba sitting alone at a secluded table in the library, a stack of reference books acting as a perfect barricade.

Fajar slid into the chair across from her, dropping a notebook on the table to keep up appearances.

Yori didn't look up from her book. "Status report?" she asked quietly.

"I need your eyes in the Sun Dormitory," Fajar said, keeping his voice to a low, localized whisper. "Last night, while I was meditating, I tracked an energy signature moving from the second floor of the girls' wing directly to the Moon Dormitory. Someone is bypassing the Disciplinary Committee entirely."

Yori finally looked up, her pragmatic eyes narrowing. "Nadeshiko? She's been trying to figure out the patrol routes for weeks."

"No. Not Nadeshiko," Fajar corrected, his expression turning serious. "The signature I felt was biologically unstable. Wakaba-san, whoever is sneaking out isn't just a fangirl trying to get a picture. They are infected. Someone in your dorm is slowly turning into a Level E vampire, and the Moon Dormitory is covering it up."

Yori’s breath hitched. Her mind instantly raced through the roster of girls on her floor. "Are you absolutely sure?"

"My senses do not lie," Fajar stated firmly. "I know the rough coordinates of where she left from, but I refuse to skulk around the girls' dorm to figure out exactly who it is. I need you to find her. Look for a girl who is chronically exhausted, extremely pale, skipping meals, or acting secretive at night."

Yori closed her book, her expression hardening into absolute resolve. The thought of a girl slowly mutating into a monster just a few doors down from her and Yuki was terrifying, but she didn't panic.

"Pale, exhausted, and secretive," Yori repeated, committing the traits to memory. "I'll find her, Fajar. Give me two days."

**Gemini:**
Chapter 2: The Rotting Foundation (Continued)

[Day 13 - 7:00 AM: The Sun Dormitory Cafeteria]

Sayori Wakaba didn't need to pick locks or crawl through air vents to gather intelligence. She was a pragmatist. People hid their secrets in the dark, but their symptoms were always on full display in the light.

Over the next forty-eight hours, Yori simply sat at her usual table with Yuki, eating her breakfast while her eyes casually scanned the room.

The checklist Fajar gave her was specific: Chronically exhausted, extremely pale, skipping meals, acting secretive.

It only took Yori one day to narrow the list down to three girls. By the second morning, she had her absolute confirmation. Two tables away, Fuka Kisaragi was staring blankly at a bowl of untouched rice. Her roommate, Kanae, was anxiously hovering over her, pushing a carton of milk into her hands and whispering fiercely about "taking her medicine."

Yori watched as Fuka offered a weak, distracted nod, her hand instinctively drifting to her uniform pocket, gripping something inside with a desperate, white-knuckled tension.

That night, Yori stayed awake in her dark dorm room, sitting quietly by her cracked door. At exactly 1:15 AM, she heard the soft, uneven footsteps padding down the hall. Peeking out, Yori saw Fuka slipping down the stairs toward the side exit, her eyes slightly glazed over, walking with the magnetic pull of an addict.

Yori didn't follow her into the woods. She was a baseline human, and Fajar had taught her enough about predatory instinct to know that following an infected target into a vampire den without Qi was a death sentence. She simply closed her door, locked it, and went to sleep. The objective was complete.

[Day 14 - 4:00 PM: Headmaster Cross's Office]

The Headmaster’s office was tense. Kaien Cross sat behind his desk, the goofy facade entirely gone. Zero leaned against the far wall, his arms crossed tightly, glaring at the floor. Yuki stood near the window, looking deeply conflicted.

Fajar sat backward on one of the leather guest chairs, resting his chin on his arms casually. He didn't look like a commanding officer receiving a report; he looked like a guy listening to a friend tell a wild story over lunch.

Yori stood by the desk, pushing her glasses up the bridge of her nose.

"Her name is Fuka Kisaragi," Yori reported, keeping her voice even and analytical. "She’s in our class. She exhibits all the physical symptoms of severe, chronic blood loss, coupled with intense lethargy. Her roommate, Kanae, is under the impression that Fuka has anemia and is taking a 'special medicine' to treat it. I observed Fuka leaving the Sun Dormitory last night at 1:15 AM, taking the direct tree-line path toward the Moon Dormitory."

Fajar whistled softly, a relaxed, appreciative smile on his face. "Flawless, Yori. Seriously, you figured that out without raising a single alarm. Remind me never to try and hide anything from you."

Yori offered a small, rare smirk. "I'll keep that in mind."

"This is impossible," Yuki interrupted, her voice trembling slightly. "Fuka? I patrol those gates every night. If a Day Class student was wandering around the woods, Zero and I would have caught her."

"Not if the Night Class is actively hiding her from you," Fajar pointed out casually, leaning back. "Yuki, you patrol the gates. If an Aristocrat—or a Pureblood—gave her a VIP pass through the back woods and masked her scent from Zero, you'd never know."

Zero’s hands clenched into tight fists. "A Level E mutating inside the human dorms. If she loses control..."

"She'll bite whoever is closest," Yori finished grimly. "Which is Kanae."

Kaien laced his fingers together, his expression dangerously dark. "If Fuka was bitten during the summer, she should have been transferred to the Hunter Association's medical ward immediately. The fact that Kaname Kuran bypassed my authority, hid her condition, and is secretly treating her on campus... it violates the very core of our peace treaty."

"He's not just treating her, Headmaster," Fajar said, his casual tone hardening just a fraction. "Think about the timeline. Aido and Kaname are giving her 'special medicine.' If they had a real cure, she wouldn't be rotting from the inside out. Her signature is unstable. They aren't treating her; they're using her as a clinical trial for an experimental drug."

Zero scoffed, a bitter, furious sound. "Using a human girl as a lab rat. Typical."

"So, what's the play?" Fajar asked, looking around the room, specifically avoiding giving orders. "You guys are the official peacekeepers of this school. I'm just the transfer student who's good at martial arts. Headmaster, do you want to storm the Moon Dormitory and demand answers?"

Kaien sighed heavily, rubbing his temples. "If I confront Kaname directly without physical proof of the medicine or her condition, he will simply deny it, and it will trigger a political war with the Senate. We need to intercept her and secure the physical evidence—the pills—before we can act."

Fajar grinned, standing up and stretching his shoulders. The dense reservoir of Qi in his lower Dantian hummed with anticipation.

"Perfect. That’s exactly what I was hoping you'd say," Fajar said smoothly. "You guys stay out of the woods tonight. Kaname has eyes everywhere. If the Disciplinary Committee suddenly changes its patrol route to intercept Fuka, the vampires will know. They'll abort the meeting."

Yuki looked worried. "Then who is going to stop her?"

Fajar tapped his own chest. "I will. My Qi doesn't register as magic or vampiric aura. To the Night Class, I'm just a kid with zero spiritual pressure. I'll intercept Fuka tonight, grab the 'special medicine', and see if I can clear the venom out of her system before she accidentally eats her best friend."

Fajar looked over at Yori. "Keep an eye on Kanae tonight. If Fuka doesn't make it back to the room, Kanae might panic."

Yori nodded. "Understood."

"Alright," Fajar said, turning toward the door with a casual wave. "I've got a clinical trial to crash."

**Gemini:**
Chapter 2: The Rotting Foundation (Continued)

[Day 14 - 11:45 PM: Fuka Kisaragi’s Perspective - The Sun Dormitory]

Fuka Kisaragi was drowning, and the surface of the water was getting further and further away.

She lay on her bed, clutching her stomach as a violently hot fever tore through her veins. The air in the dorm room felt so thin it was suffocating. Every sound—the wind rattling the windowpane, the hum of the radiator, and most terrifyingly, the steady, rhythmic thump-thump-thump of Kanae’s heartbeat across the room—echoed in her skull like a heavy drum.

Her throat felt like it was packed with dry, burning sand.

With trembling hands, Fuka reached under her pillow and pulled out the small, unmarked glass bottle. There were only a few white tablets left inside.

“Take these when the dizziness starts,” Kaname Kuran’s voice echoed in her memory. She remembered standing in the opulent, dimly lit parlor of the Moon Dormitory just a few nights ago. Kaname had sat on the velvet sofa, looking at her not as a student, but the way a scientist observes a fragile, fascinating specimen.

Beside him, Hanabusa Aido had stood silently. For all his dramatic, arrogant flair around the Day Class girls, Aido was entirely different when Fuka visited. His blue eyes always carried a heavy, complicated mixture of guilt and pity. He had been the one to press the bottle into her hands. “It’s a special medicine, Fuka. Don't skip a dose. Promise me.”

She had promised. She had believed them.

Fuka popped the cork off the bottle, poured two white pills into her palm, and swallowed them dry. She closed her eyes, waiting for the familiar, cooling relief to wash over her—the soothing numbness that usually quelled the burning in her throat.

One minute passed. Then five.

Nothing happened.

The burning didn't fade; it violently accelerated. A sudden, agonizing spasm wracked her body, and Fuka clamped a hand over her mouth, stifling a choked sob. The medicine wasn't working anymore. Her body had built an immunity to Kaname’s experimental formula. The illusion of her "anemia" was shattering, replaced by a dark, primal starvation that she could no longer deny.

She remembered the summer before transferring to Cross Academy. The dark alley. The terrifying man with glowing red eyes. The piercing pain in her neck. She had convinced herself it was a bad dream, an animal attack. But as the burning in her throat morphed into a desperate, ravenous thirst, the horrific truth finally locked into place.

She wasn't sick. She was mutating. She was a vampire.

A Level E.

"Fuka...?"

The soft, sleepy voice came from across the room. Kanae shifted in her bed, sitting up and rubbing her eyes. She looked over at Fuka’s trembling silhouette in the dark.

"Fuka, are you crying? Is the fever back?" Kanae asked, throwing her covers off. Her bare feet padded softly against the floorboards. "Hold on, I'll go get a cold towel—"

"Don't," Fuka gasped out, her voice a ragged, unnatural hiss. She scrambled backward, pressing her spine against the wall. "Kanae, stay away. Please."

But Kanae was too kind, too stubbornly loyal. She took another step forward, reaching her hand out toward Fuka’s shoulder in the dark. "Don't be stupid, you're burning up. Let me help you."

As Kanae drew closer, the scent hit Fuka.

It wasn't the smell of Kanae’s floral shampoo or her laundry detergent. It was the sweet, intoxicating, overwhelmingly rich scent of the blood pulsing just beneath the thin skin of Kanae’s wrist.

Fuka’s vision completely swam with crimson. Rational thought, love, and restraint were instantly incinerated by the absolute, biological imperative to feed.

Fuka didn't even realize she had moved.

With unnatural speed, she lunged off the bed. Kanae let out a startled gasp as Fuka pinned her against the edge of the mattress. Fuka’s lips parted, and a pair of sharp, elongated fangs extended from her gums, tearing through her own bottom lip.

"Fuka, what—"

Fuka buried her face into Kanae’s shoulder and bit down hard.

The warm, metallic taste of blood flooded Fuka’s mouth. For two terrifying seconds, it was pure, unadulterated euphoria. The burning in her throat vanished, replaced by an ecstatic rush of energy that made her entire body tremble.

And then, Kanae screamed.

It was a sharp, high-pitched scream of absolute agony and terror.

The sound shattered the blood-lust. Fuka’s human consciousness violently snapped back into control. She gasped, ripping her fangs out of Kanae’s flesh and stumbling backward in the dark.

Kanae collapsed onto the floor, clutching her bleeding shoulder. She looked up at Fuka, her eyes wide, reflecting nothing but sheer, primal horror. She was hyperventilating, completely paralyzed by the shock of what her best friend had just become.

Fuka looked at her own trembling hands. They were stained crimson. She tasted her best friend's blood on her tongue.

The weight of her sin crushed her soul instantly. She had done the unforgivable. She had become the monster from her nightmares. If she stayed here, she would kill Kanae. If she went to the Headmaster, she would be hunted down. There was no medicine. There was no cure. She was a rotting thing, destined to lose her mind and devour the people she loved.

There was only one way to end it.

"I'm sorry," Fuka sobbed, tears streaming down her pale cheeks. "Kanae... I'm so sorry."

Fuka turned and bolted. She tore out of the dorm room, sprinting down the hallway with terrifying, vampiric speed. She burst through the side exit of the Sun Dormitory and plunged into the freezing darkness of the forest.

She didn't care about the Disciplinary Committee. She didn't care about the rules. Fuka ran blindly through the trees, the branches tearing at her uniform, her destination completely fixed in her mind.

The Moon Dormitory. She needed to find Hanabusa Aido. He was the one who had given her the medicine. He was the one who had looked at her with pity. He was a predator, a true Aristocrat.

Kill me, Fuka begged in her mind as the towering silhouette of the Moon Dormitory finally appeared through the trees. Aido-senpai... please kill me before I eat anyone else.

Meta-Discussion: System Check & Confirmation

I can absolutely confirm my alignment with the Ice Blue's Sin canon regarding this climax! In the novel, Fuka reaches the Moon Dormitory and encounters Aido. She confesses her sin, absolutely terrified of herself, and begs Aido to kill her before she loses her mind completely. Aido, carrying the heavy guilt of the failed experiment, agrees to freeze her to death to spare her the humiliation of becoming a mindless Level E.

Let's weave this tragic canon moment into Fajar's Shonen intervention!

Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Continued)

[Day 14 - 11:47 PM: Headmaster Cross's Office]

Fajar was still stretching his shoulders, preparing to leave, when his Radar Intent suddenly spiked. The unstable, rotting signature in the girls' dormitory violently flared with the unmistakable, euphoric rush of a vampire tasting fresh blood.

Fajar paused. He dropped his arms and let out a slow, casual sigh.

"Well," Fajar said, his voice completely devoid of panic but heavy with finality. "Looks like we're too late. She just took a bite."

The temperature in the office plummeted. Zero’s eyes widened in horror before his hunter instincts completely took over. Without a word, he kicked the office door open and sprinted down the hallway. Yuki gasped, grabbing her Artemis Rod, and tore after him. Yori didn't hesitate, breaking into a dead sprint right behind her best friend.

Fajar didn't run. He calmly walked over to Headmaster Cross's desk.

"Headmaster," Fajar said smoothly. "I need you to write an official administrative document, right now. State clearly that Fuka Kisaragi and Kanae are officially under my absolute jurisdiction and protection, effective immediately."

Kaien Cross didn't ask questions. He pulled out a piece of official Cross Academy parchment, scribbled the mandate with lightning speed, stamped it with the Headmaster’s official seal, and handed it to Fajar.

Fajar slipped the paper into his gi. "Thank you. I'll be right back."

[Day 14 - 11:50 PM: The Sun Dormitory, Girls' Wing]

Zero and Yuki burst into Fuka’s dorm room, their weapons drawn. The metallic scent of blood was suffocating.

Fuka was gone. Kanae was collapsed on the floor, hyperventilating and clutching her bleeding shoulder in absolute terror.

Yori slid into the room a second later. She took one look at the situation, immediately dropping to her knees beside Kanae. She didn't ask what happened; the bite marks were obvious. Yori pulled a clean towel from the bathroom rack and pressed it hard against the wound.

"Go!" Yori barked, her pragmatic voice cutting through the panic as she anchored the sobbing girl. "I've got her! Track Fuka down!"

Zero’s lilac eyes glowed with pure killing intent. He spun around, tracking the lingering scent of Fuka’s bloodlust. "She's heading for the Moon Dormitory. Move!"

[Day 14 - 11:55 PM: The Moon Dormitory Gates]

Fuka collapsed onto the cold stone path just outside the towering gates of the Moon Dormitory. Her uniform was torn, her hands stained with her best friend's blood.

The heavy iron gates clicked open. Hanabusa Aido walked out, his blonde hair catching the moonlight. His usual arrogant, playful smirk was completely gone. His ice-blue eyes looked down at the sobbing, broken girl with a profound, heavy sorrow.

"Aido-senpai..." Fuka choked out, her voice a ragged sob. "I did it... I bit Kanae. The medicine stopped working. I'm a monster."

Aido crouched down in front of her. He didn't flinch away from the blood. He knew this day was coming. Kaname's experiment had failed, and Fuka was the collateral damage.

"I'm sorry, Fuka," Aido said softly, his voice devoid of its usual theatrics.

"Please," Fuka begged, grabbing the sleeve of his white uniform. "Before I completely lose my mind... before I hurt anyone else... please kill me. You're the only one who was honest with me. Do it."

Aido closed his eyes. A freezing, heavy aura began to bleed from his skin. The grass around his boots crystallized with frost. He raised his hand, aiming his palm at Fuka's chest, preparing to freeze her heart instantly so she wouldn't feel any pain.

"Stop right there, Aido!"

Yuki burst through the treeline, the Artemis Rod extended. Zero was right beside her, the Bloody Rose aimed directly at Aido's head.

"Step away from her!" Zero snarled, his finger hovering over the trigger.

Aido stood up, glaring at the Disciplinary Committee. "Stay out of this, Kiryu! You don't understand what's happening! The pills failed. She's a Level E now. There is no cure for her. If I don't do this, she'll become a mindless beast, or the Senate will execute her!"

"You don't get to execute a Day Class student to cover up Kaname's failed experiments!" Yuki screamed, tears of desperation in her eyes as she stood between Aido and the sobbing Fuka. "There has to be another way! We can isolate her, we can—"

"There is no other way, Yuki!" Aido yelled back, the ice magic flaring violently around him. "She asked me to do it! Don't make this harder than it already is!"

"Actually," a calm, deeply amused voice interrupted. "There is another way."

Aido’s ice magic instantly sputtered. Zero and Yuki froze.

Fajar was standing directly behind Fuka.

He hadn't dropped from the trees. He hadn't run out of the woods. There had been no sound of footsteps, no displacement of air, and absolutely zero spiritual pressure. To the incredibly sensitive predatory instincts of Aido and Zero, Fajar simply hadn't existed a millisecond ago.

Before Aido could even raise his hand, Fajar reached into his gi and held up the parchment bearing the Headmaster's seal, right in front of Aido's face.

"Official decree from the Headmaster," Fajar stated casually. "Fuka Kisaragi is now under my jurisdiction. I'll be taking her for medical treatment. You Aristocrats can go back to your tea party."

Aido’s eyes narrowed, his fangs baring slightly. "You arrogant human... I don't know how you snuck up on me, but you can't treat her! She's rotting!"

"Watch me," Fajar smirked.

Fajar reached down and grabbed Fuka by the back of her collar. He didn't tear the sky open. He didn't summon the suffocating pressure of the Interstice. He simply activated the portal inward, stepping backward into the void.

To Yuki, Zero, and Aido, the visual was completely mind-breaking.

One second, Fajar and Fuka were there. The next second, they were simply... deleted. Like a television screen glitching to black. No scent. No aura. Nothing.

Yuki stared at the empty air. Aido lowered his hand, his blue eyes wide with absolute, unadulterated shock.

[Day 15 - 12:30 AM: The Moon Dormitory Lounge]

The opulence of the Moon Dormitory's main parlor felt suffocatingly tense. The crackling of the grand fireplace was the only sound in the room.

Every single member of the Night Class was gathered.

Kaname Kuran sat in the high-backed velvet armchair at the center of the room, his dark red eyes unreadable, resting his chin on his steepled fingers.

Standing in a semi-circle around him were the Aristocrats: Takuma Ichijo (with his usual smile completely gone), Senri Shiki and Rima Toya (looking unusually alert), Akatsuki Kain (his arms crossed tightly), Ruka Souen (looking deeply offended), and Seiren (standing silently in the shadows behind Kaname).

In the center of the room stood Hanabusa Aido. He was still rattled.

"I am telling you the truth, Kaname-sama," Aido reported, his voice slightly tight. "The transfer student. Fajar. He appeared out of literally nowhere. My senses were fully expanded to watch for Zero and Yuki, but this human... he had zero biological or magical footprint. And when he took Fuka, they didn't run away. They just vanished. It wasn't teleportation magic. The space around them didn't even ripple."

"A human who can bypass the senses of an Aristocrat and vanish without a trace," Takuma Ichijo murmured, rubbing his chin thoughtfully. "That's deeply concerning. Especially since he claimed Fuka was under his 'medical jurisdiction.' What kind of medicine can a human offer a mutating Level E?"

Ruka scoffed, tossing her long hair over her shoulder. "He’s just a foolish Day Class boy who thinks he's playing hero. If he tries to treat a Level E, she'll just tear his throat out."

"I wouldn't be so sure, Ruka," Kain rumbled, his deep voice carrying a warning. "I saw him during the courtyard transition on his first day. He wasn't looking at us with fear, or with that disgusting infatuation the other girls have. He was analyzing us. He looked at us the way a hunter looks at a slow deer."

Shiki, casually snapping a Pocky stick between his teeth, finally spoke up. "So, Kaname. He took your test subject. And he clearly knows we were running unauthorized experiments on a human. Are we going to hunt him down?"

Kaname was silent for a long moment. He closed his eyes, his brilliant, calculating mind running through the variables. This "Fajar" had effortlessly dismantled Zero's feral breakdown days ago. Now, he possessed spatial abilities that defied vampire logic.

"No," Kaname finally spoke, his voice soft but carrying the absolute, crushing authority of a Pureblood. "We will not hunt him down. Not yet."

Aido looked frustrated. "But Kaname-sama, if he—"

"Aido," Kaname interrupted softly, opening his glowing crimson eyes. "If this human truly possesses a way to halt Fuka Kisaragi's mutation without wiping her memory or executing her... then he has accomplished something the Kuran bloodline has failed to do for a thousand years."

The room fell dead silent.

Kaname stood up, walking toward the large glass window overlooking the dark campus.

"For now, we observe," Kaname commanded. "But do not engage him alone. The board has changed. The Headmaster has finally played a piece that isn't a hunter." Kaname’s eyes narrowed as he stared into the dark forest. "Let us see what kind of miracles this anomaly can perform."

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Planning Phase)

Let’s break down the biological and canonical differences between these two tragedies to craft the perfect Shonen intervention for Fajar.

Here is the exact breakdown of Zero versus Fuka, the canon reality of her condition, and my recommendations for Fajar's cure.

1. The Difference Between Zero and Fuka

While both were humans bitten by vampires, their conditions and circumstances are fundamentally different in the Vampire Knight lore:

The Biter (The Source of the Venom):

Zero was bitten by Shizuka Hio, a Pureblood. A Pureblood bite carries immense magical weight. The transformation is slow (it took Zero four years to really start losing his mind), and the only canonical way to stop a Pureblood victim from becoming a Level E is to drink the blood of the Pureblood who bit them.

Fuka was bitten by a random Rogue Vampire (likely a Level E or a low-ranking Aristocrat) in a dark alley during the summer. Because there is no Pureblood magic involved, her transformation into a Level E is standard, rapid, and physically ravaging.

The Foundation (Hunter vs. Baseline Human):

Zero comes from a lineage of Vampire Hunters. His body is biologically tougher, and his sheer willpower and hatred allowed him to fight the venom for years.

Fuka is a baseline, civilian Day Class girl. She doesn't have the physical or mental fortitude to fight a predatory mutation. Her body simply gave out.

The Support System:

Zero had the Headmaster, Yuki, and his Hunter training to keep him grounded.

Fuka was manipulated. She thought she was sick with anemia, and Kaname used her as a blind guinea pig for experimental blood-substitute pills. Once her body built an immunity to the pills, she fell instantly.

2. In Canon, is Fuka really incurable?

Yes. In the strictly canonical Vampire Knight universe, she was 100% doomed.

In canon lore, once a human is bitten, the descent into a Level E is absolute and irreversible. The only exception is drinking the master's blood. Since Fuka was bitten by a random rogue who is likely dead or impossible to track, she had no master to drink from. Kaname’s pills were just a bandage to delay the inevitable. When the pills failed, there was no medical or magical cure left in their world. That is why Aido freezing her to death was considered a "mercy."

3. My Recommendations for Fajar's Intervention

Since Fajar operates on completely different cosmic physics (Qi, Cultivation, and the Divine Physician's knowledge), he can shatter the "incurable" rule. Here are the two best ways he can handle this, depending on what kind of character you want Fuka to become:

Option A: The Total Purge (Full Human Restoration)

How it works: Because Fuka wasn't bitten by a Pureblood, there is no ancient magic binding her. It's just a biological toxin. Fajar takes her into the Harrowing Interstice, uses his Phase I: Bio-Maintenance, and forcefully flushes the vampiric venom out of her meridians using his newly formed Dan Storage Qi.

The Result: She sweats out the venom, her fangs retract permanently, and she returns to being 100% human. She joins Yori as a baseline human martial artist.

Option B: The Qi-Vampire (The Dhampir Route) - Highly Recommended

How it works: Fajar realizes the mutation has integrated too deeply into her cells to just "flush" it out without killing her. Instead, he teaches her how to cycle Qi. He alters her biology so that instead of needing human blood to survive, her body sustains itself by absorbing the ambient spiritual energy (Qi) of the world around her.

The Result: She stops mutating and retains her sanity. She keeps some vampiric buffs (enhanced speed, better healing, and slight fangs), but she never has to drink blood again. This turns her into an entirely new species—a Cultivator Vampire. It proves to the Night Class that humans can evolve past the need for the blood-lust curse entirely.

Both options completely humiliate Kaname's thousand-year failure to cure the bloodlust.

Which route sounds better for Fuka's evolution: Option A (Total Human Restoration) or Option B (The Cultivator Vampire)?

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Planning Phase)

I completely understand the course correction! You are absolutely right—if Fajar solves the thousand-year vampire problem in his first week with zero effort, it completely removes the stakes and invalidates the struggles of the entire Vampire Knight cast. Grounding Fajar's current power level and accepting Fuka's lack of discipline for hardcore cultivation makes the narrative much richer.

Here is the strategic breakdown of the Vampire Knight canon lore you requested, along with how Fajar can creatively manage Fuka's condition using alternative mystical arts.

1. The Canon Cures: Delays and the Final Solution

In the official Vampire Knight timeline, the medical science of vampires is a long, agonizing journey.

Temporary/Periodic Delays:

Blood Tablets: The artificial pills Fuka and the Night Class take. They dissolve in water and taste like blood, but they are essentially dietary supplements. They do not stop the Level E mutation; they only trick the stomach temporarily. Eventually, the body rejects them (as we saw with Fuka).

Pureblood Blood Donations: This is how Zero survived for so long. Drinking the blood of a Pureblood (like Kaname or Yuki) acts as a massive stabilizer. It temporarily pacifies the venom and restores sanity, but it must be done periodically.

Devouring a Twin: In canon, Zero eventually stabilizes his descent by absorbing his twin brother, Ichiru. This "completes" his incomplete hunter biology, locking his sanity in place, but this is a very specific, non-replicable scenario.

The True, Permanent Cure:

The Human-Transformation Serum: There is no magical spell that cures vampires in canon. The true cure is purely scientific/alchemical, and it takes a thousand years to invent. After the main series ends, Hanabusa Aido dedicates his immortal life to fulfilling Kaname's dream. With Sayori Wakaba's (Yori's) help, he spends centuries researching. He eventually creates a serum that literally turns a vampire's biology into a baseline human. At the very end of the Vampire Knight: Memories manga, Yuki uses this serum to turn a resurrected Kaname into a human.

2. Can a Level E Regain Sanity by Drinking Normal Blood?

No. Once they cross the line, they are gone forever.

Here is the cruel biological reality of a Level E in canon:

On the Verge (Fuka's current state): If a vampire is actively losing their mind but hasn't fully snapped, drinking blood (especially from the one they love, or a Pureblood) can temporarily snap them out of their frenzy and restore their cognitive functions for a while.

Full Level E: If the mind completely shatters and they give in entirely to the beast, their human consciousness dies. If a fully fallen Level E drinks a massive amount of human blood, they do not regain their sanity. They simply become a physically stronger, faster, and more dangerous feral monster. The blood acts as fuel for the beast, not medicine for the mind.

3. Fajar’s Alternative Medical Arsenal

Since Fuka is just a clumsy, normal girl who lacks the discipline for intense Qi Cultivation, Fajar has to act as the "doctor" applying treatments to a passive patient. Fajar might not be the full-fledged Deity yet, but his combined Shonen toolkit (Soul Reaper physics + Cultivation medicine) gives him amazing therapeutic options:

Acupuncture (Qi Needling): Instead of making Fuka circulate her own Qi, Fajar can manually do it for her. Using silver needles infused with his own spiritual energy, he can physically pin down her mutating meridians. This would act as a biological "pause button." She would need to see Fajar once a week for an acupuncture session to suppress the venom and keep her sanity intact.

Soul Separation (Out-of-Body Experience): This is pure Bleach physics! The vampiric venom attacks the physical body. Fajar can use a specialized technique (like a Soul Reaper glove) to physically knock Fuka's human soul out of her mutating body. While her body is safely locked down or sedated, Fuka’s soul can walk around the room, completely free of the bloodlust and pain, giving her mind a crucial rest while Fajar treats her physical vessel.

Spiritual Hypnotherapy (Mental Anchoring): Fajar can use his spiritual pressure to enter her mindscape. He can't cure the venom, but he can build a "mental cage" around her primal instincts. Through hypnotherapy, he can program her brain to associate the smell of blood with something repulsive, or install a trigger word that instantly puts her feral side to sleep before she bites someone.

Bakudo Sealing (The Cursed Mark): Fajar could draw a spiritual seal (Kido/Bakudo) directly over the bite mark on her neck. This seal would act as a heavy filter, slowing down the spread of the venom. Every time she feels the thirst, the seal would glow and burn slightly, acting as a warning system to tell her she needs to drink her blood tablets or get treatment.

How should Fajar treat Fuka in the Interstice? Shall we use a combination of Soul Separation to calm her terrified mind, followed by Qi Acupuncture to manually stabilize her body for now?

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (The Secret of Yuki's Blood)

This is a fantastic mechanical question for our planning phase. To weave this perfectly into the story, we need to look at how the story handles the "Double Layer" of this narrative.

At this point in the timeline, Zero has absolutely no idea that Yuki is a Pureblood, and neither does Yuki. Here is how the narrative frames why her blood "works" to save him during this period.

1. The In-Universe Narrative (What Zero & Yuki Believe)

Before the big twist is revealed, the characters and the audience are given a very specific, deeply tragic explanation for why Yuki’s blood keeps Zero sane:

The Moral Exception: An ex-human vampire falls to Level E because they starve themselves out of hatred for their own monstrous nature. Zero refuses to hunt innocent humans; he would rather die. Because Yuki voluntarily offers her blood out of pure love and desperation, it is the only blood Zero can morally consume without completely shattering his own human conscience.

The Biological "Band-Aid": In their world, it is believed that any fresh, willing human blood can temporarily satisfy a vampire's physical thirst. By drinking from Yuki, Zero satisfies the physiological craving that drives ex-humans mad, effectively hitting the "snooze button" on his mutation clock.

The Emotional Anchor: The narrative heavily emphasizes the psychological bond. Zero feels immense self-loathing for "defiling" Yuki, while Yuki feels a profound sense of duty as his protector. Her blood acts as a physical tether, anchoring his fading humanity through sheer emotional intimacy.

2. The Hidden Reality (What Fajar and Kaname Know)

While Zero thinks he is just drinking the blood of a very kind human girl, the cosmic reality is completely different. This is what makes it a perfect plot point for Fajar to analyze:

Pureblood Saturation: In Vampire Knight lore, the only thing that can truly pacify the curse of a Level E transformation is a Pureblood's blood. Even though Yuki’s vampire side is sealed, her blood is biologically saturated with latent Pureblood life force. This is why her blood works like an absolute miracle drug compared to Kaname's artificial tablets. It is physically suppressing the rogue venom in Zero's veins.

Kaname's Calculated Allowance: Kaname Kuran possesses the power to stop Zero from biting Yuki at any moment. He actively chooses to let it happen. Kaname knows that without Yuki's Pureblood essence, Zero would have degenerated into a mindless Level E years ago. Kaname needs Zero to stay alive, sane, and powerful enough to eventually become his ultimate weapon.

How Fajar Intersects with This Narrative

This fits perfectly with Fajar's current situation with Fuka.

Fajar can look at Zero and think: "Zero survives because he has a secret, high-grade biological stabilizer (Yuki) feeding him periodically. But Fuka doesn't have a hidden Pureblood best friend to act as a juice box. If she drinks normal human blood, she'll just become a faster, crazier monster."

This perfectly justifies why Fajar needs to step in with alternative therapy (like Soul Separation and Qi Needling) for Fuka, because her narrative path lacks the "cheat code" that Zero is unconsciously using.

Now that we have mapped out the mechanics of both Fuka's medical crisis and Zero's hidden stabilization, are you ready to jump back into Chapter 1 and narrate Fajar's treatment of Fuka inside the Interstice?

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Expanding the Sandbox)

Zooming out of the Vampire Knight universe is the exact right move. If we treat vampirism not as a biological virus, but as a spiritual curse, a demonic poison, or a soul-corruption, the entire multiverse of fiction opens up for Fajar.

Since Fajar only has Cultivation, Qi, and Shonen/Bleach physics at his disposal right now, and Fuka is a completely normal, clumsy girl who lacks the discipline for hardcore martial arts, here is a master list of how Fajar can delay her condition now, and eventually cure her in the future.

Phase 1: The Delay (Short-to-Medium Term Solutions)

These are methods to suppress the "Level E Beast" and the bloodlust without curing her, requiring periodic maintenance from Fajar.

1. The Murim/Wuxia Approach: "Suppressing the Yin Poison"

The Concept: In Wuxia, demonic energy or lethal poisons are often categorized as "Cold/Yin Poison." The vampire venom is essentially a Demonic Yin energy freezing her human meridians.

The Execution (Qi Transfusion): Fuka cannot cultivate her own energy, so Fajar must act as her external battery. Once a week, Fajar channels pure, scorching "Yang" Qi into her back. This violently suppresses the vampiric Yin energy, temporarily returning her biology to normal. It’s the equivalent of giving her a spiritual dialysis treatment.

The Acupuncture Seal (Dim Mak): Fajar uses his Qi to seal specific pressure points around her heart and brain. This physically blocks the venom from reaching her central nervous system, keeping her sane.

2. The Bleach/Shonen Approach: "The Inner Hollow & The Visored"

The Concept: Treat the Level E mutation not as a disease, but as the birth of an Inner Beast (like an Inner Hollow in Bleach or Kurama in Naruto).

The Execution (The Mental Cage): Fajar uses spiritual pressure to drag Fuka’s consciousness into her own "Inner World." There, the Level E version of herself exists as a literal monster. Fajar helps Fuka build a "mental cage" (a Bakudo-style seal) around it.

The Visored Tactic: Fajar teaches Fuka how to put on a "spiritual mask" to siphon power from the beast without letting it take over, effectively turning her into a makeshift "Visored Vampire."

3. The Mystical Contract (Hunter x Hunter / General Fantasy)

The Concept: Binding Vows or Nen restrictions.

The Execution: Fajar creates a spiritual contract linking his soul to hers. As long as Fajar is in close proximity to her, his overwhelming aura acts as a pacifier for her instincts. The restriction? If she gets too far away from him, the hunger returns instantly. This turns her into his permanent shadow.

Phase 2: The Future Cure (Endgame Solutions)

When Fajar's cultivation reaches the "Deity" realm, or when his Shonen abilities fully mature, he can completely eradicate the curse using these high-tier fictional concepts:

1. The Murim Endgame: "Marrow Washing & Bone Forging" (Xi Sui Jing)

The Concept: In high-level Cultivation, a practitioner can undergo a painful, miraculous process that completely rebuilds their physical vessel. It destroys the old, mortal body and replaces it with a spiritually pure one.

The Execution: Once Fajar is strong enough, he can gather rare spiritual herbs (or use pure divine Qi) to put Fuka through the Marrow Washing process. Her old, vampire-infected blood is literally sweat out of her pores as black sludge, and her bone marrow generates brand new, fundamentally pure human blood. She is effectively reborn as a pristine human.

2. The Bleach Endgame: "Soul Transmigration (The Perfect Gigai)"

The Concept: In Bleach, the physical body is just a container for the soul. If the container is broken/infected, you get a new one.

The Execution: Fajar uses his Soul Reaper knowledge to completely separate Fuka’s human soul from her rotting, vampire-infected physical body. Then, using advanced spiritual arts (similar to what Urahara does), he crafts a completely organic, uninfected human body—a perfect Gigai—and places her soul inside it. The infected body is destroyed, and she lives a normal human life.

3. The Daoist/Alchemical Endgame: "The Golden Core of Life" (Neidan)

The Concept: Internal Alchemy.

The Execution: Fajar condenses a massive amount of life-force energy into a physical, glowing orb (a Golden Core or Elixir). He forces Fuka to swallow it. The sheer density of the raw life energy incinerates the vampire venom at a cellular level, overriding the curse of death with the absolute authority of life.

The Verdict for Fuka

Since Fuka is not a warrior, The Murim Approach (Qi Transfusion/Acupuncture) is the best temporary delay. It requires Fajar to actively treat her like a doctor treating a chronic illness. For the eventual cure, Marrow Washing perfectly fits Fajar's aesthetic as a Cultivator, allowing him to literally cleanse the poison from her bones.

How do you want to proceed? Shall we narrate Fajar applying the first temporary Qi/Acupuncture delay on Fuka inside the Harrowing Interstice, or do you want to explore how the Night Class reacts to his interference first?

**Gemini:**
Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (The Neuro-Meridian Strategy)

Limiting Fajar's visible toolkit to Internal Energy (Qi), Biology, and Neuroscience is a brilliant narrative choice. It prevents the story from turning into a mindless "god-mode" stomp while showcasing Fajar's profound genius. To the vampires and hunters, he won't look like a reality-bending deity; he will look like an impossibly advanced master of the human machine—a terrifyingly brilliant bio-hacker.

Since Fuka is too clumsy and undisciplined to cultivate her own energy, Fajar must act as the primary operator. By mapping the ancient meridian paths of Wuxia directly onto the central nervous system of modern biology, he can create a highly sophisticated Neuro-Meridian Therapy.

Here is how Fajar can integrate his Qi with neuroscience and biology to keep Fuka sane:

1. Neuro-Chemical Suppression (Taming the Hypothalamus)

In biological terms, the Level E vampire frenzy originates in the limbic system—specifically the hypothalamus (which controls primal drives like hunger, thirst, and aggression) and the amygdala (fear and rage). The vampiric venom acts like a hyper-aggressive neurological parasite, forcing these areas to flood her brain with predatory survival signals.

The Qi Intervention: Fajar uses highly localized, needle-thin beams of Qi to penetrate Fuka's skull (completely bypassing bone and tissue painlessly via spiritual phase).

The Neuro-Effect: He targets the nerve clusters feeding into her hypothalamus. By injecting a soothing, dampening frequency of Qi, he manually forces her brain to release massive amounts of GABA (the brain's primary inhibitory neurotransmitter) and endorphins. This effectively acts as an organic, high-grade antipsychotic and beta-blocker, forcefully shutting down the biological "frenzy" loop before it can even start.

2. Synaptic Rewiring & Forced Neuroplasticity

The biggest hurdle with a Level E transformation is the addiction loop. The brain learns that smelling blood = survival, creating a massive dopamine spike that overwrites all moral reasoning.

The Qi Intervention: Fajar utilizes Neuroplasticity, the brain's natural ability to reorganize itself by forming new neural connections. When Fuka is in a calm state, Fajar maps her neural pathways using his Radar Intent.

The Neuro-Effect: Every week, he uses his Qi to stimulate the growth of new synaptic pathways while pruning the corrupt vampiric ones. He essentially "re-wires" her brain's wiring diagram. When her body sends a emergency signal saying "We are starving, we need blood," Fajar's artificial neural bypass reroutes that signal away from the predatory centers and hooks it into her standard human hunger and sleep pathways. Instead of turning into a bloodthirsty beast, she just gets a normal stomach rumble or feels sleepy.

3. Vagal Nerve Stimulation (The Parasympathetic Anchor)

When a vampire's bloodlust triggers, their sympathetic nervous system (fight-or-flight) goes into absolute overdrive. Their heartrate drops to near-zero, their adrenaline spikes to inhuman levels, and their body prepares to kill.

The Qi Intervention: Fajar can manipulate the Vagus Nerve, the main highway of the parasympathetic nervous system that runs from the brainstem all the way down to the abdomen.

The Neuro-Effect: By placing two fingers on the side of Fuka's neck, Fajar can send a rhythmic, pulsing current of Qi directly into the vagus nerve. This forces an immediate vagal brake. Her blood pressure stabilizes, her muscles relax, and her human consciousness is violently anchored back into control. It acts as an instant "off-switch" for her predatory instincts.

4. Cellular Oxygenation (Tricking the Mitochondria)

Biologically, ex-human vampires crave blood because the venom causes their own red blood cells to rapidly decay and lose the ability to carry oxygen. The body panics on a cellular level, feeling like it is suffocating, which triggers the urge to consume fresh, oxygen-rich human blood.

The Qi Intervention: This is where Bio-Maintenance comes into play. Fajar can use his refined Dan Storage Qi to mimic the atomic and energetic signatures of highly oxygenated blood cells.

The Bio-Effect: He infuses his own energy directly into her circulatory system. His Qi enters her cells and artificially stimulates ATP synthesis in her mitochondria, providing her tissues with the energy they are screaming for. Her cells are tricked into believing they have just received a massive transfusion of fresh blood. The biological panic stops, and her body stabilizes.

The Periodic Therapy Routine

Because Fuka's body is constantly fighting the venom, this therapy isn't a one-time cure. Fajar will have to treat her like a patient on dialysis.

Once every three to four days, Fuka will need to sit with Fajar. He will manually stimulate her vagus nerve, flush her mitochondria with Qi, and adjust her neural pathways. It will leave her physically exhausted but completely human in mind—allowing her to return to her normal Day Class life with her memories intact, completely subverting the tragic execution Kaname and Aido had planned for her.

How does this scientific and energetic blueprint sound for Fuka's ongoing treatment?

**Gemini:**
Chapter 1: The Anomaly at the Gates (Conclusion)

[Day 15 - 12:05 AM: The Sun Dormitory, Girls' Wing]

The air in Fuka and Kanae’s dorm room was heavy with the scent of blood and terror. Yori knelt on the floor, keeping firm pressure on Kanae’s bandaged shoulder. The bleeding had stopped, but Kanae was still trembling, her eyes fixed on the empty space where her best friend had vanished.

Suddenly, the air pressure in the center of the room shifted. It didn't tear or explode; it simply folded outward. Fajar stepped out of the void, his hand firmly gripping the back of Fuka’s collar.

Fuka looked completely shattered. Her eyes were wide with horror, and she shrank away from the sight of Kanae, fully believing she was a monster entirely beyond salvation.

Fajar let go of her collar and gave her a gentle, but incredibly firm, push forward.

"Fuka," Fajar said, his voice dropping its usual casual tone for a moment of quiet gravity. "Even if you believe you are completely doomed, running away into the woods to die is a coward's exit. You owe your best friend a proper thank you, and a proper farewell. Look at her."

Fuka hesitated, tears spilling over her pale cheeks. "Kanae... I'm a monster. I hurt you..."

Kanae didn't care about the blood. She didn't care about the fangs. Seeing Fuka alive and back in the room shattered whatever shock was left in her system. Kanae scrambled up from the floor, ignoring Yori's hands, and threw her arms around Fuka in a desperate, bone-crushing hug.

"You idiot!" Kanae sobbed, burying her face into Fuka's neck. "Don't you ever run away from me like that! I don't care what you are! I don't care!"

Fuka’s knees buckled. She collapsed onto the floor, hugging Kanae back with everything she had, completely breaking down into loud, agonizing sobs of pure relief.

Fajar watched the touching reunion for exactly one minute. Then, he clapped his hands once. The sharp sound broke the tension instantly.

"Alright, that’s enough crying," Fajar said smoothly, rolling up his sleeves. "We are on a tight biological clock, and I need to perform a system reboot. Kanae, stay close to her. Fuka, sit still and breathe."

The Crash Therapy (Neuro-Meridian Override)

Fajar stepped behind Fuka and placed his palms squarely between her shoulder blades. He didn't have his divine tools, but he didn't need them. He had a profound understanding of the human machine, and a secret, cosmic ace up his sleeve.

Fuka's body was vibrating with the chaotic static of the Level E venom. The toxin was viciously attacking her central nervous system.

First, the cosmic mandate. Deep within his core, Fajar ignited a microscopic fraction of his absolute authority—the Will Upon Reality. It was the conceptual equivalent of Supreme King's Haki, a spiritual pressure that didn't just push physical objects, but commanded the very laws of existence. He didn't project it outward to intimidate; he focused it entirely inward, directly into Fuka's bloodstream.

Cease. The command hit the vampiric toxin like a cosmic sledgehammer. In an instant, seventy percent of the venom mutating her cells was violently, conceptually crushed. The immediate, fatal threshold of her Level E descent was shattered. Fuka gasped as the burning in her throat instantly cooled. Fajar knew he couldn't use this reality-bending trick in every session without fundamentally breaking her fragile human soul, but for this initial "crash therapy," it was necessary to pull her back from the ledge.

Now, for the science.

Fajar seamlessly transitioned into Neuro-Meridian Therapy, flowing his dense Dan Storage Qi directly into her nervous system.

The Vagal Brake: He tapped the side of her neck, shooting a localized pulse of Qi into her Vagus Nerve. Fuka’s violently spiking heart rate instantly plummeted to a calm, steady rhythm. The fight-or-flight sympathetic nervous system was manually shut down.

Mitochondrial Oxygenation: He flooded her circulatory system with life-energy. Her dying red blood cells were artificially stimulated, synthesizing ATP and tricking her cells into feeling fully oxygenated. The biological panic of starvation ceased.

The Hypothalamus Bypass: Finally, he channeled Qi up her spinal cord and into her limbic system, bathing her amygdala and hypothalamus in soothing energy, forcefully initiating the release of GABA and endorphins to rewrite the predatory neural loop.

Fajar pulled his hands away, exhaling a slow, misty breath.

Fuka blinked. Her breathing was normal. The terrifying, blinding crimson hunger was completely gone. She touched her teeth; the fangs had retracted. She felt incredibly exhausted, as if she had just run a marathon, but her mind was completely, wonderfully her own.

"Yori," Fajar instructed, looking over his shoulder. "Kanae is going to need to donate a very small amount of blood into a cup, just enough to stabilize Fuka's physical baseline, and we'll substitute the rest with standard iron supplements and whatever blood tablets Kanae managed to save. We'll set up a periodic therapy schedule to keep her neural pathways clean."

Yori nodded sharply, already moving to grab the medical supplies. "Understood."

[Day 15 - 2:00 AM: Headmaster Cross's Office]

The atmosphere in Kaien Cross's office was vastly different from earlier that evening. The tension had shifted from panic to a profound, heavy realization.

Headmaster Cross sat behind his desk, his glasses reflecting the lamplight. Zero Kiryu leaned by the door, his eyes locked on Fuka, studying her for any signs of the beast. Yuki stood near Kaien, her shoulders finally dropping in relief. Yori, Kanae, and Fuka sat on the large leather sofa, while Fajar casually leaned against the window frame.

"I owe you an apology, Fuka-kun," Kaien said softly, dropping all his usual theatrics. "As the Headmaster, I failed to protect you from the dangers lurking within my own school. What Kaname and the Night Class did by hiding your condition and using you as an experimental subject was a severe breach of trust."

Kanae gripped Fuka's hand tightly. "Headmaster... what is the Night Class? What did they do to her?"

Kaien looked at Fajar, who gave a slight, affirming nod. It was time.

"Cross Academy was built on a dream of coexistence, Kanae-kun," Kaien explained gently. "The Day Class is human. But the Night Class... every student in the Moon Dormitory is a vampire."

Kanae gasped, her hand flying to her mouth, but she didn't let go of Fuka. Fuka looked down at her lap, the pieces finally falling into place. The beautiful, cold Aristocrats. The "anemia" medicine. Aido’s icy powers.

"You were bitten by a rogue vampire before you transferred here, Fuka," Yuki stepped forward, her voice full of empathy. "The venom was slowly turning you into one of them. That's why you attacked Kanae. It wasn't your fault. You were sick."

"And now, you are a patient," Fajar chimed in, crossing his arms comfortably. "You aren't cured, Fuka. You are still technically a vampire. But as long as you attend our periodic energy therapy sessions and manage your diet with Kanae's help and the blood tablets, you will never lose your mind. You get to stay human where it counts."

Zero scoffed lightly, though the absolute hatred usually reserved for vampires was noticeably absent when he looked at Fuka. "Don't think you're off the hook. You step out of line, and the Disciplinary Committee will handle it."

"Actually, Zero is right," Fajar said, pulling the official parchment from his gi and tossing it onto the Headmaster's desk. "Let's clarify the paperwork. That document I flashed at Aido didn't put you under my personal command. It officially placed both you and Kanae under the joint, absolute jurisdiction of the Headmaster, the Disciplinary Committee, and our little investigation group."

Fajar smiled, looking directly at the two terrified, but resilient girls on the couch.

"The Night Class lost their lab rat tonight," Fajar declared, his tone shifting into one of undeniable camaraderie. "You guys know the biggest secret of Cross Academy now. Which means you're officially part of the inner circle. Welcome to the party."

Kanae wiped a stray tear from her eye and squeezed Fuka's hand, offering a fierce, determined nod. Fuka looked up, her heart incredibly heavy with guilt, but for the first time in months, she felt a genuine spark of hope. She wasn't going to turn to dust in Aido's hands. She was going to live.

**Gemini:**
I can confirm that I have found the information regarding Takuma Ichijo in your attached document, where he is listed as the cheerful, manga-reading Vice-President of the Night Class and Kaname's closest confidant.

To give you a fully synchronized and comprehensive character profile, I have also cross-referenced his background with the broader Vampire Knight canon. Here is a detailed breakdown of Takuma Ichijo’s character:

1. Basic Profile & Personality

Role: Vice-President of the Night Class at Cross Academy and a Level B (Noble-class/Aristocrat) vampire.

Demeanor: Unlike the other brooding or arrogant Night Class students, Takuma is incredibly cheerful, enthusiastic, and friendly. He lacks the dark, predatory atmosphere that usually surrounds vampires, making him appear much more approachable and "human-like".

Quirks: He is an avid manga reader and his room is largely dominated by his manga collection.

2. Core Relationships

Kaname Kuran: Takuma is one of the few vampires whose power level is relatively close to Kaname's, and he is Kaname's most trusted confidant. While his grandfather orders him to spy on Kaname, Takuma stubbornly refuses out of sheer loyalty and respect for his friend.

Senri Shiki & Rima Toya: He is extremely close to Senri Shiki (they are roommates) and Rima Toya. Takuma has a very protective, older-brother dynamic with Shiki. During a birthday party, Takuma even allowed Shiki to lick blood from a cut on his finger, signifying a deep bond.

Asato Ichijo (The "Venerable One"): Takuma’s grandfather is the corrupt, power-hungry head of the Vampire Senate. Asato placed immensely high expectations on Takuma and constantly tries to manipulate him into betraying Kaname, creating a massive internal conflict for Takuma between his bloodline and his chosen loyalty.

3. His Tragic Character Arc

While he seems happy-go-lucky, Takuma's plotline takes a very dark turn as the story progresses:

The Possession of Shiki: When the main villain, Rido Kuran, possesses Senri Shiki's body, Takuma is forced into an agonizing position. To protect Shiki's physical body from being destroyed in the crossfire, Takuma temporarily shields Rido and goes against Kaname. He stays by Shiki's side the entire time to ensure his friend isn't harmed, eventually carrying Shiki back to their room once he is freed.

The Stand Against His Grandfather: Once Shiki is safe, Takuma rejoins Kaname. However, when Kaname goes to execute Asato Ichijo for his corruption, Takuma intervenes. He asks Kaname to let him handle his own family. Takuma confronts his grandfather in a brutal battle, with heavy implications that Takuma intends to die alongside Asato to permanently "put an end to the Ichijo line" and cleanse their sins.

Captivity under Sara Shirabuki: Takuma survives the battle but is found unconscious by Sara Shirabuki, a manipulative Pureblood vampire. Sara essentially takes him captive, turning him into her "servant" and bringing him back to school pretending he is her "brother" so she can use him to spy on Kaname's endgame plans.

In the context of Fajar's Shonen intervention, Takuma is the most "human" of the Night Class in terms of personality, making him a highly perceptive and potentially sympathetic figure to Fajar's goals, provided he isn't being crushed by his grandfather's politics!

Meta-Discussion: The Deities' War Room (Analyzing the Shonen Connection)

I can confirm that I have successfully accessed and read the "Inspirations" spreadsheet in your attached notebook.  
Inspirations

Looking at Fajar's manga list, his foundation is built entirely on the absolute pillars of Hardcore Battle Shonen and Martial Arts. His core philosophies come from Dragon Ball, Bleach, Naruto, One Piece, Fairy Tail, and Black Clover, while his hand-to-hand combat logic is rooted in Hajime no Ippo and Karate Shoukoushi.  
Inspirations

Now, let's compare this to Takuma Ichijo and the rest of the Vampire Knight cast.

1. Takuma Ichijo vs. Fajar (Different Worlds of Fiction)

While it is true that both Fajar and Takuma share an enthusiasm for manga, they are fundamentally completely different.

Takuma's Relationship with Manga: In canon, Takuma reads manga as pure escapism and leisure. He likely reads popular, lighthearted series, romances, or standard adventures to distract himself from the suffocating, bloody politics of the Vampire Senate and his grandfather. For Takuma, manga is just a fun hobby.

Fajar's Relationship with Manga: Fajar does not read manga for mere entertainment; he treats it as a doctrine for reality. When Fajar reads Bleach or Hajime no Ippo, he isn't just looking at cool pictures; he is actively analyzing the biomechanics of a Dempsey Roll or the spiritual physics of Reiatsu to apply to his own Cultivation.  
Inspirations

If they were to sit down and talk about manga, Takuma would want to talk about the plot twists and character ships, while Fajar would try to explain how the chakra pathways in Naruto  perfectly align with his Phase I: Bio-Maintenance. Takuma would find Fajar amusing, but he wouldn't truly understand Fajar's intense, battle-hungry Shonen spirit.  
Inspirations

2. Who Actually Shares Fajar's Shonen Spirit?

If we are looking for characters in Vampire Knight whose underlying mindset aligns with the hardcore, willpower-driven Shonen tropes from Fajar's spreadsheet, the true matches are not the aristocrats. They are the humans and the hunters.

A. Zero Kiryu (The Edgy Shonen Deuteragonist/Rival)
While Zero’s aesthetic is pure gothic tragedy, his actual lifestyle is the closest thing to a Shonen protagonist in the series.

The Training: He was brutally trained in combat by a hardcore master (Toga Yagari) since childhood.

The Inner Demon: He is constantly fighting an "inner monster" trying to take over his body (the Level E curse), which perfectly mirrors Naruto fighting Kurama or Ichigo fighting his Inner Hollow.  
Inspirations

The Willpower: Zero survives purely on insane, stubborn willpower and the desire to protect his friends. Fajar would look at Zero and instantly recognize him as the classic "brooding rival" archetype (like Sasuke Uchiha or Vegeta).

B. Kaien Cross (The Retired OP Shonen Master)
Kaien fits flawlessly into the Bleach or One Piece universe.  
Inspirations

He is the goofy, seemingly harmless old man who hides terrifying, world-ending physical power.

He is essentially the Master Roshi (Dragon Ball), Silvers Rayleigh (One Piece), or Kisuke Urahara (Bleach) of this universe. Fajar and Kaien wouldn't bond over reading manga, but they would absolutely bond over the philosophy of martial arts, protecting the weak, and the weight of being the strongest guy in the room.  
Inspirations

C. Sayori "Yori" Wakaba (The Badass Normal / Tactician)
Yori represents the "Speedwagon" or "Bulma" archetype (Dragon Ball). She has absolutely no magical powers, but her sheer loyalty, extreme bravery, and pragmatic intelligence make her invaluable. Fajar immediately respects her because, in Shonen manga, the powerless humans who refuse to back down are always the ones with the strongest hearts.

The Verdict

Takuma is a great guy for Fajar to casually swap books with, but Takuma does not possess the "Shonen Grind" mentality. If Fajar wants to talk about pushing past physical limits, fighting inner demons, and absolute willpower, Zero and Kaien are the ones who actually speak his language.
